# Decision Log

This document is the single source of truth for **why** non-trivial implementation
decisions were made in the Blitzy Slack proof-of-concept. Per the project's
Explainability rule, rationale MUST live here — **not** in code comments. A decision
is "non-trivial" if a competent engineer could reasonably have chosen differently.
Any deviation from a literal or obvious interpretation of the requirements MUST have
an explicit entry here; unexplained deviations are treated as defects.

Downstream code-generation agents MUST append a row to the relevant table below for
every additional non-trivial decision they make.

## How to use this log

- **Scope — every non-trivial decision.** A decision is "non-trivial" if a competent engineer could reasonably have chosen differently. Each one gets a row in the relevant section below.
- **Append-only.** Rows are never edited or removed. If a decision is later reversed or refined, add a NEW row in the same section that names the decision it supersedes, rather than rewriting history.
- **Code comments carry HOW, this log carries WHY.** Comments may describe mechanics, edge cases, and non-obvious control flow; rationale and trade-offs belong here. This keeps the "why" out of line-level `git blame` churn and in one auditable place (AAP §0.8.3).
- **Deviations are defects unless logged.** Any departure from a literal or obvious reading of the Agent Action Plan (AAP) MUST have an explicit row explaining it.
- **Organisation.** Decisions are grouped by the package or concern they belong to — one `##` section per area — and each section holds a four-column table: _What was decided_ · _What alternatives existed_ · _Why this choice was made_ · _What risks it carries_. Add a new `##` section for a new area, or append to an existing section when one already fits.
- **Adding a row.** Append to the bottom of the matching section's table, fill all four columns, wrap code identifiers in backticks, and escape any literal pipe inside a cell as `\|`.

## Decision-log format

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                    | What alternatives existed                                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                             |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| This log is organised as one four-column table per package/concern — the format already established by every section below — rather than a single flat table keyed by a sequential `#` with `Date`/`Author` columns | A single global table with `#`/`Date`/`Author` columns (the shape sketched in this file's planning seed)                     | The per-section format was the convention already in use by every committed entry when this section was authored. Preserving it keeps the existing decisions intact (append-only, AAP §0.8.3) and co-locates related decisions by package as the codebase grows. Rewriting into a flat numbered table would have deleted committed rationale and reformatted history, which the Explainability rule forbids             | Rows cannot be referenced by a global index ("decision N"); they are instead referenced by their section heading plus _What was decided_ text. Acceptable for an append-only, package-grouped log |
| Three planning-seed decisions were deliberately NOT adopted because the implemented code chose differently; the authoritative rows are the ones already in this log                                                 | Record the seed values verbatim: `engines.node >=22.11.0`, explicit package enumeration, and `@blitzy-slack/*` package scope | A decision log must match shipped code. (1) The workspace uses the `packages/*` wildcard — see the _Root workspace & tooling_ wildcard row — not explicit enumeration. (2) Packages are scoped `@app/*` — see the `@app/db` and `@app/web` rows — not `@blitzy-slack/*`. (3) `engines.node` is `>=22.12.0` — see the row below — not `>=22.11.0`. Recording the seed values would have made the log contradict the code | A reader expecting the planning-seed values will not find them as adopted decisions; this row is the explicit pointer that reconciles seed intent with the implemented choices                    |

## Root workspace & tooling

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| pnpm workspace declared with the `packages/*` wildcard in `pnpm-workspace.yaml`                                                                                                                                                   | Enumerate each package path explicitly (`packages/db`, `packages/shared`, `packages/api`, `packages/web`)                                                                                                                                                             | The wildcard is the AAP/checkpoint-specified workspace contract and automatically includes any future package added under `packages/` without editing the manifest. Explicit enumeration silently omits new packages and drifts from the spec.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | A stray non-package directory under `packages/` would be matched by the glob; acceptable because that tree holds only the four intended workspaces.                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| `onlyBuiltDependencies` allow-list declared in `pnpm-workspace.yaml` (`@prisma/client`, `prisma`, `bcrypt`, `esbuild`, `@playwright/test`)                                                                                        | Rely on interactive `pnpm approve-builds`; disable build-script gating entirely                                                                                                                                                                                       | pnpm 10+ refuses to run a dependency's install/build scripts unless it is allow-listed (pnpm 9 accepts the field without complaint), so without the list `prisma generate` and `bcrypt`'s native binding never build and `make local` (Gate 1) fails on a clean checkout                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A new native or install-script dependency that is omitted from the list fails silently — its binding is simply not built; the list must be updated whenever such a dependency is introduced                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Root `package.json` sets `"type": "module"` so the workspace root is ESM by default                                                                                                                                               | CommonJS by default (omit the field) and use `.cjs` for tooling configs                                                                                                                                                                                               | `eslint.config.js`, `vite.config.ts`, and `playwright.config.ts` use `import`/`export`, and `tsconfig.base.json` sets `module: NodeNext`; ESM at the root keeps the toolchain consistent and avoids per-file `.mjs`/`.cjs` juggling                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | A tool that assumes a bare `.js` config is CommonJS could break; mitigated by renaming any such file to `.cjs`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| Root `engines.node` pinned to `>=22.12.0`, with `.nvmrc` selecting the same line                                                                                                                                                  | The AAP's stated floor `>=22.0.0`; Prisma's hard floor `>=22.11.0`                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Prisma 6 requires Node `>=22.11.0`, so the AAP's `>=22.0.0` would let an unsupported Node install and then fail at `prisma generate`/runtime; `22.12.0` is the current Node 22 LTS patch and the value `.nvmrc` selects, so `engines` and `.nvmrc` stay in agreement                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Developers on Node 22.0–22.11 cannot `pnpm install`; mitigated by `.nvmrc` driving `nvm use` / `fnm use` to the pinned version                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| ESLint 9 **flat config** authored in `eslint.config.js`, with `packages/web/src/components/ui/**` placed in `ignores`                                                                                                             | Legacy `.eslintrc.cjs`; an `eslint.config.mjs` variant                                                                                                                                                                                                                | ESLint 9 and `typescript-eslint` v8 are flat-config-first, and the ESM root lets a `.js` flat config load natively (Rule 3 runs `eslint . --max-warnings 0`); the shadcn-generated `ui/**` primitives are copied verbatim and owned upstream, so they are ignored rather than linted against project rules                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Editor/CI integrations that only understand `.eslintrc` will not read this config; mitigated by pinning ESLint 9 across environments. Ignoring `ui/**` means a defect inside a generated primitive is not caught by lint                                                                                                                                          |
| Prettier configured with `printWidth: 100` (plus `singleQuote: true`, `trailingComma: "all"`, `endOfLine: "lf"`)                                                                                                                  | Prettier's default `printWidth: 80`; a wider `120`                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | 100 columns suit modern wide displays while staying readable in side-by-side diffs on laptops, and the value is common across the TypeScript ecosystem; `make format` / `prettier --check` enforces it uniformly, including the table alignment in this Markdown file                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Contributors used to 80 columns may find some lines wide on small screens; immaterial because the formatter rewrites everything to the policy                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| `tsconfig.base.json` enables `noUncheckedIndexedAccess: true`, beyond the strict flags the AAP lists                                                                                                                              | Only the AAP-listed flags (`strict`, `noUnusedLocals`, `noUnusedParameters`, `noFallthroughCasesInSwitch`, `forceConsistentCasingInFileNames`)                                                                                                                        | Typing `arr[i]` as `T \| undefined` catches a common class of runtime "undefined is not …" bugs at compile time, reinforcing Rule 3's strictness                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Array/record access needs explicit guards or a `!` assertion (the latter justified in this log where used); accepted in exchange for the safety win                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| `tsconfig.base.json` leaves `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: false` (the TypeScript default)                                                                                                                                          | Enable `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` for stricter optional-property semantics                                                                                                                                                                                    | Zod infers optional fields as `T \| undefined`, which clashes with the stricter `T?` discriminant `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` demands; enabling it would force hand-written type adapters across every Zod-inferred DTO                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | `{ foo: undefined }` and `{}` are treated alike by the checker; mitigated because Zod validates the same shapes at runtime                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| The `make local` API-readiness gate is an **inline POSIX-shell loop** in the `Makefile` (`for i in $(seq 1 60); do curl -sf "$API_HEALTH_URL" …; sleep 2; done`) rather than a separate `scripts/wait-for-health.sh`              | A dedicated wait-for-health script file; a `tsx` Node waiter; relying on `docker compose --wait` (which covers only the DB/Redis containers, not the host API)                                                                                                        | Keeps the committed file inventory minimal and the polling portable across bash/dash/zsh; the loop blocks `make seed` and the web start-up until `GET /api/health` returns 200, satisfying Rule 4 ("seed only after the API is healthy") and Gate 1                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Windows `make` users need WSL or Git-Bash with `curl` on `PATH`; documented as a prerequisite in the README                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| `eslint.config.js` block 9 (the `disableTypeChecked` group for files outside any package tsconfig) extended so its `files` glob also matches `**/prisma/seed.ts`, linting the Prisma `db seed` delegate with syntactic rules only | (a) Add `prisma/seed.ts` to `packages/db/tsconfig.json` `include` so the type-aware project service can resolve it; (b) leave the config untouched and accept that `eslint .` cannot lint the file; (c) add the file to a `projectService` `allowDefaultProject` list | `packages/db/prisma/seed.ts` is deliberately excluded from every tsconfig (it runs from source via `tsx`, never compiled), so `typescript-eslint`'s `projectService: true` rejects it at parse time ("not found by the project service") and `eslint . --max-warnings 0` (Rule 3) fails. (a) would force the file into `tsc`/`dist` output, which the design forbids; (b) leaves a file silently un-lintable, defeating Rule 3; (c) is functionally equivalent, but `disableTypeChecked` already covers exactly this category (root `*.config.ts`, `scripts/**`), so extending that one glob is the established minimal pattern. Verified: full-workspace `eslint .` stays green and the glob matches only `packages/db/prisma/seed.ts` | Type-aware rules (`no-floating-promises`, `consistent-type-imports`) do not run on the delegate; acceptable because it is a tiny dependency-free `child_process.spawn` shim whose correctness is covered by syntactic lint plus a runtime smoke test. Any future type-checked `*.ts` named `seed.ts` under a `prisma/` dir would likewise skip type-aware linting |

## Infrastructure (`docker-compose.yml`)

| What was decided                                                            | What alternatives existed                                      | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                  | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                      |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| No top-level `version:` field in `docker-compose.yml`                       | Declare `version: '3.x'` as in legacy Compose files            | The Compose Specification (Compose v2) ignores `version:` and emits an "obsolete" warning when it is present; omitting it is the current-format default.                                                  | Standalone `docker-compose` v1 binaries would not parse the file, but the project targets Compose v2 (`docker compose`).                                                   |
| `postgres:16-alpine` and `redis:7-alpine` images                            | `postgres:16` / `redis:7` (Debian-based), or pinned patch tags | Alpine variants are the smallest official images, speeding first-run pulls for the local PoC; the `16`/`7` majors match the AAP-required engine versions.                                                 | Floating on the minor tag means `docker compose pull` can advance the patch level. No native extensions compile against these images, so musl vs glibc is immaterial here. |
| PostgreSQL initialised as UTF-8 with `C` collation (`POSTGRES_INITDB_ARGS`) | Default locale collation (e.g. `en_US.UTF-8`)                  | `C` collation gives stable byte-level ordering identical across host locales, keeping cursor pagination deterministic between developer machines. Search ranking is handled by `tsvector`, not collation. | `C` collation sorts bytes, not linguistic order; acceptable because ordering keys are timestamps/ids. Applied only on first volume initialisation.                         |
| Redis started with AOF persistence (`--appendonly yes`)                     | RDB snapshotting (default) or no persistence                   | AOF persists presence keys and Socket.io adapter state across container restarts with a tighter durability window than periodic RDB snapshots.                                                            | AOF files grow larger than RDB and add minor write overhead; negligible at PoC scale.                                                                                      |
| API and web run on the host; only Postgres and Redis run in Compose         | Containerise the API and web servers too                       | Running the Node servers on the host keeps Vite/tsx hot-reload fast and avoids bind-mount/file-watch friction inside containers for the local PoC.                                                        | The host must have Node 22 + pnpm installed (documented in the README). Container/production parity is out of PoC scope.                                                   |
| Named volumes (`blitzy-slack-postgres-data`, `blitzy-slack-redis-data`)     | Anonymous volumes, or host bind mounts                         | Stable, predictable names survive `make down`/`make clean` (neither passes `-v`) and are independent of the Compose project directory.                                                                    | Data persists until explicitly removed with `docker compose down -v`; a developer expecting a clean slate must run that command.                                           |

## `packages/shared` — Shared contracts

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What alternatives existed                                                                                      | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                           |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Socket.io event names exported as `as const` string constants (`events.ts`) rather than a TypeScript `enum`                                                                                                                                                                      | A TypeScript `enum`, or a plain (non-`as const`) object                                                        | `as const` literals erase at compile time (zero runtime cost, no emitted object) and give exact literal types for the typed `ClientToServerEvents`/`ServerToClientEvents` contract; an `enum` emits a runtime object and is awkward to use as a union of literals.                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Consumers import the constants rather than a runtime enum namespace; this matches how both client and server reference the shared contract.                                     |
| The error event constant is exported as `ERROR = 'error'` (no `SOCKET_ERROR` alias)                                                                                                                                                                                              | Keep the prior `SOCKET_ERROR` name, or export both                                                             | The checkpoint/shared contract specifies `ERROR`; socket typings and imports are generated against that name. A second alias would create two ways to reference one wire event and risk drift.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Any code referencing `SOCKET_ERROR` must switch to `ERROR`; no such consumers exist at this checkpoint.                                                                         |
| `PresenceState` modelled as a string-literal union (`'online' \| 'away' \| 'offline'`)                                                                                                                                                                                           | A TypeScript `enum`                                                                                            | Same reasoning as the event constants: a union of string literals is zero-runtime, serialises directly over the wire/JSON, and narrows cleanly.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Values are bare strings, so a typo is caught only where the `PresenceState` type is applied; usage sites are typed, so this is contained.                                       |
| User DTOs modelled as four shapes — `User` (internal, includes `passwordHash`), `UserResponse = Omit<User,'passwordHash'>` (authenticated self), `PublicUser` (peer view, omits `email`/`passwordHash`), `AuthenticatedUser extends PublicUser` (adds `email`)                   | A single `User` type without `passwordHash`, or overloading `User` for both DB row and wire response           | The four-shape contract is the checkpoint/AAP §0.4.4 specification: `passwordHash` stays on the server-only `User` shape, the self-view exposes `email` but no hash, and the peer-view omits `email`. Overloading one type for DB and wire blurs the privacy boundary and risks leaking `passwordHash`.                                                                                                                                                                          | More named types to keep aligned with the Prisma model; mitigated because all derive from `User` via `Omit`/`extends`, so one source change propagates.                         |
| Zod request schemas use `.strict()` to reject unknown keys (e.g. `startDmSchema` in `schemas/dm.ts`)                                                                                                                                                                             | Default Zod object parsing (unknown keys silently stripped); `.passthrough()` (unknown keys kept)              | `.strict()` rejects over-posting / prototype-pollution attempts at the validation boundary instead of silently dropping unexpected fields, so a malformed or hostile body fails fast with a clear 400 (Gate 12)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | A client that sends extra cosmetic fields gets a 400; acceptable because every request shape is defined by the shared schema and the web forms submit exactly those fields      |
| Numeric limits centralised as `as const` constants in `constants/limits.ts` (`PAGE_SIZE = 50`, `MAX_PAGE_SIZE = 100`, `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB = 10`, `HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL_MS = 30_000`, `ONLINE_THRESHOLD_MS = 60_000`, `AWAY_THRESHOLD_MS = 300_000`, plus message/channel/emoji caps) | Hardcode each value at its use site across `api` and `web`; read every limit from the environment              | One shared module is the single source of truth so the API validator, the DB `VARCHAR(n)` caps, and the web's fail-fast UI all agree on the same numbers (AAP §0.8.4); the env loader layers a runtime override only for `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB`, where tuning is actually needed                                                                                                                                                                                                     | If a limit ever needs to differ between client and server a single constant cannot express that; none currently do, and the env loader covers the one runtime-tunable value     |
| `createMessageSchema` enforces the channel/DM XOR with `.superRefine`, not `.refine`                                                                                                                                                                                             | A single `.refine` returning one boolean with a generic message                                                | `.superRefine` attaches a field-specific issue to BOTH `channelId` and `dmId` (distinct messages for the "both set" vs "neither set" cases), so the API and the web form surface the error on the correct field; a single `.refine` can only emit one form-level message (CP2 review remediation, M26).                                                                                                                                                                          | Two issues are emitted when the XOR fails, so a consumer counting issues must expect both `channelId` and `dmId` paths; intended for clearer field-level feedback.              |
| `reactionSchema.emoji` validated by a Unicode-emoji regex (`isStandardEmoji`) in addition to the `.min(1).max(MAX_EMOJI_LENGTH)` length bound                                                                                                                                    | Length-only validation; a hardcoded allow-list of specific emoji; `Intl.Segmenter` single-grapheme enforcement | A length-only check accepted arbitrary text as a "reaction"; the regex requires every code point to be emoji-related (`\p{Emoji}`, VS16, ZWJ, keycap, tag chars) AND at least one pictograph / regional-indicator / keycap, so plain text, digits, and punctuation are rejected while skin-tone, ZWJ sequences, flags, and keycaps pass (CP2 review remediation, M27). `Intl.Segmenter` was rejected to avoid a `lib.esnext.intl` type dependency and Firefox <125 runtime risk. | Allows multiple emoji in one value, bounded only by `MAX_EMOJI_LENGTH` (64); a single-grapheme cap can be layered later if the product requires exactly one emoji per reaction. |
| `FileAttachment.uploadedById` typed `string \| null` (not `string`)                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Keep it non-nullable `string` and assume an uploader always exists                                             | The `File.uploadedById` relation is `ON DELETE SET NULL` (see the migrations section), so an API response can legitimately carry `null` after the uploader is deleted; the DTO must mirror the nullable column (CP2 review remediation, M28).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | UI and API consumers must handle a missing uploader (`null`) — e.g. render "Unknown" — rather than assuming a user id is always present.                                        |

## `packages/db` — Database package

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Singleton `PrismaClient` via a `globalThis` guard in `packages/db/src/client.ts`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | (a) A factory function returning fresh instances; (b) A module-level constant only, with no `globalThis` cache                                                                                                                                | Option (a) fragments the connection pool across test files and breaks Prisma's intended single-instance model; option (b) leaves a window where `tsx watch` and test-runner hot-reload can double-construct the client. The `globalThis` guard handles both production correctness and dev-mode hot-reload safety.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Couples the module to Node-specific `globalThis` semantics. Acceptable because the package is Node-only (server-side).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| Prisma logging fixed to `log: ['warn', 'error']`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | (a) `['query', 'info', 'warn', 'error']` for verbose dev; (b) `['error']` only                                                                                                                                                                | AAP §0.6.1 Group 2 mandates `['warn', 'error']` verbatim. Verbose `query` logging would flood the Pino output and obscure real signals (Gate 10 — Observability). Suppressing warnings would hide deprecations.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | If a hot debugging scenario needs query-level logs, a developer must temporarily edit `client.ts`. Documented here as the trade-off.                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| Graceful shutdown via an exported `async disconnectPrisma()` plus `process.once('SIGTERM'\|'SIGINT')` handlers that `await` the disconnect (inside a re-entrancy guard) and then re-raise the original signal with `process.kill(process.pid, signal)`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | (a) `process.on` with fire-and-forget `void prisma.$disconnect()`; (b) `beforeExit` only; (c) no shutdown hook; (d) export `disconnectPrisma()` with no in-package signal handlers, letting the API layer own all signal handling             | `process.on` + `void` (a) swallows disconnect failures and, by registering a listener, overrides Node's default signal termination so the process can hang or surface unhandled rejections; `beforeExit` (b) never fires on signal kill (`docker compose down`, `make down`); (c) orphans PostgreSQL connections, eventually causing "too many connections". `process.once` + `await` guarantees the disconnect runs exactly once and completes, and re-raising the now-removed signal restores default termination. The exported `disconnectPrisma()` additionally lets the API server's top-level shutdown path coordinate HTTP/socket closure with the Prisma disconnect (subsuming option (d)).                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | A failed disconnect is swallowed best-effort (the logger may already be torn down). Re-raising depends on `once` having removed the handler, so a repeated signal terminates immediately — intended.                                                                                                                                                  |
| JSDoc references in `client.ts` use the package name `@app/db` rather than the AAP's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/db`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/db` string from the agent prompt                                                                                                                                                                              | The actual workspace package name (set during setup in `packages/db/package.json`) is `@app/db`. Documentation must match the real import specifier so consumers are not misled. Functional code is unchanged.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | None functional; this is a documentation-accuracy alignment. If the package is ever renamed, the JSDoc must be updated alongside `package.json`.                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `packages/db/src/index.ts` barrel re-exports the 8 Prisma-generated model TYPES (`User`, `Channel`, `ChannelMember`, `DirectMessage`, `DMParticipant`, `Message`, `MessageReaction`, `File`) directly from `@prisma/client` via `export type { … }`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | (a) Redefine the entity DTOs in `@app/shared`; (b) force every consumer to import them from `@prisma/client` directly                                                                                                                         | (a) duplicates the model surface and must be hand-synced with every schema migration; (b) leaks `@prisma/client` into every API service file. Re-exporting from the db barrel keeps `schema.prisma` the single source of truth and centralises the import surface in one module. `export type` (not `export`) is required because `isolatedModules` (TS1205) and the `consistent-type-imports` ESLint rule both demand the `type` keyword for type-only re-exports                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Tight coupling to Prisma's generated type shape — a Prisma 6→7 type-shape change would need fixes in consumer code. Acceptable given Prisma's stable type contract                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| The `@app/db` barrel re-exports the `PrismaClient` class as a runtime VALUE (plain `export`), not merely as a type                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Re-export it type-only via `export type`                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Tests construct isolated client instances with custom datasource URLs (`new PrismaClient({ datasources: { db: { url } } })`) for parallel test isolation; a value re-export enables this through `@app/db` without leaking `@prisma/client` into test files                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Negligibly larger compiled-output footprint                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| The `@app/db` barrel re-exports the `Prisma` namespace alongside the `PrismaClient` class                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Force consumers to `import type { Prisma } from '@prisma/client'` themselves                                                                                                                                                                  | The `Prisma` namespace supplies generated input/where types (`Prisma.UserCreateInput`, `Prisma.MessageWhereInput`) and the `PrismaClientKnownRequestError` error family used heavily by `@app/api` services; centralising the re-export prevents `@prisma/client` from leaking into service code                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Marginally larger barrel surface                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `packages/db/src/index.ts` re-exports BOTH `prisma` AND `disconnectPrisma` from `./client.js`, although the `index.ts` file schema/agent-prompt enumerate only `prisma`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Re-export only `prisma`, leaving `disconnectPrisma` reachable solely through the `@app/db/client` subpath export                                                                                                                              | `client.ts` documents its public contract as "Consumers import `prisma` (and, for shutdown, `disconnectPrisma`) from `@app/db`", and the graceful-shutdown row above notes `disconnectPrisma()` lets the API server's shutdown path coordinate HTTP/socket closure with the Prisma disconnect. Since this barrel IS the `@app/db` entry point, re-exporting `disconnectPrisma` honours that documented surface and prevents `import { disconnectPrisma } from '@app/db'` from breaking once the API is authored. Re-exporting an extra value from a whitelisted dependency violates no rule, and the schema export list is a required minimum, not an exhaustive cap                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | One symbol beyond the schema's literal enumeration; immaterial since it is a documented part of the package's intended public API                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| `packages/db/prisma/seed.ts` (the `prisma db seed` entry resolved from the `prisma.seed` field) delegates to the single-source-of-truth `scripts/seed-via-api.ts` via `child_process.spawn('tsx', [scriptPath])` with `stdio: 'inherit'`, `env: process.env`, `shell: false`, propagating the child exit code through `process.exit`; `scriptPath` is computed cwd-independently from `import.meta.url` as `resolve(dirname(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url)), '..', '..', '..', 'scripts', 'seed-via-api.ts')` | (a) `await import(scriptPath)` to run the root script in-process; (b) set `prisma.seed` directly to `tsx ../../scripts/seed-via-api.ts` with no delegate file; (c) `exec`/`execSync`/`fork`; (d) a hardcoded relative path or `process.cwd()` | Rule 4 (AAP §0.8.1) forbids a direct DB insert, so the delegate must defer to the registration-flow script; `spawn` reproduces the separate-process semantics of `make seed` (same env, exit codes, streamed stdio) and is robust to whether the root script is top-level-executable or function-exporting. (a) shares the process, so the root script's top-level `process.exit` would pre-empt the delegate and its CLI detection (`argv[1] === import.meta.url`) would misfire; (b) is fragile because Prisma changes cwd before seeding and `..` traversal in `prisma.seed` has historically broken; (c) `exec`/`execSync` buffer rather than stream and `fork` needs a Node IPC entry point `tsx` is not; (d) `process.cwd()` is unreliable under Prisma, so `import.meta.url` is the cwd-independent ESM-native form. `__filename`/`__dirname` are inlined, not declared, to avoid `no-redeclare` against Node globals | A child `tsx` process adds ~200 ms startup over an in-process import (negligible for a one-shot seed); bare `tsx` must be on `PATH` (guaranteed in the pnpm/Prisma contexts that run the seed, and forwarded via `env: process.env`); the three `..` levels assume the fixed `packages/db/prisma/` layout, so a directory move requires updating them |

## `packages/db` — Prisma migrations

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Full-text search column named `contentTsv` (index `Message_contentTsv_idx`)                                                                                                                                                                                                           | The earlier `contentSearch` / `Message_contentSearch_idx` names                                                                 | `contentTsv` is the checkpoint/AAP-specified name that later search queries (`prisma.$queryRaw` in `search.service.ts`) are written against. A mismatched name fails at runtime with a missing-column error.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | The generated column must stay in sync with the Prisma schema authored in CP2; the migration is the source of truth until then.                                                                                             |
| 1:1 DM uniqueness enforced via sorted `participantOneId`/`participantTwoId` columns on `DirectMessage` plus a unique pair index, retaining `DMParticipant` for membership                                                                                                             | (a) Rely only on the `DMParticipant(dmId,userId)` PK; (b) a single canonical `participantKey` string column with a unique index | The `DMParticipant` PK only prevents duplicate participants inside one DM — it does not stop two `DirectMessage` rows holding the same pair, violating the AAP "unique composite on the participant pair". Sorted columns + a unique index give deterministic DB-level enforcement and stay queryable; a concatenated key (b) is opaque and harder to join on.                                                                                                                                                                                           | The service layer MUST canonicalise the pair (sort the two user ids) before insert so the unique index is effective — an application invariant the CP2 service code must honour.                                            |
| Message cursor indexes created `createdAt DESC, id DESC` (the `channelId`/`dmId` composites and the standalone `createdAt` index)                                                                                                                                                     | Default ascending `createdAt` indexes (relying on PostgreSQL backward scans)                                                    | Pagination loads newest-first with a `(createdAt, id)` cursor; a matching `DESC, DESC` index represents that contract explicitly and serves the ordering without depending on backward-scan behaviour.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Ascending range scans for the rare oldest-first case use the index less optimally; acceptable because the product only paginates newest-first.                                                                              |
| DB-level `VARCHAR(n)` caps mirroring `packages/shared/src/constants/limits.ts` (`displayName` 80, channel `name` 80 / `description` 250, message `content` 4000, reaction `emoji` 64) plus `VARCHAR(255)` on file `originalName`/`storedName`/`mimeType`                              | Unbounded `TEXT` everywhere, relying solely on Zod validation at the API                                                        | DB caps add defense-in-depth against oversized direct writes (DoS/data-integrity) independent of the API. The 80/250/4000/64 values mirror the shared limit constants; 255 is the conventional bound for filesystem names and MIME types. No `CHECK` constraint is added — the forbidden Message channel/DM XOR check is intentionally omitted.                                                                                                                                                                                                          | The DB caps must stay in sync with the shared constants if those limits change; the CP2 Prisma schema expresses these via `@db.VarChar(n)`.                                                                                 |
| `File.uploadedById` made nullable with FK `ON DELETE SET NULL ON UPDATE CASCADE`                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Keep `NOT NULL` with `ON DELETE CASCADE` (delete file metadata when the uploader is deleted)                                    | The checkpoint requires uploaded-file records to survive deletion of the uploader; `SET NULL` preserves the file row and clears only the author reference, which `CASCADE` cannot do on a non-nullable column.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | A file can exist with no uploader (`uploadedById IS NULL`); consumers and the CP2 Prisma relation must treat the uploader as optional.                                                                                      |
| `Message.contentTsv` kept as `Unsupported("tsvector")? @default(dbgenerated("to_tsvector('english'::regconfig, (content)::text)"))` in `schema.prisma`, with a marker comment that the real column is `GENERATED ALWAYS AS (...) STORED`, owned by raw-SQL migration `20260527000001` | Remove the `@default` and document the column as unmanaged; model it as a plain `tsvector` column                               | `prisma db pull` of the deployed STORED generated column reproduces exactly this `@default(dbgenerated(...))` form, and `migrate diff --from-migrations -> --to-schema-datamodel` reports NO drift against it; removing the `@default` INTRODUCES drift (`ALTER COLUMN ... DROP DEFAULT`), and a from-empty diff emits an invalid `DEFAULT to_tsvector(content)` (column ref in a DEFAULT). So `@default(dbgenerated())` is Prisma's own canonical introspection of a STORED generated column and is the drift-free choice (CP2 review remediation, C4). | `prisma migrate dev` must never regenerate this column from the schema (it would emit the invalid DEFAULT form); the generated-column DDL lives only in the raw-SQL migration, which is the source of truth for the column. |
| Every Prisma relation declares an explicit `onUpdate` (`Cascade` on all FKs except `Message.parent`, which is `onDelete: NoAction, onUpdate: NoAction`) mirroring the migration FK clauses verbatim                                                                                   | Rely on Prisma's implicit `onUpdate: Cascade` default and omit the annotations                                                  | The init migration emits `ON UPDATE CASCADE` on all 14 FKs except `Message_parentId_fkey` (`ON UPDATE NO ACTION`); stating each `onUpdate` explicitly makes `schema.prisma` self-documenting and proves zero drift — `migrate diff` confirms "No difference detected" because the explicit value equals Prisma's implicit default (CP2 review remediation, M29).                                                                                                                                                                                         | None of note; the explicit annotations equal the generated SQL, so behaviour is unchanged and the schema simply states what the migration already enforces.                                                                 |

## `packages/api` — Configuration (env loader)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                         | What alternatives existed                                                                   | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Zod-validated env loader (`packages/api/src/config/env.ts`) calls `EnvSchema.parse(process.env)` inside a `loadEnv()` function and throws a formatted `Error` on failure | `safeParse` + `process.exit(1)`; lazy per-getter validation; no validation at all           | Fail-fast at module load surfaces an immediate, human-readable diagnostic before any other module initialises, satisfying Gate 12; throwing rather than calling `process.exit` keeps the module import-safe and unit-testable while still aborting startup, and a `z.ZodError` is reformatted via `error.format()` into the thrown message. Updated during CP2 review remediation — the earlier `safeParse` + `process.exit(1)` mechanism is superseded. | An invalid environment cannot be recovered without a restart — the intended behaviour for a configuration error; the process entry point must not swallow the throw.                                                                                          |
| `JWT_SECRET` requires `.min(32)` characters (no default)                                                                                                                 | No minimum; 16 chars; 64 chars                                                              | 32 bytes is the recommended floor for HS256 signing-key strength (AAP §0.8.4 security baseline).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Operators must supply a real 32+ char secret; the `.env.example` placeholder is long enough to pass and documents the requirement.                                                                                                                            |
| `BCRYPT_ROUNDS` requires `.min(10)`, default `10`                                                                                                                        | No minimum; default/minimum of 12                                                           | 10 is the OWASP-recommended minimum bcrypt cost factor (AAP §0.8.4); keeping it as the default while allowing higher values lets ops tune the work factor via env.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Higher rounds increase login latency; ops can raise the value when hardware allows.                                                                                                                                                                           |
| `CORS_ORIGIN` defaults to `http://localhost:5173`                                                                                                                        | No default (require it); derive it from `VITE_APP_URL`                                      | Neither root nor `packages/api/.env.example` declares `CORS_ORIGIN`, so a default equal to the Vite dev origin keeps `make local` working out of the box (Gate 1).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Production deployments must override it; this row is the single source of truth for that obligation.                                                                                                                                                          |
| The env loader throws a formatted `Error` on failure and no longer calls `console.error`; Pino is the only logging path in the API package                               | Log the failure via `console.error` before exiting; a temporary console-based pseudo-logger | The Pino logger imports from env.ts, so logging the env failure there would be circular and the logger is not yet constructed; throwing defers presentation to the process entry point and keeps env.ts free of `console`. Updated during CP2 review remediation — the earlier `console.error` fail-fast use is superseded.                                                                                                                              | The thrown error must reach a top-level handler or Node's default printer to be visible; intended, since an unhandled configuration error should abort with a stack trace.                                                                                    |
