| `z.coerce.number()` for the numeric vars `PORT`, `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB`, `BCRYPT_ROUNDS`                                                                                     | A custom `transform`; `parseInt` + `refine`                                                 | `process.env` values are always strings; `z.coerce.number()` is the idiomatic Zod way to convert and then validate via `.int().positive()` / `.min()`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | None of note.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| `.startsWith('postgresql://')` on `DATABASE_URL` and `.startsWith('redis://')` on `REDIS_URL`, in addition to `.url()`                                                   | `z.string().url()` alone                                                                    | `.url()` accepts any scheme, so a mis-pasted `http://` connection string would pass; the scheme guard rejects that class of typo at startup with a clear message before Prisma/ioredis fail later.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Belt-and-suspenders validation that overlaps `.url()`; accepted in exchange for an earlier, clearer failure.                                                                                                                                                  |
| Schema field named `PORT` (reads `process.env.PORT`, default `3000`), matching the `env.PORT` export contract                                                            | Read `API_PORT` (the name used in both `.env.example` files); support both names            | The file schema and agent prompt specify `PORT`, and consumers (`index.ts` → `httpServer.listen(env.PORT)`) depend on `env.PORT`; the default `3000` converges with the `.env.example` `API_PORT=3000`, so `make local` (Gate 1) works with no `PORT` set.                                                                                                                                                                                               | If an operator sets a non-default `API_PORT` expecting the server to follow, `env.PORT` will not track it; the server port and the Makefile health-check URL should both align on `PORT` (or `PORT` should be set explicitly) when a custom port is required. |

## `packages/web` — Web client package manifest

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                          | What alternatives existed                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Package named `@app/web` (workspace dependency declared as `@app/shared`)                                                                                                 | Use the AAP/agent-prompt illustrative name `@blitzy-slack/web` (and `@blitzy-slack/shared`)                  | The actual workspace convention set during setup is `@app/*` — `packages/shared`/`db`/`api` are `@app/shared`/`@app/db`/`@app/api`, and the root `dev:web` script, the `Makefile` `local`/`dev` targets, and `pnpm --filter` all reference `@app/web`. Naming the package `@blitzy-slack/web` would break `pnpm install` (no `@blitzy-slack/shared` package exists to satisfy `workspace:*`) and every `--filter @app/web` invocation. Mirrors the precedent already recorded for `@app/db`. | None functional; this aligns the manifest with the real workspace. If the monorepo is ever renamed to `@blitzy-slack/*`, every package, the root scripts, and the `Makefile` must be renamed together. |
| `@tailwindcss/postcss` is NOT declared as a dependency                                                                                                                    | Declare `@tailwindcss/postcss` (as the agent-prompt skeleton suggested, "referenced by `postcss.config.js`") | The committed `packages/web/postcss.config.js` is a deliberate no-op (`export default { plugins: {} }`) because Tailwind v4 is processed by the `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin wired in `vite.config.ts`; nothing imports `@tailwindcss/postcss`, and it is not listed in AAP §0.3.1. Declaring it would add an unused dependency.                                                                                                                                                               | If a future change moves Tailwind processing to the PostCSS pipeline, `@tailwindcss/postcss` must be added then; the `vite` plugin remains the single processing path until that change is made.       |
| Build/test tooling (`tailwindcss`, `@tailwindcss/vite`, `vite`, `@vitejs/plugin-react`, `@types/react`, `@types/react-dom`, `@playwright/test`) kept in `devDependencies` | Place the Tailwind packages in `dependencies` (per the agent-prompt skeleton)                                | These are build-time tools: Tailwind compiles to CSS at build, Vite bundles, types and Playwright are dev-only — none are imported into the runtime bundle. Keeping them in `devDependencies` matches the committed manifest and the sibling treatment of `vite`/`@vitejs/plugin-react`. For a private, never-published workspace app the placement is immaterial to resolution (pnpm installs both groups for workspace packages).                                                          | If this package were ever published or installed with `--prod`, build tooling would be excluded — acceptable because it is `private` and only ever installed in dev mode via `pnpm install`.           |
| `typescript` is NOT declared in this package's `devDependencies`                                                                                                          | Declare `typescript` locally (as the earlier committed manifest did)                                         | The root workspace declares `typescript` and pnpm hoists its `tsc` bin to the workspace-root `node_modules/.bin`, which is exposed to filtered package execution — verified: `pnpm --filter @app/api exec tsc` and `--filter @app/shared exec tsc` both resolve TypeScript 5.9.3 without a local declaration. Omitting it matches the `@app/shared`/`@app/db`/`@app/api` siblings, none of which declare `typescript`.                                                                       | If the root ever drops `typescript`, this package's `build`/`typecheck` (`tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit`) would fail; the root manifest is the single source for the compiler version.                 |
| `cmdk` and the `@radix-ui/react-accordion`/`@radix-ui/react-alert-dialog` primitives are retained as runtime `dependencies`                                               | Restrict the manifest to only the ten Radix packages explicitly enumerated in the agent-prompt skeleton      | `cmdk` backs the shadcn `Command` primitive that AAP §0.5.2 maps to the Ctrl+K quick switcher (the skeleton omitted it); `accordion`/`alert-dialog` back catalogued shadcn primitives from AAP §0.2.2 and are present in the committed manifest. AAP §0.3.1 declares `@radix-ui/react-*` as "latest matching shadcn add", so a superset that covers the catalogued primitives is compliant and avoids breaking components added later by `npx shadcn@latest add`.                            | A small number of Radix packages may go unused if the corresponding components are never generated; unused entries add negligible install weight and are not bundled unless imported.                  |
| `build` runs `tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit && vite build`; the dead `test:e2e` script was removed                                                                        | `build` = `vite build` alone; keep a per-package `test:e2e` script                                           | Vite/esbuild does not type-check, so prefixing `tsc --noEmit` enforces Rule 3 (strict, zero-warning) before bundling in the root `pnpm -r build` path. The former `test:e2e` ("playwright test") was dead because there is no `playwright.config` in `packages/web` — E2E runs from the repository root (`make test-e2e` → root `playwright test` over `packages/web/test/e2e`).                                                                                                             | The `tsc` gate makes `build` fail on any type error (intended). E2E is now invoked only from the root; a developer must not expect `pnpm --filter @app/web test:e2e` to exist.                         |
| `vite.config.ts` defines no `server.proxy`; the web client calls the API at the absolute `import.meta.env.VITE_API_URL` / `VITE_WS_URL`                                   | Add a Vite dev proxy that forwards `/api` and the Socket.io path to `http://localhost:3000`                  | AAP §0.6.2 places CORS on the API side (the API allow-lists the `http://localhost:5173` dev origin — see the `CORS_ORIGIN` row above), so the browser reaches the API directly on its own origin. A proxy would mask CORS misconfiguration in development and make the effective request origin ambiguous between dev (same-origin, proxied) and production (cross-origin).                                                                                                                  | The API must keep the Vite origin on its CORS allow-list (already defaulted). A future single-origin deployment would still work via absolute URLs but without the proxy's same-origin convenience.    |
| `server.port: 5173` and `preview.port: 4173` are pinned with `strictPort: true`                                                                                           | Omit `strictPort` and let Vite auto-increment to the next free port when 5173/4173 is occupied               | The dev port is contractually referenced by `VITE_APP_URL`, the root `playwright.config.ts` `baseURL`, and the API CORS allow-list; a silent shift to 5174 would break the Playwright `baseURL` and CORS. `strictPort` keeps `make local` deterministic by failing loudly instead of drifting to another port.                                                                                                                                                                               | If 5173 (or 4173 for `vite preview`) is already in use, the server refuses to start — an intentional fail-fast that requires the developer to free the port before retrying.                           |
| `vite.config.ts` sets `build.target: 'es2022'`                                                                                                                            | Vite's default `'modules'` target; a lower `'es2015'` or higher `'esnext'`                                   | `es2022` matches `tsconfig.base.json` `target: ES2022`, so the bundler emits the language level TypeScript type-checks against (top-level `await`, class fields), keeping build output and type-check assumptions aligned; the PoC targets current Chromium/Firefox/WebKit, all of which support ES2022 (CP2 review remediation moved this rationale out of the config comment, M17).                                                                                                        | Pre-2022 browsers are unsupported; acceptable for the PoC's modern-browser scope.                                                                                                                      |

## `packages/web` — shadcn/ui component manifest (`components.json`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                        | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| shadcn `style: "new-york"` selected in `components.json`                                                                                | `style: "default"`, the other shadcn preset                                                                                                                                  | shadcn is deprecating the `default` style and initialises all new Tailwind-v4 projects with `new-york`; its denser shadows and smaller default radius better match Slack's tight, compact web UI (Rule 1), and it keeps the manifest aligned with the CLI's current defaults rather than a deprecated preset.                                                                                                                                                                                          | `style` cannot be changed after initialisation without deleting and re-adding components; a later switch to `default` would require regenerating every `src/components/ui/*` primitive.                         |
| `tailwind.config` left as an empty string (`""`) — a deviation from the agent-prompt skeleton, which illustrated `"tailwind.config.ts"` | Set `"config": "tailwind.config.ts"` and author a `tailwind.config.ts` (the Tailwind v3 / Next.js convention)                                                                | The web package uses Tailwind CSS v4, processed by the `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin with a deliberate no-op `postcss.config.js`; there is no `tailwind.config.ts` and theming is expressed via the `@theme` directive in `src/index.css` (AAP §0.5.1, §0.5.3). The official shadcn documentation states that for Tailwind v4 the `tailwind.config` field must be left blank; pointing it at a non-existent file would misconfigure the CLI. The skeleton value reflected the older Tailwind-v3 template. | If the project is ever downgraded to Tailwind v3, or a JS/TS Tailwind config is introduced, this field must then point at that config's path; until then the empty string is the correct, CLI-supported value.  |
| `baseColor: "neutral"` with `cssVariables: true` (and `prefix: ""`) chosen as the manifest theming foundation                           | Another shadcn base palette (`slate` / `gray` / `zinc` / `stone`); `cssVariables: false` (inline colour utilities); or baking the Slack aubergine directly into the manifest | `neutral` is a pure-grayscale foundation onto which the Slack-aubergine palette is layered via `@theme` overrides in `src/index.css` (AAP §0.5.3), which keeps shadcn updates clean and the colour override in a single place. `cssVariables: true` is required by Tailwind v4's `@theme` token mechanism; `false` would emit inline colour utilities and break the design-token architecture. The manifest itself carries no colour literals, consistent with Rule 1 and Rule 3.                      | `baseColor` and `cssVariables` cannot be changed after initialisation without deleting and re-installing components; the aubergine override must be maintained in `src/index.css` rather than in this manifest. |

## `packages/web` — Theme tokens (`src/index.css`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| OKLCH color space for every theme token in the `@theme` block                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | sRGB hex literals, HSL, or P3 wide-gamut                                                                                                        | Tailwind v4's default palette is authored in OKLCH and the `@theme` mechanism expects static color values; OKLCH is perceptually uniform, so the aubergine and lavender steps interpolate predictably, and Rule 1 + Rule 3 forbid hex/rgb/hsl literals in app code.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | OKLCH requires a modern engine (no IE11); acceptable because the PoC targets current Chromium/Firefox/WebKit.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| Slack-aubergine sidebar palette expressed as the eight `--color-sidebar*` `@theme` tokens that override shadcn's neutral baseColor                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Keep shadcn's grayscale sidebar; or bake the aubergine directly into each component                                                             | Rule 1 (Screenshot-Driven UI) requires the dark-aubergine sidebar and lavender active accent seen in screenshots 29/100; centralising them as tokens keeps every shadcn primitive and utility class consistent and the override in one place (AAP §0.5.3).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | The OKLCH values are snapped approximations of sampled sRGB; if Slack's palette is re-captured the tokens must be re-tuned.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| `--color-sidebar-bg` anchored to the canonical Slack aubergine `#3F0E40` rather than the lighter sampled channel-sidebar surface                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Pin `--color-sidebar-bg` to the sampled channel-sidebar gradient midpoint (~`oklch(0.36 0.087 323)`, sRGB `#4D2651`–`#562F5C`)                  | AAP §0.5.3 explicitly cites "~#3F0E40" as the sidebar reference and it is Slack's canonical brand aubergine; the far-left workspace rail samples at `#3A0E3C`–`#3F1543`, confirming this exact aubergine is present in the screenshots. The lighter channel-sidebar step is `--color-sidebar-hover`. The exact AAP §0.5.3 token names `--color-sidebar-bg` and `--color-sidebar-hover` are used — CP2 review remediation renamed them from the earlier `--color-sidebar` / `--color-sidebar-accent`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | The rendered channel-sidebar column is ~10–15% darker than the Mobbin capture; still unmistakably Slack aubergine, and Gate 8 visual thresholds tolerate the difference.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| `--color-primary` set to the Slack blue/link accent `#1164A3` (`oklch(0.491 0.125 248)`), replacing shadcn neutral's near-black primary                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Keep shadcn neutral primary (`oklch(0.205 0 0)`); or use Slack's green send-button CTA `#007A5A`                                                | AAP §0.5.3 maps the active-channel/link accent (~#1164A3) to `--color-primary`; screenshots 29/100 show links (`#design`, Edit description) and the reaction chip rendered in this blue.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Slack's send-button green is a separate component-level accent and is intentionally NOT modelled as `--color-primary`; downstream agents must not treat `bg-primary` as the send button.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| Light mode only — no dark-mode token set in this file                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Add a parallel `.dark` / `:root.dark` token block with dark OKLCH values                                                                        | Dark mode is out of scope for the PoC (AAP §0.7.2) and the reference screenshots depict the light content area; the file-spec restricts this file to one `@theme` and one `@layer base` block.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | A future dark mode requires a second token set plus a `dark` variant and runtime variable indirection; recorded here as a known follow-up.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| Tailwind v4 `@import 'tailwindcss';` + `@theme` directive, not the v3 `@tailwind base/components/utilities` directives                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Tailwind v3 directives with a JS `theme` config object                                                                                          | AAP §0.5.1 prescribes Tailwind v4 with `@tailwindcss/vite`; the `@theme` directive emits both the CSS variable and the matching `bg-*`/`text-*`/`border-*` utility for each token, which `components.json` `cssVariables: true` relies on.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | v4 is newer and a few third-party plugins lag it; none are used by this file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| Each `--color-*` custom property declared exactly once (the Slack primary is written directly, not as a neutral value then re-declared)                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Emit shadcn's neutral `--color-primary` and then re-declare the Slack value lower in the same block (as the file-spec illustrated the override) | A single declaration is unambiguous about the final value and avoids any duplicate-custom-property diagnostic if stylelint is added later (Rule 3 zero-warning).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | The override relationship to shadcn neutral is documented here rather than being visible as two declarations in the file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| `@import 'tailwindcss';` written with single quotes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Double quotes (`@import "tailwindcss";`) as the agent file-spec illustrated                                                                     | The repository's enforced Prettier config sets `singleQuote: true`, and `prettier --check .` (run by `make format` and the format gate) rewrites CSS strings and attribute selectors to single quotes; single- and double-quoted `@import` are equivalent to the Tailwind v4 parser, so honouring the formatter keeps the file passing the build's format gate.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Purely stylistic; if the `singleQuote` policy ever changes the formatter rewrites it automatically.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| The active-channel selected-state highlight (light lavender `#F7EDFE`, ~`oklch(0.959 0.025 312)`) is NOT added as a theme token                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Add a bespoke `--color-sidebar-selected` token                                                                                                  | The shadcn sidebar token contract is fixed at the eight `--color-sidebar*` names and the file-spec mandates exactly those; the selected-channel pill is a component-level treatment owned by the downstream ChannelList component.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | The reference value is recorded here so the downstream component can reuse it; a token can be promoted later if several components need it.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| The active-channel selected-state highlight is PROMOTED to two `@theme` tokens — `--color-sidebar-accent` (light-lavender pill background) and `--color-sidebar-accent-foreground` (dark-aubergine pill text) — added to `src/index.css`; this supersedes the row above that left the highlight as a non-token "component-level treatment" | (a) keep it component-level as the superseded row planned; (b) a bespoke `--color-sidebar-selected` token                                       | The `ChannelListItem` file-spec mandates the exact utilities `bg-sidebar-accent`, `text-sidebar-accent-foreground`, and `hover:bg-sidebar-accent/50` and its "Final Note" states `src/index.css` MUST define these tokens; Tailwind v4 only emits a `bg-*` / `text-*` utility for a token that exists in `@theme`, so without them the active highlight silently renders nothing (a broken view, UI10). Under Rule 1 / Rule 3 a component-level colour would have to be an arbitrary-value class (`bg-[oklch(...)]`) or inline style — both forbidden colour literals — so a token is the only compliant path. The superseded row anticipated exactly this ("a token can be promoted later if several components need it") and recorded the reference value, which this promotes; the name follows shadcn's sidebar semantic (`accent` = selected-item surface). Values: `--color-sidebar-accent: oklch(0.95 0.02 320)` (independent sample from screenshots 29/100, within imperceptible ΔE of the earlier-recorded `oklch(0.959 0.025 312)`) and `--color-sidebar-accent-foreground: oklch(0.21 0.045 318)` (sampled near-black active-row text) | Re-introduces the `--color-sidebar-accent` identifier that CP2 review remediation had renamed to `--color-sidebar-hover`, now with a DIFFERENT meaning (active/selected pill, not the hover/lighter-aubergine step) — the distinction is recorded here; the sidebar consequently carries two "lightening" treatments (`--color-sidebar-hover` aubergine vs `bg-sidebar-accent/50` lavender), and the component uses the latter per its spec |

### Color token resolution

All sRGB → OKLCH conversions use the standard sRGB → linear-light → OKLab → OKLCH pipeline (Ottosson, 2020). Sampled sRGB values are averaged pixel patches taken from `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 29.png` and `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 100.png`. The shadcn neutral baseColor tokens are preserved verbatim from the shadcn "neutral" light-mode palette and are not re-derived here.

| Token(s)                                                                              | sRGB reference (source)                                                                                 | Final OKLCH                    | Note                                                                                                                       |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `--color-sidebar-bg`                                                                  | `#3F0E40` (AAP §0.5.3 canonical aubergine; workspace rail sampled `#3A0E3C`–`#3F1543`)                  | `oklch(0.272 0.101 327)`       | Slack brand aubergine; the dominant sidebar surface.                                                                       |
| `--color-sidebar-hover`                                                               | ~`#532C58` (channel-sidebar lighter step, sampled `#4D2651`–`#562F5C`)                                  | `oklch(0.37 0.09 323)`         | Hover / lighter-aubergine step.                                                                                            |
| `--color-sidebar-border`                                                              | ~`#310A33` (darker than the sidebar background)                                                         | `oklch(0.234 0.086 326)`       | Derived darker aubergine for dividers.                                                                                     |
| `--color-sidebar-ring`                                                                | ~`#8B5C90`                                                                                              | `oklch(0.545 0.096 323)`       | Mid-lavender focus ring.                                                                                                   |
| `--color-sidebar-foreground`                                                          | `#F8DAFF` (lightest sampled sidebar text, chroma reduced)                                               | `oklch(0.94 0.022 320)`        | Near-white lavender, tuned for legibility on aubergine.                                                                    |
| `--color-primary`, `--color-sidebar-primary`                                          | `#1164A3` (AAP §0.5.3 lavender/blue accent; link samples `#305C91`/`#356592`/`#38649B` confirm the hue) | `oklch(0.491 0.125 248)`       | Active-channel / link / focus accent.                                                                                      |
| `--color-primary-foreground`, `--color-sidebar-*-foreground`                          | near-white                                                                                              | `oklch(0.985 0 0)`             | Foreground on the accent/aubergine surfaces (shadcn neutral).                                                              |
| `--color-background`, `--color-card`, `--color-popover`                               | `#FFFFFF` (white content area, screenshot 29)                                                           | `oklch(1 0 0)`                 | shadcn neutral; the white content column.                                                                                  |
| neutral foreground / secondary / muted / accent / destructive / border / input / ring | shadcn neutral light-mode (grayscale; destructive in the red family)                                    | as authored in `src/index.css` | Preserved verbatim from the shadcn "neutral" baseColor palette.                                                            |
| `--color-sidebar-accent`                                                              | `#F7EDFE` (active-pill highlight, screenshots 29/100; reference recorded earlier in this section)       | `oklch(0.95 0.02 320)`         | Light-lavender selected-channel pill background; within imperceptible ΔE of the earlier-recorded `oklch(0.959 0.025 312)`. |
| `--color-sidebar-accent-foreground`                                                   | ~`#100319` (active-row text, sampled `rgb(16, 3, 25)`)                                                  | `oklch(0.21 0.045 318)`        | Near-black aubergine text for contrast on the light active pill.                                                           |

## `scripts` — Test-user seed (`seed-via-api.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                          | What alternatives existed                                                                               | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                               |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The seeder is **dual-mode**: a CLI entry (detected via `process.argv[1] === fileURLToPath(import.meta.url)`, used by `make seed`) and a default-exported `globalSetup` consumed by `playwright.config.ts` | Two separate scripts (one CLI, one for Playwright); a Playwright-only or CLI-only seeder                | One module is the single source of the seed logic for both `make seed` and the E2E run, so the test user is created identically in both paths with no drift                                                                                                                                                                                  | The dual-entry detection relies on `import.meta.url`/`argv[1]` semantics under `tsx` ESM; documented here so future refactors keep both entry points working        |
| Seeding calls `POST /api/auth/register` with Node's **native `fetch`** and **no workspace imports**                                                                                                       | `node-fetch` or `axios`; importing `@app/shared` for the request type; inserting into Postgres directly | Rule 4 (AAP §0.8.1) mandates seeding through the registration endpoint, never a direct DB insert; Node 22's built-in `fetch` removes a dependency, and keeping the script import-free keeps `tsx` ESM resolution trivial                                                                                                                     | The hardcoded request body must stay shape-compatible with `registerSchema` in `packages/shared/src/schemas/auth.ts`; if that schema changes, this body must follow |
| HTTP **201 and 409 are both treated as success** (idempotent seeding); any other status, a network error, or the timeout is a failure                                                                     | Treat only 201 as success (re-runs fail once the user exists); ignore all errors                        | `make local` and the E2E setup may run repeatedly against a populated database; a 409 `Conflict` (user already exists) means the seed goal is already met, so it counts as success                                                                                                                                                           | A 409 from an unrelated cause would be masked as success; acceptable because the register endpoint returns 409 only for the duplicate-email case                    |
| A **60-second `AbortController` timeout** guards the request                                                                                                                                              | No timeout (hang until TCP fails); a shorter 5–10s timeout                                              | `make local` starts the API in the background and polls health, but the seed can still race a slow first boot; 60s tolerates cold starts while still failing rather than hanging forever                                                                                                                                                     | An API that takes longer than 60s to first response fails the seed; the error message tells the developer to confirm the API is running and reachable               |
| The seeder polls `GET /api/health` (`waitForApiHealth`) until it returns 2xx before calling `POST /api/auth/register`, in both the CLI and Playwright-globalSetup paths                                   | Register immediately and rely on the `Makefile` health gate alone; gate only the `make local` path      | Standalone `make seed` and the Playwright `globalSetup` can run without the `Makefile` loop in front of them, so gating inside the script guarantees Rule 4's "seed only after the API is healthy" for every invocation (CP2 review remediation, M20/M21); each poll is bounded by its own `AbortController` and the loop by a 60s deadline. | If `/api/health` never reaches 2xx within 60s the seed fails with a descriptive error; intended fail-fast rather than registering against an unready API.           |

## `packages/api` — Service errors (`middleware/errors.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                      | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Services throw **typed error classes** from `middleware/errors.ts` (`abstract ServiceError` → `UnauthorizedError` 401 / `ForbiddenError` 403 / `NotFoundError` 404 / `ConflictError` 409 / `ValidationError` 400 / `AppError` caller-supplied); each subclass exposes a `readonly statusCode` that the error-handler middleware reads, with `instanceof` for dispatch | Services return HTTP responses directly (`res.status().json()`); framework-specific error objects; a single untyped error type | Keeping services transport-agnostic (they never touch `res`) lets the same service code back both HTTP routes and Socket.io handlers, and centralises status mapping in one place; carrying `statusCode` on each subclass makes the HTTP status intrinsic to the error rather than re-derived by a `switch`. The module lives under `middleware/` (CP2 review remediation moved it from `services/errors.ts`) so the AAP/checkpoint import path `packages/api/src/middleware/errors.ts` resolves. | `instanceof` identity must survive module boundaries — the base restores the prototype chain with `Object.setPrototypeOf` so the checks stay reliable under NodeNext; a forgotten prototype restore would break dispatch. |
| `errors.ts` is a **zero-import, lowest-level module**, and Prisma's own `PrismaClientKnownRequestError` is intentionally NOT wrapped here (the error-handler maps it separately via `P2002 → 409`, `P2025 → 404`)                                                                                                                                                     | Wrap Prisma errors into the custom classes inside `errors.ts`; import Prisma types here                                        | Zero imports keep the module at the bottom of the services dependency tree so every service and the middleware can import it without cycles; Prisma error mapping belongs to the middleware that already owns HTTP translation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | New Prisma error codes are mapped in the error-handler middleware, not here — a separation contributors must remember                                                                                                     |

## `packages/api` — Socket.io room keys (`sockets/rooms.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | What alternatives existed                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                         |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Room keys are built by **four centralised pure helpers** — `channelRoom` → `channel:<id>`, `dmRoom` → `dm:<id>`, `threadRoom` → `thread:<id>`, `userRoom` → `user:<id>` — and every `io.to`/`io.in` and `socket.join`/`socket.leave` routes through them | Inline string concatenation at each call site; an enum or namespace of room prefixes | A single source for the room-key format guarantees the keys the `@socket.io/redis-adapter` publishes on are identical everywhere (AAP §0.4.5); inline concatenation drifts and silently breaks cross-instance delivery | The helpers do no input validation (cuid shape is enforced by Zod at the route/socket boundary); passing an unvalidated id would produce a malformed room key, so callers must validate first |

## `packages/api` — Jest runner config (`jest.config.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| The Jest config lives at the package root `packages/api/jest.config.ts` with `rootDir: '.'` (`packages/api/`)                                                                                                                                                                                                       | A config co-located with the suites under `test/jest.config.ts` (`rootDir: '..'`)                                                                                                                                                                              | The package-root location is the AAP/checkpoint-conventional path a bare `jest` invocation auto-discovers, so `make test` (script-driven) and a bare `jest` behave identically; CP2 review remediation moved it here from `test/jest.config.ts` and dropped the `--config` flag from the package scripts                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | None of note; standard discovery means no `--config` flag is required, and `test/setup.ts` is wired via `setupFiles`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| ts-jest with the `ts-jest/presets/default-esm` preset is the test transformer                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | `babel-jest` (no type-checking), `@swc/jest` (fastest, no type-checking), or Bun's test runner (different runtime)                                                                                                                                             | AAP §0.3.1 pins `ts-jest`; running the suites through ts-jest type-checks every `.ts` file at compile time (`diagnostics.warnOnly: false`), so the test run itself enforces Rule 3 strictness. The `default-esm` preset (not `default`) matches the api package's `"type": "module"`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | ts-jest is slower than swc/esbuild transformers; acceptable at PoC suite size and offset by the type-safety guarantee                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Workspace dependencies are resolved by `moduleNameMapper` straight to each package's **source** (`<rootDir>/../shared/src`, `<rootDir>/../db/src`) rather than to built `dist/` output                                                                                                                              | Build every workspace package to `dist/` before testing; rely solely on the pnpm symlink plus each package's `exports` map                                                                                                                                     | Source resolution removes a build step from `make test`, lets ts-jest compile workspace TypeScript directly, and mirrors the source-first dev model Vite uses in `packages/web`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Tests can run against source that has not been built to `dist/`; mitigated because each package has its own `tsc -p … --noEmit` typecheck script                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| The `moduleNameMapper` keys target the real workspace names **`@app/shared`** and **`@app/db`**                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | The `@blitzy-slack/shared` / `@blitzy-slack/db` names written in this file's own implementation seed                                                                                                                                                           | Deviation logged per the Explainability rule: the packages are actually scoped `@app/*` (their `package.json` `name` fields and the api package's `workspace:*` deps confirm it). The seed's `@blitzy-slack/*` keys would have produced a mapper that matches no import — dead config. This aligns with the existing log rows that scope packages `@app/*`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | If the workspace is ever rescoped to a different npm scope, these mapper keys must be updated in lockstep                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| `ts-node@^10.9.2` was added to `packages/api` devDependencies, beyond the AAP §0.3.1 inventory                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Keep the loader-free root `jest.config.mjs`; precompile the config to JS; author a `.cjs`/`.js` config instead of `.ts`                                                                                                                                        | Deviation logged per the Explainability rule: Jest 29 reads a **`.ts`** config by registering `ts-node` at bootstrap (ts-jest transforms test files at runtime but does not read the config file itself). The assigned file is mandated to be `.ts`, so `ts-node` is a necessary implicit dependency (AAP §0.1.2). Jest invokes it with a forced `module: CommonJS` override, so the ESM-package `.ts` config loads correctly                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | One extra devDependency plus a `pnpm-lock.yaml` update; the lockfile delta is confined to the ts-node subtree and `--frozen-lockfile` was re-verified so Gate 1 still passes                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| The api `test` / `test:watch` / `test:coverage` scripts rely on Jest auto-discovery of the package-root `jest.config.ts` (no `--config` flag); the redundant `jest.config.mjs` stub was deleted and `--passWithNoTests` was removed so the coverage gate cannot pass with zero tests                                | Keep an explicit `--config` flag; leave the `.mjs` stub in place; retain `--passWithNoTests`                                                                                                                                                                   | A single canonical root config with auto-discovery makes `make test` and a bare `jest` behave identically; removing `--passWithNoTests` (CP2 review remediation) restores the Gate 13 >=80% coverage gate now that a real `errors.test.ts` suite exists                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | A developer must keep at least one runnable test in the package or `jest` exits non-zero (intended for the coverage gate)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| Coverage thresholds set to **80** for lines/functions/statements and **70** for branches (`coverageThreshold.global`), collected from `src/services/**/*.ts`                                                                                                                                                        | A uniform 80 across all four metrics; a lower 60 floor; no enforced threshold                                                                                                                                                                                  | Gate 13 mandates an 80% line floor on the services layer; lines/functions/statements reach 80 with reasonable suites, while branch coverage lags initially because error/ACL branches accrue more slowly, so a 70 branch floor lets the suite land without masking the line-coverage gate                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Branch coverage sits below the 80% industry norm until the suites mature; the branch floor can be raised once per-service ACL/error-path tests exist                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| `setupFiles` is the empty array `[]` (superseding the first row's note that `test/setup.ts` is wired via `setupFiles`); `test/setup.ts` is now loaded only by an explicit `import './setup.js'` from the integration suites, never auto-run per worker                                                              | Keep `setupFiles: ['<rootDir>/test/setup.ts']`; split into a tiny env-only `setupFiles` shim plus the helper; move connection setup into `globalSetup`/`globalTeardown`                                                                                        | The AAP redefines `test/setup.ts` as the shared test-infrastructure HELPER, and it imports `config/redis.ts`, whose ioredis clients use `lazyConnect: false` — so the mere import OPENS three Redis connections; auto-running it in EVERY worker would open those sockets even in suites that never use them (e.g. `errors.test.ts`) and, with Jest `forceExit:false`, the open handles hang the run. Each suite that needs the infra imports `./setup.js` and calls `closeTestResources()` in its own `afterAll`; env now comes from `config/env.ts`'s `loadDotenv()` plus `setup.ts`'s first-statement `NODE_ENV='test'` and Jest's default. Verified: `errors.test.ts` runs and exits cleanly with `--detectOpenHandles` reporting none                                                                                                               | A suite that forgets `closeTestResources()` leaks Redis/Prisma handles for that run; mitigated by the documented `afterAll(closeTestResources)` contract every integration suite follows and by Node tearing down sockets on process exit                                                                                                                                                        |
| The per-file Gate 13 coverage gaps on `messages.service.ts` (74.79%) and `presence.service.ts` (79.59%) were closed by adding two SERVICE-LEVEL suites (`test/messages.service.test.ts`, `test/presence.service.test.ts`) that invoke the service functions directly, separate from the existing route-level suites | Append `describe` blocks to the existing route suites (`messages.test.ts` / `presence.test.ts`); add per-file `coverageThreshold` overrides; lower the gate; widen the `GET /:id/replies` route to surface the reply cursor purely to make HTTP tests reach it | The uncovered lines — reply-cursor pagination (`encodeReplyCursor`/`decodeReplyCursor`/`resolveReplyLimit`), DM-message add/remove reactions, the presence away/offline read-time buckets, and the single-user `getPresence` getter — are unreachable over HTTP because `GET /api/messages/:id/replies` intentionally returns only the first page (thread sizes are bounded in the PoC) and the route Zod schemas reject the defensive-guard inputs (XOR violation, oversized/empty content, malformed cursor) before the service runs; only direct service calls reach them.
