SEPARATE files (not appended `describe`s) give each suite its own fresh Jest module registry and its own `afterAll(closeTestResources)`, matching the per-suite teardown contract. The change is purely additive — no service source was modified (322/322 already passed) | Two more suites add a few seconds to `make test`; mitigated by `maxWorkers:1` serial execution plus `beforeEach(cleanDatabase)` and per-key Redis teardown keeping state isolated. Driving the service directly bypasses the route Zod layer, so these tests assert service-internal guards the HTTP path would reject earlier — intended, since those guards are precisely the lines under test |

## `packages/api` — Configuration (Pino logger, `config/logger.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                           | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                 |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Pino as the logging library, exposed as a single `logger` singleton constructed at module load                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Winston; Bunyan; bare `console`                                                                                                     | Pino is the fastest structured logger, is JSON-first, is widely supported by aggregators (Loki, CloudWatch, Datadog), and has the `pino-http` / `pino-pretty` ecosystem the rest of the API relies on (Gate 10)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Less feature-rich than Winston (no built-in transport fan-out) — acceptable for a PoC; a second sink would need a custom transport                                                    |
| `pino-pretty` transport is attached **only** when `NODE_ENV === 'development'`; test and production emit raw JSON to stdout                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Pretty output in every environment; never pretty (raw JSON even in dev)                                                             | Production logs must stay machine-ingestible JSON, while dev ergonomics need human-readable colorized lines; gating on `NODE_ENV` gives both without a code change                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | The dev pretty path spawns a `pino-pretty` worker thread on first flush (negligible overhead); the two code paths must be kept behaviourally equivalent apart from formatting         |
| Redaction policy covers authorization (`req.headers.authorization`, `res.headers.authorization`, bare `authorization`, `*.authorization`), cookies (`req.headers.cookie`, `req.headers["set-cookie"]`, `res.headers["set-cookie"]`, `["set-cookie"]`) and credential/token fields (`password`, `passwordHash`, `token`, `secret`, `jwt` as bare keys plus `req.body.*` and one-level `*.` wildcards), with `censor: '[REDACTED]'` and `remove: false` | Redact nothing (trust producers); redact an exhaustive deny-list of everything that looks sensitive                                 | A conservative, explicit allow-list blocks the known secret-bearing fields (JWTs, cookies, set-cookie response headers, credentials) emitted by `pino-http` and ad-hoc logs while keeping the log shape intact for ingestion (`remove: false`). Expanded during CP2 review remediation to add bare/nested `authorization`, `set-cookie`, `secret`, and `jwt` variants.                                                                               | A novel secret-bearing field name would slip through; mitigated by this documented policy and by producers not passing secrets explicitly.                                            |
| Timestamps use `pino.stdTimeFunctions.isoTime` (ISO 8601 UTC strings)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Pino default Unix-epoch milliseconds; locale-specific formatting                                                                    | ISO 8601 is sortable, timezone-explicit, and the lingua franca of log aggregators                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Marginally larger log lines than an epoch integer (negligible)                                                                                                                        |
| The level formatter emits the string label (`formatters.level(label) => { level: label }`) so lines carry `"level":"info"`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Pino default numeric levels (`"level":30`)                                                                                          | String labels are human-scannable in a raw `tail` and friendlier to downstream parsing/alerting while preserving structured semantics                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Differs from the Pino default; documented here so consumers expect labels, not numbers                                                                                                |
| `env.LOG_LEVEL` (when set) overrides the `NODE_ENV`-derived default (`debug` in development, `info` in test/production), resolved in `resolveLogLevel()`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | A `NODE_ENV`-only level with no override hook                                                                                       | Ops can raise or lower verbosity at runtime via env without a code change or redeploy                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A forgotten `LOG_LEVEL=trace` (or `silent`) in production would over- or under-log; mitigated by env review and the fail-fast env loader making the value visible                     |
| `resolveLogLevel()` is annotated `: Level \| 'silent'` instead of the agent prompt's literal `: Level`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Return pino's `Level` verbatim (the prompt's literal); treat `'silent'` as the `NODE_ENV` default and drop it; suppress with a cast | Deviation logged per the Explainability rule: pino 9.x's exported `Level` union omits `'silent'`, but `env.LOG_LEVEL` is validated as `z.enum([...,'silent']).optional()` and may legitimately be `'silent'`. `Level \| 'silent'` is structurally identical to pino's `LevelWithSilent`, is assignable to `LoggerOptions.level` (`LevelWithSilentOrString`), preserves the explicit-`silent` behaviour, and compiles with zero `@ts-ignore` (Rule 3) | If a future pino major adds `'silent'` to `Level`, the union becomes redundant (harmless); the narrowed name `Level` is still imported and used so the schema's import contract holds |
| The static `base.service` log field is the literal `'@blitzy-slack/api'` even though the workspace package is scoped `@app/api`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Use the real package name `@app/api`; derive it from `package.json` `name` at runtime                                               | Deviation logged per the Explainability rule: `service` is a free-form observability label (not a module specifier, so unlike the Jest `moduleNameMapper` keys it has no resolution requirement), the project itself is named `blitzy-slack` (catalog-info.yaml / mkdocs), and the file schema plus the spec's own validation command assert on exactly `"service":"@blitzy-slack/api"`                                                              | A reader correlating logs with the npm package name sees `@blitzy-slack/api` rather than `@app/api`; this row is the single source of truth reconciling the two                       |

## `packages/api` — Request validation middleware (`middleware/validate.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                         | What alternatives existed                                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Validated payloads are funnelled through an explicitly `unknown`-typed local (`const data: unknown = parsed.data; req.body = data;` and `const source: unknown = req[target];`) before being written back to the request | Make `validate` generic over `z.infer<T>`; cast `parsed.data` to a concrete type; relax the `no-unsafe-assignment` lint rule | Zod's `ZodTypeAny.safeParse().data` and Express 5's `req.body`/`req[target]` are both typed `any`, which tripped `@typescript-eslint/no-unsafe-assignment` and failed the module-wide zero-warning gate (Rule 3). Routing the value through `unknown` is the lint-sanctioned way to tame an `any`, keeps the public overload signatures unchanged, and preserves runtime behaviour exactly. Fixed during `logger.ts` validation as the module-level final validator (the file is an in-scope AAP CREATE and had no call sites yet, so the change is zero-blast-radius) | The middleware still does not statically type the parsed output for downstream handlers; a future generic refactor over `z.infer<T>` would carry the schema's type through to `req.body`, and this row should be superseded when that lands |
| On Zod failure the validator calls `next(new ValidationError(...))` (built by `toValidationError(error, source)` carrying `error.flatten().fieldErrors`), not `next(parsed.error)` with the raw `ZodError`               | Pass the raw `ZodError` to `next`; format the 400 response inline in the middleware                                          | Wrapping in the project `ValidationError` (status 400) routes Zod failures through the same typed-error -> error-handler mapping as service-thrown errors, so HTTP and Socket.io paths produce one consistent 400 shape with field details (CP2 review remediation, M4); the raw `ZodError` would force the error-handler to special-case Zod.                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | `ValidationError.details` carries Zod's `fieldErrors` map; the error-handler must serialise it into the 400 body, and a future schema change reshapes those details.                                                                        |

## CP2 review remediation — seed decisions & dependency hardening

The eight decisions the AAP §0.6.3 seed mandates, recorded here during CP2 review remediation alongside the security upgrades they motivated.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                        | What alternatives existed                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| shadcn/ui consumed via the copy-paste CLI model (`npx shadcn@latest add`) that emits owned source under `src/components/ui/`, not as a runtime npm component dependency | Install a packaged component library (a published npm `@shadcn/ui`); build bespoke primitives directly on Radix | shadcn's distribution model IS copy-paste (AAP §0.5.1): the components become first-party source the project owns and restyles with the Slack-aubergine tokens, with no version-locked black-box dependency; it is the only supported shadcn workflow for Tailwind v4.                                                                                                                | Future shadcn upgrades require re-running the CLI per component rather than one `npm update`, and local edits can diverge from upstream; the `ui/**` tree is intentionally ESLint-ignored as vendored code. |
| Password hashing uses `bcryptjs` (pure JS), replacing native `bcrypt`                                                                                                   | Keep native `bcrypt@5.1.1`; switch to `argon2`; pin a patched `bcrypt`                                          | `bcrypt@5.1.1` pulls `@mapbox/node-pre-gyp -> tar@6.2.1`, which `pnpm audit` flags high-severity; `bcryptjs` is the AAP §0.3.2-documented portable fallback, has zero native/transitive deps (clearing the `tar` path), ships its own types, and exposes the same `hash`/`compare` API (CP2 review remediation, C3). No API code imported `bcrypt` yet, so the swap is manifest-only. | `bcryptjs` is ~30% slower than native `bcrypt` at the same cost factor; acceptable at PoC login volume and `BCRYPT_ROUNDS` is tunable.                                                                      |
| Client state (`auth`, `presence`) held in Zustand stores                                                                                                                | React Context + `useReducer`; Redux Toolkit; Jotai/Recoil                                                       | Zustand (AAP §0.3.1) gives a minimal hook store with selector subscriptions and no provider boilerplate, so a Socket.io event can update the presence map outside React and only subscribed components rerender; Context rerenders all consumers and Redux Toolkit adds boilerplate disproportionate to a PoC.                                                                        | Global singleton stores need discipline to avoid scattered mutations; mitigated by keeping mutations behind named actions in `stores/*.ts`.                                                                 |
| Routing uses React Router 7                                                                                                                                             | TanStack Router; Next.js App Router; wouter                                                                     | React Router 7 is the AAP §0.3.1 pin, is React 19-compatible, and its `BrowserRouter`/`createBrowserRouter` model covers the nested authenticated shell and modal/sheet routes without adopting a meta-framework; TanStack Router's type-safe routing adds a learning curve and codegen step not needed here.                                                                         | RR7 merged the former Remix data APIs; the project uses library (BrowserRouter) mode only and must not be confused with framework mode.                                                                     |
| Full-text search uses a PostgreSQL `tsvector` generated column + GIN index, queried via `prisma.$queryRaw`                                                              | `pg_trgm` trigram similarity; an external engine (Elasticsearch/Meilisearch/Typesense); `ILIKE` scans           | A native `tsvector`/GIN index gives ranked, language-aware search inside the existing Postgres with no extra infrastructure (AAP §0.4.4), keeping `make local` single-stack; trigram suits fuzzy/prefix not word search, and an external engine adds a service to run and sync — both disproportionate for the PoC.                                                                   | `tsvector` is word/stemming based (no fuzzy typo tolerance); ACL filtering runs in the service layer after the index match and the search service must always apply it.                                     |
| Cross-instance Socket.io fan-out uses `@socket.io/redis-adapter`                                                                                                        | A hand-rolled Redis pub/sub bridge over `io.emit`; a single sticky-session instance with no adapter; NATS/Kafka | The official adapter (Rule 2, AAP §0.3.1) transparently makes `io.to(room).emit(...)` reach clients on any instance via Redis pub/sub, handling room/ack semantics a custom bridge would have to reimplement; a single instance would not meet the horizontal-scale intent.                                                                                                           | Adds a hard Redis dependency for real-time delivery (already required for presence); an adapter major upgrade must track the Socket.io server version.                                                      |
| File uploads use `multer` 2.x (`^2.0.1`), upgraded from the `1.4.5-lts.x` line                                                                                          | Stay on `multer@1.4.5-lts.1`; use `busboy` directly; `formidable`                                               | The `1.4.4-lts.1 ... <2.0.1` range carries high-severity malformed-multipart and empty-field-name DoS advisories; `multer` 2.x patches both, keeps the identical `diskStorage`/`.single()` API (verified against `upload.ts`), and drops the `node-pre-gyp`/`tar` transitive path (CP2 review remediation, C2). 2.x is verified compatible with Express 5.                            | `multer` 2.x is a newer major; the middleware was smoke-tested but route-level upload tests land in CP3 and must re-confirm behaviour.                                                                      |
| Uploaded files stored on the local filesystem at `FILE_UPLOAD_PATH`, served via Express static                                                                          | Object storage (S3/GCS/MinIO) with signed URLs                                                                  | Local disk is the AAP §0.7.2-scoped PoC choice: no cloud credentials or extra service, keeping `make local` self-contained; object storage is explicitly an out-of-scope production follow-up.                                                                                                                                                                                        | Local storage does not survive container/host loss and does not scale across instances; flagged as a production-only migration (signed-URL object storage) when the PoC graduates.                          |

## Root workspace & tooling — Playwright E2E runner (`playwright.config.ts`)

Decisions for the root Playwright configuration that drives the `packages/web/test/e2e` suite (`make test-e2e` → root `playwright test`).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                          | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                         | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| All three browser engines — `chromium`, `firefox`, AND `webkit` — are declared UNCONDITIONALLY in `projects` (no env gate), satisfying the AAP's literal "three projects" requirement (Gate 8 / Gate 13). | Gate `webkit` behind `PLAYWRIGHT_WEBKIT=1` (the prior CP2 behaviour the CP3 review flagged); drop WebKit entirely.                                                | CP3 requires the config to DEFINE chromium, firefox, and webkit. The config is the portable contract: on a supported OS or the official `mcr.microsoft.com/playwright` image all three launch. The host-specific WebKit limitation is recorded as an explicit exception (see the CP3 remediation section) rather than bending the config to one machine.                                                                   | On this host (Ubuntu 25.10, ICU 76 vs WebKit's ICU 74) the `webkit` project cannot launch, so `make test-e2e` runs WebKit red here; use a supported image, or scope to `--project=chromium --project=firefox` locally. Recorded as an accepted environment-specific exception in the CP3 remediation section. |
| `reporter` is `[['html', { open: 'never' }], ['list']]`, declared inline inside `defineConfig`.                                                                                                           | The prior stub's env-conditional `process.env.CI ? 'github' : 'list'`; a single `'list'` or `'html'` reporter; extracting the reporter array to a typed variable. | A persistent HTML report (written under `playwright-report/`, which `make clean` already removes) is useful locally and on CI, while `list` gives live progress; `open: 'never'` stops it launching a browser in headless/CI runs. Keeping the array inline lets `defineConfig` contextually type the literals as `ReporterDescription` tuples — extracting to a variable widens them to plain arrays and breaks the type. | GitHub Actions inline annotations (the `'github'` reporter) are not emitted; they can be added as a third reporter entry under CI if wanted.                                                                                                                                                                  |
| `expect.toHaveScreenshot` is configured centrally with `maxDiffPixelRatio: 0.02` and `threshold: 0.2`.                                                                                                    | Playwright defaults (no pixel-ratio cap); duplicating per-assertion options in every spec.                                                                        | Gate 8's `screenshot-fidelity.spec.ts` explicitly relies on these tolerances being supplied centrally and does not repeat them on each `toHaveScreenshot` call; a 2% pixel-ratio budget absorbs anti-aliasing and font-rasterisation variance across machines while still catching layout regressions.                                                                                                                     | Genuine visual diffs affecting under 2% of pixels pass; baselines are Chromium-only (other engines rasterise differently), which is why the fidelity suite restricts itself to Chromium.                                                                                                                      |
| `webServer` is gated behind `PLAYWRIGHT_AUTOSTART`: when set it boots `pnpm --filter @app/api dev` (waited on via `…/api/health`) and `pnpm --filter @app/web dev`; otherwise it is `undefined`.          | Always autostart both servers from Playwright; never autostart and require `make local` first.                                                                    | `make local` / `make test-e2e` normally start the API and web servers externally, so unconditional autostart would collide with already-running servers; gating delegates the default path to Make while giving CI/standalone runs a one-flag bring-up. Filters use the workspace's `@app/*` scope (not the planning-seed `@blitzy-slack/*`).                                                                              | When `PLAYWRIGHT_AUTOSTART` is unset the servers must already be listening or specs fail fast on first navigation; `reuseExistingServer` is disabled on CI to force a clean boot.                                                                                                                             |
| CI-aware execution profile: `forbidOnly: !!process.env.CI`, `retries: process.env.CI ? 2 : 0`, `workers: process.env.CI ? 1 : undefined`, with `fullyParallel: true`.                                     | Identical settings for CI and local; multiple parallel workers on CI.                                                                                             | Serialising to a single worker on CI keeps real-time/WebSocket ordering deterministic and avoids cross-test interference on the shared seeded user, while local runs stay fully parallel for speed; CI retries absorb genuinely flaky network timing, and `forbidOnly` stops a stray `test.only` silently shrinking the CI suite.                                                                                          | Single-worker CI runs are slower, and retries can mask intermittent product bugs — a spec that only passes on retry should still be investigated.                                                                                                                                                             |

## `packages/web` — HTTP API client (`src/lib/api-client.ts`)

Decisions for the typed `apiClient` fetch wrapper — the single declaration site for all REST traffic to the API (AAP §0.4.2); direct `fetch` elsewhere is forbidden.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                         |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| A custom `ApiError extends Error` carrying `status: number` and `body: unknown` is thrown on every non-2xx response and on network failure.                                                                                                     | Throw the raw `Response`; throw strings; a result-type `{ ok: false, error }` pattern.                                                                                                       | A typed `Error` subclass gives uniform `try/catch` across hooks and components and carries the status plus parsed body for granular error UX (e.g. a 409 conflict and a 422 validation error drive different toasts).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A generic `ErrorBoundary` could swallow it; mitigated by feature hooks catching explicitly and surfacing via Sonner.                                                                          |
| Response validation is opt-in per call via `options.schema` (`ZodType<T>`), not enforced on every call; the client itself imports nothing from `@app/shared`.                                                                                   | Mandatory schema on every call; no response validation at all.                                                                                                                               | Balances safety against `schema.parse` CPU cost — untrusted or critical endpoints (auth, message create) pass a schema while trusted or cosmetic ones (health) may skip it; keeping the client schema-agnostic avoids bundling every shared schema into this base layer.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Drift between the API shape and the client's expectation on schema-less calls; mitigated by integration and E2E coverage of each endpoint.                                                    |
| A 401 response calls `useAuthStore.getState().logout()` before re-throwing `ApiError(401)`.                                                                                                                                                     | Throw only and leave logout to the caller; logout only and swallow the error; route logout through a global event bus.                                                                       | Bundles the side effect (clear the token, disconnect the socket) with error propagation, so the UI redirects to `/login` while the caller can still surface a "session expired" toast.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | A 401 returned by the login endpoint itself would also call logout; harmless because the store is already in the logged-out state, so `logout()` is a no-op there.                            |
| The DELETE helper is named `del`, not `delete`.                                                                                                                                                                                                 | A quoted `'delete'` property key; a `remove` alias.                                                                                                                                          | `delete` is a reserved word and cannot be a method-shorthand name; the folder spec uses `del` verbatim, and the method body still sends the `DELETE` verb.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | A minor naming mismatch with the HTTP verb; mitigated by the correct verb inside the request.                                                                                                 |
| The JWT is read at request time via `useAuthStore.getState().token`, never cached at module load.                                                                                                                                               | Cache the token at module load; cache it at the first authenticated call.                                                                                                                    | The auth store is the single source of truth for the token, and a user may sign in after this module loads — a cached initial `null` would freeze the client to the logged-out state.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | One extra `getState()` call per request (sub-microsecond); negligible.                                                                                                                        |
| DEVIATION from the verbatim AAP source: three type assertions in the seed snippet — `(body as { error: unknown })`, `(body as { message: unknown })`, and `body as FormData` — were dropped (left as `body.error`, `body.message`, and `body`). | Keep the verbatim casts and suppress `@typescript-eslint/no-unnecessary-type-assertion` with an `eslint-disable` comment or a per-file config override; weaken the workspace ESLint ruleset. | Under the project's actual toolchain (TypeScript 5.9.3 with `no-unnecessary-type-assertion` from `recommendedTypeChecked`), control-flow narrowing — `'error' in body`, `'message' in body`, and the `isFormData` const-alias guard — already yields the exact target type, so the casts are reported as unnecessary and fail `eslint --max-warnings 0` (Rule 3). Removal is type-identical (confirmed by `tsc --noEmit` and by the rule's own analysis) and is exactly what `eslint --fix` would apply; Rule 3 outranks byte-for-byte fidelity to the seed snippet. | The file is no longer byte-identical to the AAP snippet; the runtime behaviour and the public type surface are unchanged, and the deviation is confined to removing provably redundant casts. |
| A new ambient `packages/web/src/vite-env.d.ts` augments the global `ImportMetaEnv` with `VITE_API_URL`, `VITE_WS_URL`, and `VITE_APP_URL` typed as `readonly string`.                                                                           | A triple-slash `/// <reference types="vite/client" />` template file; inline-typing the env read inside `api-client.ts`; leaving the keys as `any`.                                          | `api-client.ts` is the first `import.meta.env` consumer in the web source, and Vite's default `ImportMetaEnv` index signature types `VITE_API_URL` as `any`, which trips the `no-unsafe-*` rules on `.replace()` and fails Rule 3. A global interface merge (no `import`/`export`, and no triple-slash since `vite/client` is already in the tsconfig `types` array) types the keys as `string` without altering the verbatim client; triple-slash was avoided because `@typescript-eslint/triple-slash-reference` would flag it.                                    | Any future `VITE_*` variable must be added to this interface to stay typed; low maintenance and standard Vite practice.                                                                       |
| DEVIATION from the verbatim AAP snippet: `src/lib/api-client.ts` was reformatted with the repository's Prettier config (`printWidth: 100`), collapsing several multi-line expressions and method signatures onto single lines.                  | Commit the file with the snippet's narrower (~80-col) wrapping; add the file to `.prettierignore`; widen Prettier's `printWidth` to preserve the original wrapping.                          | The workspace ships `eslint-config-prettier` plus `format` / `format:check` scripts, so Prettier is the authoritative formatter and `make format` (`prettier --write .`) would reformat the file regardless; committing a file that fails `prettier --check` would leave a formatting violation. The edit is whitespace-only — `eslint --max-warnings 0` and all 39 ad-hoc behavioral assertions still pass — so repo-wide formatting consistency outranks byte-for-byte fidelity to the snippet's wrapping.                                                         | The file is no longer byte-identical to the AAP snippet; runtime behavior and the public type surface are unchanged, and the deviation is limited to line wrapping.                           |

## `packages/api` — Configuration (Redis clients, `config/redis.ts`)

Decisions for the three ioredis client connections and the graceful-shutdown helper exported by `config/redis.ts`. The module owns the `@socket.io/redis-adapter` wiring behind a `createRedisAdapter()` factory that returns `createAdapter(pubClient, subClient)`; the bootstrap in `src/index.ts` calls it and passes the result to `io.adapter(...)` (Rule 2).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                           | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `redis.ts` exposes a `createRedisAdapter()` factory returning `createAdapter(pubClient, subClient)` from `@socket.io/redis-adapter`, alongside the raw `pubClient`/`subClient`/`redisClient` ioredis instances; the bootstrap calls `io.adapter(createRedisAdapter())` in `src/index.ts` | Export the raw clients only and assemble `createAdapter(pubClient, subClient)` at the call site (the prior CP2 approach); export a pre-built adapter INSTANCE rather than a factory | CP3 requires the Redis adapter foundation to be exposed FROM this module (Rule 2). A factory (not a pre-built instance) defers `createAdapter` until the bootstrap calls it, so importing `redis.ts` does not eagerly build the adapter while the raw clients stay available for presence reads. This supersedes the CP2 decision that kept `@socket.io/redis-adapter` out of this module                                                                                                                 | `redis.ts` now imports `@socket.io/redis-adapter`, so it is no longer coupled to `ioredis` alone; the bootstrap must still invoke `createRedisAdapter()` once and pass the result to `io.adapter(...)`                                                                    |
| Three DISTINCT `new Redis(env.REDIS_URL, baseOptions)` connections — `pubClient`, `subClient`, and `redisClient` (presence)                                                                                                                                                              | Reuse a single client for publish, subscribe, and presence; or build `subClient` as `pubClient.duplicate()`                                                                         | `@socket.io/redis-adapter` REQUIRES independent pub and sub connections (a Redis connection in subscriber mode cannot serve ordinary commands), and keeping presence on its own `redisClient` avoids head-of-line blocking behind the subscriber connection (AAP §0.4.5, Rule 2); `.duplicate()` is intentionally avoided so each connection is constructed identically and independently from `env.REDIS_URL`                                                                                            | 3× the connection count to Redis (acceptable at PoC scale) and three sockets to close on shutdown, handled by `disconnectRedisClients()`                                                                                                                                  |
| `maxRetriesPerRequest: 3` on the shared `baseOptions`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | The ioredis default (`20`); `null` (retry a command indefinitely)                                                                                                                   | Fails a command after three retries so a persistent Redis problem surfaces quickly to operators instead of silently hanging requests; transient blips are still absorbed by `reconnectOnError`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | A Redis hiccup spanning more than three retries can fail an in-flight command; mitigated by `reconnectOnError` reconnecting on `READONLY`/`ECONNRESET`/`ETIMEDOUT`                                                                                                        |
| `lazyConnect: false` (eager connect at construction) together with `enableReadyCheck: true`                                                                                                                                                                                              | `lazyConnect: true` (defer the connection until the first command)                                                                                                                  | Eager connection surfaces a Redis misconfiguration at startup rather than at the first request; `make local` waits for the Redis healthcheck before starting the API, so the eager connect succeeds on a clean bring-up (Gate 1)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Importing the module raises connection errors at startup if Redis is unreachable (the intended fail-fast); any consumer importing `redis.ts` opens three TCP connections as a load-time side effect, so `index.ts` must call `disconnectRedisClients()` on SIGTERM/SIGINT |
| URL credentials stripped via a local `safeUrl()` helper, and only the resulting `REDIS_URL_SAFE` is ever logged; the `error` event handler logs `err.message` only                                                                                                                       | Log the raw `env.REDIS_URL`; or log nothing about the URL at all                                                                                                                    | The raw connection string may embed credentials (AAP §0.8.4 security baseline), so logging it verbatim would leak secrets; stripping `username`/`password` via the Node `URL` API keeps the diagnostic value (host, port, db) without the auth portion, and never stringifying the whole error keeps connection details out of the logs                                                                                                                                                                   | A small extra surface (one helper); if `env.REDIS_URL` is unparseable the log shows the constant `[invalid url]` placeholder rather than a real value                                                                                                                     |
| DEVIATION from the verbatim agent-prompt snippet: in `disconnectRedisClients()` a rejected settle result is logged as a narrowed string (`result.reason instanceof Error ? result.reason.message : String(result.reason)`) instead of the raw `err: result.reason`                       | Log `err: result.reason` verbatim and suppress the resulting lint error with an `// eslint-disable` comment; weaken the workspace ESLint ruleset                                    | `PromiseRejectedResult.reason` is typed `any`, so `{ err: result.reason }` trips `@typescript-eslint/no-unsafe-assignment` and fails `eslint --max-warnings 0` (Rule 3) — verified empirically with a throwaway probe. Narrowing to the message is also strictly more compliant with the §0.8.4 baseline ("log `err.message` only, never the whole error"), and `@ts-ignore`/`eslint-disable` are forbidden by Rule 3. Runtime behaviour is preserved — a rejection is still logged with its client label | The logged value is the error message string, not the original error object; acceptable because §0.8.4 forbids serialising the whole error anyway                                                                                                                         |

## `packages/api` — Messages service (`services/messages.service.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                          | What alternatives existed                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                             |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Threads are single-level — `createMessage` rejects a `parentId` whose target is itself a reply (`parent.parentId !== null` → `ValidationError`)                                                                           | Allow arbitrary reply nesting (a reply to a reply)                                                           | Slack's thread model is single-depth (AAP §0.6.3 thread side panel); a flat `parentId` self-reference keeps `listThreadReplies` a single `where: { parentId }` lookup and the thread UI a flat list                                                                                                                         | A future need for nested threads would require schema and query changes; explicitly out of scope per AAP §0.7.2                                                                   |
| `addReaction` is an idempotent `upsert` on the `messageId_userId_emoji` composite (empty `update: {}`), and `removeReaction` is a `delete` whose Prisma `P2025` ("record to delete does not exist") is swallowed          | Read the reaction first, then conditionally `create`/`delete` (check-then-act)                               | The single-statement upsert/delete is atomic and race-free and lets the client call add/remove blindly without first fetching state; the `@@unique([messageId, userId, emoji])` constraint guarantees no duplicate rows                                                                                                     | The idempotent remove path constructs and discards one `PrismaClientKnownRequestError` when the reaction was absent; a negligible cost for the simpler client contract            |
| Both reaction mutations re-fetch the full message (`findUniqueOrThrow` with author/reactions/file/`_count` includes) to build the returned `MessageWithAuthor`                                                            | Mutate the in-memory reaction array and return the message without a second query                            | The database stays the single source of truth for the post-mutation reaction set, so the DTO can never drift from persisted state, and it reuses the exact include shape used by `createMessage`/`listThreadReplies`                                                                                                        | One extra `SELECT` per reaction operation; negligible at PoC scale and well within the Gate 9 latency budget                                                                      |
| A file may be attached only by its uploader — `createMessage` throws `ForbiddenError` when `File.uploadedById !== authorId`                                                                                               | Allow any authenticated user to attach any previously uploaded `File` by id                                  | Prevents attachment hijacking (user A uploads a file, user B references its id on their own message); combined with `Message.fileId @unique`, a file binds to exactly one message and one owner                                                                                                                             | A legitimate multi-step "upload then send" flow must run under the same authenticated session; enforced and expected                                                              |
| `listThreadReplies` returns replies ASC (oldest-first), whereas channel/DM timelines paginate DESC (newest-first)                                                                                                         | Use one consistent ordering direction across all message reads                                               | A thread panel reads top-to-bottom from the parent while a channel reads bottom-to-top with infinite scroll; each endpoint matches its UI's natural reading order                                                                                                                                                           | Consumers must know the per-endpoint direction; documented in the function JSDoc and here                                                                                         |
| `listThreadReplies` is cursor-paginated — `base64url(JSON({createdAt,id}))` cursor, ASC (oldest-first), `take: limit + 1` peek, default `PAGE_SIZE` (50), cap `MAX_PAGE_SIZE` (100), returning `{ messages, nextCursor }` | Return the entire reply list unpaginated (the prior CP2 behaviour the CP3 review flagged); offset pagination | CP3 requires `listThreadReplies` to paginate with the SAME `(createdAt, id)` cursor + `take + 1` peek contract as the channel/DM timelines, so a long thread cannot load unbounded rows; ASC ordering matches the thread panel's top-to-bottom reading order                                                                | Clients must follow `nextCursor` to walk a long thread; the wire DTO gains a `nextCursor` field (additive, non-breaking)                                                          |
| DEVIATION from this file's `depends_on_files` metadata: the domain error classes (`ForbiddenError`, `NotFoundError`, `ValidationError`) are imported from `../middleware/errors.js`                                       | Import them from `packages/api/src/services/errors.ts`, the path named in the file's dependency metadata     | No `services/errors.ts` exists; the committed error classes live in `middleware/errors.ts` (see the _Service errors_ section above) and `search.service.ts` already imports them from there. Importing the same named symbols from their actual location is the only compilable path and keeps the service layer consistent | The dependency metadata names a path that differs from the real one; this row makes the reconciliation explicit so the deviation is not treated as a defect (Explainability rule) |

## `packages/api` — Channels service (`services/channels.service.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                         | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| The channel creator is made an `owner` by inserting the `Channel` row and the creator's `ChannelMember` row (with `role: 'owner'`) inside a single `prisma.$transaction`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Two sequential un-transacted writes; a post-insert `update` of the member row; relying on the schema default `role: 'member'` and never marking an owner                                                          | Atomicity guarantees a channel never exists without its owner membership, and the explicit `'owner'` overrides the schema's `'member'` default in one round-trip. A non-transactional pair could leave an orphaned channel with no members if the second insert failed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | The role vocabulary is just `'owner'`/`'member'` (no admin tier — out of scope per AAP §0.7.2); a richer role model would need a schema change                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| `joinChannel` refuses PRIVATE channels with `ForbiddenError`; only public channels are self-joinable                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Allow self-join of private channels; implement an invite/token flow; silently no-op for private channels                                                                                                          | The PoC has no invitation flow (AAP §0.7.2), and private-channel membership is established at creation time with members pre-baked. Blocking self-join keeps the private-channel ACL meaningful — otherwise any user could join any private channel by id                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Private channels can only gain members through creation-time seeding until an invite flow is added; this is an accepted PoC scope limitation, surfaced to the user as a 403                                                                                                                                                          |
| The message-history cursor is `base64url(JSON({ createdAt, id }))` — an opaque compound (createdAt, id) token                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | A bare message `id`; a numeric `OFFSET`; a signed JWT cursor; a raw (unencoded) JSON string                                                                                                                       | A compound (createdAt, id) key gives a stable total order even when several messages share a millisecond timestamp (cuid `id` breaks ties), matching the `ORDER BY createdAt DESC, id DESC` contract of AAP §0.8.4. `base64url` is URL-safe (no `+`, `/`, `=` to escape in a query string) and trivially decodable for debugging. This mirrors the identical cursor used by `dms.service.ts` for one pagination contract across channels and DMs                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | The cursor embeds the `createdAt` representation, so a change to how timestamps are stored could invalidate in-flight cursors; acceptable for a PoC and versionable later. The token is opaque but NOT authenticated — a client could forge one, but it only shifts that same caller's own page window, leaking nothing              |
| Pagination uses a `take: limit + 1` "peek" to compute `hasMore`/`nextCursor`, rather than a separate `COUNT`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | A second `COUNT(*)` query over the same `WHERE`; offset pagination; always returning a cursor                                                                                                                     | Fetching one extra row determines whether an older page exists in a single query, avoiding a second round-trip and the staleness a `COUNT` can show under concurrent inserts. `nextCursor` is emitted only when the peek row is present, so the client stops paging exactly when the timeline is exhausted                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | One surplus row is fetched per page and discarded — negligible at the 50-row PoC page size                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| The channel timeline returns only top-level messages (`where: { parentId: null }`); thread replies are excluded                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Return every message flat (replies inline with parents); fetch replies and merge in memory                                                                                                                        | AAP §0.6.3 renders replies in a separate thread side-panel (served by `messages.service.listThreadReplies`), so the channel view shows only roots. Filtering in the query keeps the page size meaningful (a busy thread cannot crowd out other conversations)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | A reply is invisible until its thread panel is opened; acceptable and consistent with the Slack UI model                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| `leaveChannel` translates Prisma `P2025` ("record to delete does not exist") into `NotFoundError`, making the operation idempotent from the client's view                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Let `P2025` propagate as a 500; pre-check membership with a `findUnique` then delete (check-then-act); return success even when no row was deleted                                                                | "Leave a channel you are not a member of" is semantically a 404 (the membership resource does not exist), and catching the single delete's `P2025` avoids a check-then-act race in one statement. Returning success silently would hide a genuinely wrong channel id from the caller                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Constructing and discarding one `PrismaClientKnownRequestError` on the not-a-member path; negligible cost for the simpler, race-free contract                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| DEVIATION from this file's `depends_on_files` / agent-prompt metadata: error classes are imported from `../middleware/errors.js` and workspace types from the `@app/*` scope (not `./errors.js` / `@blitzy-slack/*`); `ChannelMember` and `ChannelWithMembers` are NOT imported; `listChannels` maps each row to `ChannelSummary` as `{ id, name, isPrivate }` only; reaction summaries use the `hasCurrentUser` field | Import error classes from a non-existent `services/errors.ts`; import every type named in the metadata regardless of use; add a `memberCount` / `description` to the summary; name the reactor flag `reactedByMe` | No `services/errors.ts` exists — the committed classes live in `middleware/errors.ts`, and the sibling `dms`/`messages`/`search` services already import them from there. Packages are scoped `@app/*` (see the package-scope rows above), not `@blitzy-slack/*`. Importing `ChannelMember`/`ChannelWithMembers` or emitting `memberCount` would be a Rule 3 violation: the unused imports trip `@typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars` and `noUnusedLocals`, and `memberCount`/`description` are absent from the actual `ChannelSummary` shape (`{ id, name, isPrivate, unreadCount? }`), so the object would fail to typecheck. The actual `ReactionSummary` field is `hasCurrentUser`. Matching the shipped contracts is the only path that compiles under `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint --max-warnings 0` | The metadata names paths/types/shapes that differ from the real ones; this row makes the reconciliation explicit so the deviation is not treated as a defect (Explainability rule). `memberCount` is therefore unavailable from the list endpoint and must come from a future channel-detail endpoint returning `ChannelWithMembers` |

## `packages/api` — Files service (`services/files.service.ts`)
