| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | What alternatives existed                                                                                                  | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| File access control is derived from message visibility: `getFile` grants access iff a `Message` referencing the file lives in a channel the caller is a member of or a DM the caller participates in — there is no separate `FileAccess(fileId, userId)` table                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | An explicit `FileAccess` share table; an ACL list stored on the `File` row                                                 | Messages already enforce channel/DM ACL, and `Message.fileId @unique` binds a file to exactly one message, so file visibility can inherit from its containing message with no extra schema or sync logic; a single `message.findFirst` with an `OR` over `channel.members.some` / `dm.participants.some` decides access in one query                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A file uploaded but never attached to a message is reachable only by its uploader (see next row); were the `@unique` constraint ever relaxed, inheritance could over-grant — the constraint prevents this today |
| The uploader (`File.uploadedById === userId`) is granted access unconditionally and the ACL message lookup is short-circuited                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Require the uploader to also be a member/participant of the referencing message's channel/DM before serving their own file | A user who uploads a file but has not yet sent the message must not lose access to their own upload (the two-step "upload then send" flow), and skipping the lookup on the owner path saves a query                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Marginal — the uploader already holds a valid session token; an uploaded-but-unsent file stays private to its uploader, which is the intended behaviour                                                         |
| `createFile` re-checks `multerFile.size` against `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB * 1024 * 1024` and throws `ForbiddenError` (not `ValidationError`) when exceeded                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Trust multer's `limits.fileSize` entirely and omit the service check; throw `ValidationError` instead                      | Defense-in-depth against a misconfigured upload middleware: multer should reject oversize uploads first (HTTP 413), so reaching this branch is a security-layer failure the client cannot trigger through normal input — 403 fits better than a 400 input error — and the check is a single numeric comparison logged at `warn`                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | None of note — under correct multer configuration the branch is unreachable; it exists only to fail closed on misconfiguration                                                                                  |
| `getFile` returns `{ file, diskPath }` with `diskPath = path.resolve(env.FILE_UPLOAD_PATH, record.storedName)`; the route streams via `res.sendFile(diskPath)`, and the service never touches `req`/`res`/sockets nor reads file content (`node:fs` is not imported)                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Stream the file from inside the service (accept `res`); use `path.join` instead of `path.resolve`                          | Keeps the service HTTP-agnostic and unit-testable, consistent with the sibling services that emit no I/O of their own; `path.resolve` yields a canonical absolute path for `res.sendFile`, and because `storedName` is the multer-generated filename (not user input) the resolved path is traversal-safe                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | The route layer must stream the returned `diskPath`; documented in the function JSDoc and the route contract                                                                                                    |
| `toFileDto` sets the DTO `url` to the relative API route `/api/files/${id}`, never the on-disk path                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Return the absolute disk path; return a fully-qualified URL including host                                                 | The web client composes the absolute URL as `${VITE_API_URL}${url}`, the API route streams the bytes behind that path, and a relative path leaks nothing about the server filesystem layout — the standard REST pattern already used by `messages.service.ts` for attachment DTOs                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | None — the client owns origin composition via `VITE_API_URL`                                                                                                                                                    |
| DEVIATION from this file's `depends_on_files` / agent-prompt metadata: error classes (`ForbiddenError`, `NotFoundError`) are imported from `../middleware/errors.js` and workspace symbols from the `@app/*` scope (not `./errors.js` / `@blitzy-slack/*`); `toFileDto` emits the full shared `FileAttachment` shape — all eight fields including `storedName` and a nullable `uploadedById` (`string \| null`) — correcting the agent-prompt draft mapper that omitted `storedName` | Import from a non-existent `services/errors.ts` under the `@blitzy-slack/*` scope; emit the draft DTO without `storedName` | No `services/errors.ts` exists — the committed classes live in `middleware/errors.ts` and every sibling service imports them from there; packages are scoped `@app/*` (see the package-scope rows above). The shared `FileAttachment` interface requires `storedName` and types `uploadedById` as `string \| null`, so the draft mapper omitting `storedName` would not typecheck; emitting all eight fields (matching the file mapping in `messages.service.ts`) is the only path that compiles under `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint --max-warnings 0` | The metadata names a path/scope and a DTO shape that differ from the real ones; this row makes the reconciliation explicit so the deviation is not treated as a defect (Explainability rule)                    |

## `packages/api` — Authentication service (`services/auth.service.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Password hashing imports `bcryptjs` (`import bcrypt from 'bcryptjs'`; `bcrypt.hash(pw, env.BCRYPT_ROUNDS)` / `bcrypt.compare(pw, hash)`) — this service is the FIRST API consumer of the hashing library                                                                                                                                                              | Native `bcrypt@5.1.x` (named by this file's `external_imports` metadata); `argon2`                                                                                                           | The CP2 dependency-hardening row already swapped the manifest to `bcryptjs` (native `bcrypt` pulled a high-severity `tar` advisory), and only `bcryptjs` is installed/symlinked for `@app/api`; it exposes the identical async `hash`/`compare` surface and ships its own ESM types, so it default-imports cleanly under `module: NodeNext`. Importing native `bcrypt` would fail to resolve and break `eslint --max-warnings 0` / `tsc` (Rule 3)                                                                                                                                                                                                      | `bcryptjs` is ~30% slower than native at the same cost factor; acceptable at PoC login volume and `BCRYPT_ROUNDS` is env-tunable                                                                                                              |
| JWTs are signed AND verified with HS256 only — `signToken` sets `algorithm: 'HS256'`, `verifyToken` pins `algorithms: ['HS256']` — and the payload carries only `sub` (user id) + `email`                                                                                                                                                                             | RS256 (asymmetric, rotation-friendly); accept the library's default algorithm set on verify; embed role/profile claims                                                                       | A single shared secret (`env.JWT_SECRET`, Zod `min(32)`) fits the single-process PoC and enables a stateless Socket.io handshake reusing the same verifier (AAP §0.8.4 JWT scope discipline); pinning the accepted algorithm blocks algorithm-confusion attacks (an `alg:none` or RS/HS-swap token is rejected); a minimal payload avoids leaking profile or secret data into the token                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A compromised `JWT_SECRET` is a total auth bypass (mitigated by the 32-char floor); HS256 cannot do per-consumer key rotation like RS256 — out of PoC scope                                                                                   |
| `registerUser` does NOT wrap `prisma.user.create` in try/catch, so a duplicate-email `PrismaClientKnownRequestError` (`P2002`) propagates UNWRAPPED; consequently the `Prisma` namespace (listed in this file's `internal_imports` metadata) is intentionally NOT imported, and the domain error classes come from `../middleware/errors.js` under the `@app/*` scope | Catch `P2002` and rethrow a `ConflictError`; import the `Prisma` namespace to reference the error type; import errors from a `./errors.js` / `services/errors.ts` under `@blitzy-slack/*`    | Rule 4 idempotency requires the seed flow to receive HTTP 409 on duplicate email; the error-handler middleware maps `instanceof Prisma.PrismaClientKnownRequestError && code === 'P2002'` → 409, so this service must let the raw error through and never inspects it here — importing the unused `Prisma` namespace would fail `no-unused-vars` (Rule 3). No `services/errors.ts` exists; the committed classes live in `middleware/errors.ts` and every sibling service imports them from there under `@app/*`                                                                                                                                       | The 409 contract depends on the error-handler recognising the Prisma error class (documented in that file); one metadata-listed symbol (`Prisma`) is intentionally omitted, reconciled by this row so it is not treated as a defect           |
| `loginUser` throws a single uniform `UnauthorizedError('Invalid email or password')` for BOTH unknown-email and wrong-password, and runs `bcrypt.compare` only when a user row exists (`user !== null && (await bcrypt.compare(...))`)                                                                                                                                | Distinct messages per failure cause; always compare against a precomputed dummy hash when the user is absent for fully constant-time behaviour                                               | A uniform message prevents account enumeration through differing API responses; gating the compare on user existence avoids a pointless hash when no account matches                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | The short-circuit leaks a sub-millisecond timing signal on the no-user path (no hash computed); acceptable for a PoC, and a dummy-hash compare can be layered later if timing-attack hardening is required                                    |
| `toUserDto` returns the shared `UserResponse` (= `Omit<User, 'passwordHash'>`) — the type backing `AuthResult.user` and `getMe` — built by an explicit field map with ISO-8601 date strings; the ONLY type assertion in the file is `env.JWT_EXPIRES_IN as SignOptions['expiresIn']`                                                                                  | Return the shared `User` named by this file's metadata (which INCLUDES `passwordHash`); destructure-and-rest to drop `passwordHash`; silence the `expiresIn` type mismatch with `@ts-ignore` | The shared `User` carries `passwordHash`, so returning it would both leak the hash and fail to typecheck against the explicit map; `UserResponse` is the documented self-view (see the shared-contracts section). An explicit map (vs `{ passwordHash: _, ...rest }`) avoids an unused-binding lint error and is auditable. jsonwebtoken types `expiresIn` as a narrow `StringValue \| number`, so a validated free-form duration string needs one asserted conversion — `@ts-ignore` is forbidden by Rule 3, and `jwt.verify`'s `string \| JwtPayload` result is narrowed via `typeof` checks (through a `Record<string, unknown>` view) with no cast | `UserResponse` must stay aligned with the Prisma model — it derives from `User` via `Omit`, so one change propagates; a malformed `JWT_EXPIRES_IN` would fail at sign time, surfaced immediately on first token issuance rather than silently |

## `packages/api` — Error-handler middleware (`middleware/error-handler.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt "EXACT content" / metadata: the `Prisma` namespace is imported from `@app/db` (not `@blitzy-slack/db`), the domain error classes from `./errors.js` (the sibling `middleware/errors.ts`, not `../services/errors.js`), and `jsonwebtoken` / `multer` are imported as DEFAULT exports (`import jwt from 'jsonwebtoken'`, `import multer from 'multer'`) with `jwt.TokenExpiredError`, `jwt.JsonWebTokenError`, and `multer.MulterError` accessed as members for the `instanceof` guards | Use the literal metadata: the `@blitzy-slack/*` scope, a `../services/errors.js` path, and ESM NAMED runtime imports `import { JsonWebTokenError, TokenExpiredError } from 'jsonwebtoken'` and `import { MulterError } from 'multer'`                           | No `@blitzy-slack/*` package and no `services/errors.ts` exist — packages are scoped `@app/*` (see the package-scope rows above) and the committed error classes live in `middleware/errors.ts`, from which every sibling service imports them. `jsonwebtoken` is a CommonJS module whose error classes are NOT lexer-detectable as ESM named exports under `module: NodeNext`; a native-Node-ESM probe proved `import { JsonWebTokenError } from 'jsonwebtoken'` throws "Named export not found" at runtime, which would crash both `node dist/index.js` and `tsx`. The default-import + member-access form (matching `auth.service.ts` and `upload.ts`) is the only shape that both compiles under `tsc` / `eslint --max-warnings 0` and runs; `multer` is converted likewise for native-ESM + jest-ESM robustness and convention parity, while `zod` (true ESM) and `@app/db` (workspace TS source) keep their named imports | The metadata names a scope, a path, and an import style that differ from the shipped ones; this row reconciles them so the deviation is not treated as a defect (Explainability rule). The `instanceof` semantics are unchanged — `jwt.TokenExpiredError`/`multer.MulterError` are the same runtime constructors the named imports would have referenced |
| `req.log` is typed by loading pino-http's `declare module "http"` augmentation through a bare type-only import `import type {} from 'pino-http'` placed first in the file                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | A side-effect `import 'pino-http'` (incurs a runtime module load); a local `declare module 'http'` block duplicating pino-http's own declaration; relying on the not-yet-created `request-logger.ts` to import pino-http and activate the augmentation globally | `resolveLogger` reads `req.log` (the per-request child logger that the pino-http request-logger attaches), which is typed only when pino-http's augmentation of `http.IncomingMessage` (the interface Express `Request` extends) is part of the program. No compiled file currently imports pino-http and `tsconfig` `types` is `["node", "jest"]`, so the augmentation is otherwise dormant and `req.log` would fail to typecheck. A type-only empty import activates it with ZERO runtime cost (fully elided by both `tsc` and `ts-jest`) and does not depend on `request-logger.ts` existing yet                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Reads like an unused import to a casual reader; the adjacent code comment states its purpose to prevent accidental removal. Becomes redundant — but harmless — once `request-logger.ts` imports pino-http for real                                                                                                                                       |
| `err instanceof jwt.TokenExpiredError` is checked BEFORE `err instanceof jwt.JsonWebTokenError`, mapping to `code: 'token_expired'` vs `code: 'token_invalid'` respectively (both HTTP 401)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | A single `JsonWebTokenError` branch that sub-inspects the message/name; the reverse check order                                                                                                                                                                 | `TokenExpiredError` extends `JsonWebTokenError`, and `instanceof` matches a subclass instance against the superclass test, so checking the superclass first would misclassify every expired token as merely "invalid" and lose the distinct `token_expired` signal the client needs to trigger a silent re-login                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | None                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| Unknown errors, non-`P2002`/`P2025` Prisma known errors, and `PrismaClientValidationError` all return a GENERIC 500 body (`InternalServerError` with a fixed message); the raw `err.message`, `err.stack`, and Prisma `err.meta` are logged at `error` but NEVER placed in the response, while routine 4xx client errors are logged at `warn`                                                                                                                                                                                  | Echo `err.message` / `err.stack` / `meta` in the response for easier client-side debugging; log every error at a single level                                                                                                                                   | Leaking internal text (e.g. `connect ECONNREFUSED`, SQL fragments, or the conflicting column names Prisma puts in `meta.target`) exposes infrastructure to attackers; operators still receive the full detail via the structured Pino line (Gate 10). The warn-for-4xx / error-for-5xx split lets dashboards alert on server bugs (5xx) without noise from expected client errors (bad inputs, expired tokens)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Less helpful client UX on unexpected 500s; mitigated by always-on structured logging keyed by `reqId`/`userId` for operator forensics                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| `MulterError` with `code === 'LIMIT_FILE_SIZE'` maps to 413 Payload Too Large; all other multer codes (`LIMIT_FIELD_COUNT`, `LIMIT_UNEXPECTED_FILE`, …) map to 400 Bad Request                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Map every `MulterError` to 500; map all multer errors (including the size cap) to 400                                                                                                                                                                           | The size cap is the enforcement point for `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB` and earns the specific, semantically-correct 413; the remaining multer errors are client multipart-input mistakes (4xx), not server faults (5xx)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | A multer error that actually reflects a server misconfiguration is surfaced as a 400; mitigated by the `warn` log line carrying the real multer `code`                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| The handler is the SINGLE centralized error formatter (`app.use(errorHandler)` mounted last); inline 5xx payloads use `satisfies ErrorPayload` rather than an `as` cast; `resolveLogger` returns `req.log ?? appLogger`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Per-route try/catch with hand-written JSON; an `as ErrorPayload` cast; always use the bare logger singleton, or hard-require `req.log` to be present                                                                                                            | One handler yields a uniform JSON shape and removes per-route duplication (AAP §0.8.4); Express 5 forwards both sync throws and async rejections to it automatically. `satisfies` validates each literal against the `ErrorPayload` contract without widening the type or suppressing errors (Rule 3-safe, unlike `as`). Nullish-coalescing the logger keeps the handler resilient to unusual middleware ordering (a low-level failure before the request-logger ran) without crashing on `undefined.error`, and `??` (not `                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | `) treats only nullish values as absent so a validly-disabled logger is still used | All errors funnel through one hot function; mitigated by the trivial `instanceof` type guards that carry no allocation or I/O |

## `packages/api` — Direct-messages service (`services/dms.service.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                | What alternatives existed                                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What risks it carries                                                                                                 |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The public export is `startDm(userId, targetUserId)`; it finds an existing 1:1 DM for the unordered pair or creates one (symmetric idempotency) | Name it `createOrFindDm` (the CP2 draft the CP3 review flagged); always create a new DM row per call | CP3/AAP name the export `startDm`. Resolving the participant pair order-independently and returning the existing DM on repeat calls keeps a single canonical DM per pair, matching the `DMParticipant` unique constraint | A future group-DM feature would need a different participant-set lookup; single-pair only is the documented PoC scope |
| `listDms` is bounded with `take: MAX_PAGE_SIZE` (100)                                                                                           | Return every DM unpaginated (the CP2 behaviour the CP3 review flagged as an unbounded list)          | CP3's performance checklist forbids unbounded list methods; capping at `MAX_PAGE_SIZE` bounds the worst-case payload at PoC scale                                                                                        | A user with more than 100 DMs sees only the first page; a cursor can be layered in later without changing the DTO     |
| Starting a DM with one's own id is rejected (`ValidationError`); the request body field is `targetUserId` (the shared `startDmSchema`)          | Allow self-DMs; accept a `participantUserId` field                                                   | A self-DM has no second participant; the shared `startDmSchema` is the single source of truth for the field name (`targetUserId`), which the e2e specs were corrected to use                                             | None of note; self-DM is out of scope per AAP §0.7.2                                                                  |

## `packages/api` — Search service (`services/search.service.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                             | What alternatives existed                                              | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                           | What risks it carries                                                                                               |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Search logs `{ userId, queryLength: query.length, latencyMs, count }` — the raw query text `q` is NEVER logged                                               | Log the full `query` string for debugging; log nothing                 | CP3 privacy requirement: `q` may contain sensitive content, so only its length (and non-reversible metadata) is logged while preserving Gate 10 observability (latency, result count)              | Operators cannot see the exact query in logs; acceptable, and length + count still support latency/aboutness triage |
| Full-text search uses parameterized `prisma.$queryRaw` (`websearch_to_tsquery`) with ACL filtering to the caller's channel memberships and DM participations | String-concatenated SQL / `$queryRawUnsafe`; an external search engine | Parameterized bindings prevent SQL injection (special characters never break out of the query), and ACL filtering in the service guarantees a user only sees hits from channels/DMs they belong to | Postgres FTS ranking is coarser than a dedicated engine; sufficient for the PoC Gate 9 < 2 s budget                 |

## `packages/shared` — Socket.io event contract (`types/socket-events.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                      | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                 |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `ClientToServerEvents` / `ServerToClientEvents` use COMPUTED property keys from the `constants/events.ts` string constants (e.g. `[MESSAGE_SEND]`, `[CHANNEL_JOIN]`) — not duplicated string literals | Keep duplicated string-literal keys (`'message:send'`, the CP2 form the CP3 review flagged) that happen to match by inspection | CP3 / Rule 2 require a single source of truth for event names; computed keys make `constants/events.ts` authoritative so a renamed event cannot silently drift between the constants and the interfaces | A typo in a constant now fails typecheck loudly (intended); the interfaces are slightly less readable than inline literals — an acceptable trade for drift prevention |

## CP3 review remediation — service contracts, real-time adapter, operations & UI tokens

Consolidated record of the decisions made while resolving the Checkpoint-3 review. Per-file rows above carry the canonical decision; these rows capture the cross-cutting remediation rationale (Explainability rule, AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                   | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                              |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| All six service public exports were ALIGNED to the AAP/checkpoint names — `registerUser`/`loginUser`/`getMe` (auth), `listChannelMessages` (channels), `createMessage`/`listThreadReplies` (messages), `startDm` (dms), `createFile` (files); behaviour unchanged                                                             | Retain the CP2 drift names (`register`/`login`/`getCurrentUser`/`listMessages`/`sendMessage`/`getReplies`/`createOrFindDm`/`saveUploadedFile`) or add compatibility aliases | The CP3 review flagged the export-name drift as a CP4 integration risk (route/socket code is written to the AAP names). There are zero existing consumers, so a clean rename (not aliases) is the simplest correct fix and avoids a dual-name surface                                         | None — verified no consumers exist via repo-wide grep; `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint --max-warnings 0` stay green                                                                     |
| `messages.createMessage` (and the thread/reaction read+mutate paths) now require `ChannelMember` membership for ALL channels — `assertChannelAccess` no longer treats public channels as open                                                                                                                                 | Keep the CP2 behaviour allowing any authenticated user to post/read/react in public channels without joining                                                                | CP3 CRITICAL security finding: posting/reacting in a public channel before joining is an authorization gap. Requiring membership uniformly closes it; discovery/listing remains separate                                                                                                      | A user must `joinChannel` before posting in a public channel; this matches the Slack model and the AAP membership contract                                                         |
| `channels.joinChannel` is idempotent — a duplicate-membership `P2002` is caught and the already-joined channel DTO is returned (not a 409)                                                                                                                                                                                    | Let `P2002` propagate as a 409 conflict (the CP2 behaviour)                                                                                                                 | CP3 requires duplicate joins to be idempotent; returning the existing channel makes repeated joins safe for the client                                                                                                                                                                        | Constructs and discards one Prisma error on the duplicate path; negligible                                                                                                         |
| `channels.listChannels` and `dms.listDms` are bounded with `take: MAX_PAGE_SIZE` (100)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Return unbounded lists (CP2 behaviour)                                                                                                                                      | CP3 performance checklist forbids unbounded list methods; a cap bounds worst-case payloads at PoC scale                                                                                                                                                                                       | First-page only beyond 100 rows; cursoring can be added later                                                                                                                      |
| `auth.service` logs no PII — `email` was removed from the register-success and failed-login log lines (`userId` and safe event metadata only)                                                                                                                                                                                 | Keep logging `email` for traceability                                                                                                                                       | CP3 privacy finding forbids logging PII/credential-adjacent identifiers; `userId` is sufficient for correlation                                                                                                                                                                               | Slightly less human-readable logs; `userId` joins to the user record when needed                                                                                                   |
| `config/redis.ts` adds an explicit `retryStrategy(times) => min(times * 200ms, 5000ms)` backoff on `baseOptions`                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Rely on ioredis's built-in reconnect with no documented backoff                                                                                                             | CP3 requires an explicit retry/reconnect strategy; linear-then-clamped backoff avoids hammering a downed Redis while staying responsive on recovery                                                                                                                                           | A long outage settles at a 5 s reconnect cadence; tunable via `RETRY_BACKOFF_STEP_MS`/`RETRY_BACKOFF_MAX_MS`                                                                       |
| `playwright.config.ts` adds `snapshotPathTemplate: '{testFileDir}/__screenshots__/{arg}{ext}'`; `screenshot-fidelity.spec.ts` seeds those baselines by copying the authoritative `/screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 {0,1,8,29,500}.png` assets, with the viewport pinned to the reference 1920×1320 and volatile regions masked | Compare against self-generated first-run Playwright snapshots (the CP2 behaviour the CP3 review flagged); keep per-project/per-platform baseline suffixes                   | CP3 / Rule 1 / Gate 8 require visual fidelity against the PROVIDED Slack references, not arbitrary self-captures. Dropping the project/platform suffix lets every engine compare against the one authoritative baseline                                                                       | Baselines are real Slack captures, so a from-scratch clone will differ until CP4+ pages exist; the suite documents the masking/cropping and is expected to fail until the UI lands |
| ENVIRONMENT EXCEPTION: on the build host (Ubuntu 25.10) the `webkit` Playwright project cannot launch — Playwright's WebKit build links ICU 74 while the host ships libicu76                                                                                                                                                  | Omit WebKit from config to keep this host green (rejected — violates the CP3 "three projects" requirement)                                                                  | The config correctly DEFINES webkit (portable contract); the launch failure is a host limitation, not a config defect. On the official `mcr.microsoft.com/playwright` image or a supported OS all three engines run                                                                           | `make test-e2e` runs WebKit red on this host; CI must use a supported image, or scope to chromium/firefox locally                                                                  |
| UI design-token compliance: added `--color-overlay` to the `@theme` block and switched `dialog`/`sheet` overlays from `bg-black/50` to `bg-overlay`; `button`/`badge` destructive variants from `text-white` to `text-destructive-foreground`; `tabs` from arbitrary `p-[3px]` to the `p-0.5` scale value                     | Keep the hardcoded hex/arbitrary values (CP2 primitives)                                                                                                                    | CP3 / Rule 1 token discipline: hardcoded colours and off-scale spacing bypass the design system. Semantic tokens keep the aubergine theme overridable in one place                                                                                                                            | A semantic overlay token did not previously exist; `--color-overlay: oklch(0 0 0 / 0.5)` reproduces the prior 50%-black visual exactly                                             |
| Added the shadcn `Sonner` primitive at `components/ui/sonner.tsx` (Vite-adapted: no `next-themes`, `theme="light"`, Sonner CSS vars mapped to project tokens); `<Toaster />` mounting is deferred to the CP4 app shell                                                                                                        | Pull in `next-themes` to match the upstream shadcn snippet; defer the whole primitive to CP4                                                                                | CP3 flagged the missing Sonner primitive (the file-upload e2e asserts `[data-sonner-toast]` and the `sonner` dependency is installed). This Vite app has no `next-themes`, so a light-themed wrapper is the correct adaptation; the shell that renders `<Toaster />` does not exist until CP4 | The primitive is present but not yet mounted, so toasts will not render until CP4 wires `<Toaster />`; the component itself typechecks and lints clean                             |
| `Makefile`: `install` uses `pnpm install --frozen-lockfile`; `clean` runs `docker compose down -v` (removing named volumes) and no longer depends on `down`; `local` runs the backgrounded API + health-wait + seed + foreground web in ONE shell guarded by `trap '... kill $API_PID' EXIT INT TERM`                         | Keep `pnpm install` (non-frozen), `clean` depending on `down` (no `-v`), and the multi-line `local` that leaves an orphan API/pid file on failure                           | CP3 / Rule 5: a committed lockfile demands frozen installs for reproducibility; `clean` must remove Docker volumes; and `local` must terminate API + web together. The single-shell trap kills exactly the spawned API pid (safe spawn-and-kill-own-pid pattern)                              | A long Redis/Postgres reset now requires `make up` again after `clean`; intended                                                                                                   |
| E2E specs: all six suites wrap actions/assertions in `test.step` narrative blocks; `dms.spec.ts` uses `targetUserId` (matching `startDmSchema`); `messaging.spec.ts` keeps `getByRole`/`getByTestId` selectors with `data-testid` adoption DEFERRED                                                                           | Add speculative `data-testid` selectors now; keep `participantUserId`; skip `test.step`                                                                                     | CP3 test-standards finding requires `test.step` coverage and a schema-aligned DM payload. `data-testid` adoption is explicitly "once components/pages exist" — CP4 pages do not exist yet, so inventing IDs would be guesswork; `getByRole` is the robust interim strategy                    | `data-testid` hardening lands in CP4 when pages/components are authored; specs remain pre-staged until then                                                                        |

## `packages/web` — Search bar (`src/components/search/SearchBar.tsx`)

Decisions for the top-bar `SearchBar` navigator — a debounced search field that pushes the user to `/app/search?q=<encoded query>`. It navigates only; the actual request and results rendering live in the sibling `SearchResultsList`/`SearchResults` surface (AAP §0.6.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Debounce the search input at 300 ms before navigating (inline `setTimeout`/`clearTimeout` in a `React.useEffect`), tunable via the `debounceMs` prop                                            | (a) 200 ms (snappier, more navigations); (b) 500 ms (fewer navigations, laggier); (c) a `use-debounce` / `lodash.debounce` dependency or a shared `useDebounce` hook                                                                                                                                                                      | 300 ms is the established UX sweet spot — responsive enough to feel instant after a short pause, yet slow enough to coalesce rapid typing into a single navigation; an inline `setTimeout` keeps the component zero-dependency because no `useDebounce` hook exists under `@/hooks`                                                                                           | May feel slow for very fast typists or on fast networks; mitigated by the `debounceMs` override prop                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Navigate with `useNavigate` from `react-router` (v7) to `/app/search?q=${encodeURIComponent(query)}`, using the default push (not `replace`)                                                    | (a) a `<Link>` element with a click handler; (b) `window.location.assign`; (c) `useNavigate` with `{ replace: true }`                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | `useNavigate` integrates with React Router's history stack so browser back/forward work naturally, and a default push (not replace) lets the user return to the page they searched from; React Router v7 consolidates `react-router-dom`, so the hook is imported from `react-router`                                                                                         | None significant — standard React Router v7 pattern                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| Manage the field with `react-hook-form` + `zodResolver(searchQuerySchema)` (uncontrolled `register('q')`, `mode: 'onChange'`, value read via `watch('q')`) rather than `useState`               | (a) plain `useState` + manual validation; (b) a controlled input with imperative validation; (c) `react-hook-form` with the Zod resolver                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Reuses the shared `searchQuerySchema` (trim, min 1, max 200) the API also enforces, so client and server validate identically with no duplicated rules (AAP §0.8.4); `watch('q')` is already reactive and drives the debounced navigation effect                                                                                                                              | Adds `react-hook-form` to this component's surface, but it is already a dependency of the Register/Login/CreateChannel forms, so the cost is amortized                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Defer the Ctrl+K / Cmd+K `Command` palette — `SearchBar` ships as the debounced input only                                                                                                      | (a) implement it now with the shadcn `CommandDialog`; (b) implement it as a separate component mounted in the app shell; (c) defer entirely                                                                                                                                                                                               | AAP §0.6.3 mandates only the debounced input that fires `GET /api/search?q=`; the palette is a separate enhancement, so keeping `SearchBar` focused reduces scope creep and avoids forcing the `cmdk` runtime path here unless another feature needs it                                                                                                                       | Future users may expect Ctrl+K — tracked as a backlog enhancement; re-evaluate if usability testing surfaces friction                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt "exact imports": the shared schema is imported from `@app/shared/schemas/message`, not the prompt's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/schemas/message` | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the agent prompt printed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and existing web imports such as `@app/shared/types/user` all confirm it; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc`/Vite (Rule 3). Mirrors the `@app/*` precedent already recorded for `@app/db` and `@app/web` | None functional — this aligns the import with the real workspace name; if the monorepo is ever rescoped, every `@app/*` specifier must change together                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Prefix the imperative `navigate(...)` calls with the `void` operator and bind the form as `onSubmit={(event) => void onSubmit(event)}` (where `onSubmit = form.handleSubmit(...)`)              | (a) leave the bare `navigate(...)` calls and pass `form.handleSubmit(...)` straight to `onSubmit`, exactly as this file's agent-prompt canonical reference printed; (b) disable `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises` / `no-misused-promises` for this file or the whole package; (c) `await` the navigations inside `async` handlers | React Router v7's `navigate` returns `void                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Promise<void>`and`form.handleSubmit(cb)`returns a Promise-returning handler, so the canonical reference tripped`no-floating-promises`(the two`navigate`calls) and`no-misused-promises`(the Promise-returning handler bound to React's void`onSubmit`) under the project's type-checked ESLint config. The `void`operator is typescript-eslint's prescribed, zero-runtime-cost mitigation; it satisfies`--max-warnings 0`(Rule 3) without the forbidden`@ts-ignore`/`@ts-expect-error` and without weakening the shared lint rules for the rest of the module | A rejected navigation promise is swallowed silently, but React Router navigation does not reject in practice; the explicit `void` documents the intentional fire-and-forget |

## `packages/web` — Search result item (`src/components/search/SearchResultItem.tsx`)

Decisions for the per-row search-result renderer — a discriminated-union component (`message` \| `channel` \| `file`) consumed by the sibling `SearchResultsList` surface (AAP §0.6.3). It owns the row layout, the query-highlighted excerpt, and the click-navigation target for each result kind.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                         | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt "exact imports": the shared DTOs are imported from `@app/shared/types/channel` and `@app/shared/types/message`, not the prompt's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/...` | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the agent prompt printed                                                                                                        | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and the sibling `SearchBar.tsx` import of `@app/shared/schemas/message` all confirm it; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc`/Vite (Rule 3). Mirrors the `@app/*` precedent already recorded for `SearchBar`, `@app/db`, and `@app/web` | None functional — this aligns the import with the real workspace name; a future monorepo rescope must change every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                                 |
| Query-match highlighting uses the native semantic `<mark>` element styled with `bg-yellow-200/70 text-foreground rounded-sm px-0.5`, computed by a regex-free `indexOf`/`toLowerCase` matcher                    | (a) a `<span>` with an inline `backgroundColor` style; (b) a third-party highlighter such as `react-highlight-words`; (c) a global-flag `RegExp` driving `String.prototype.split` | `<mark>` is semantic HTML announced by assistive technology, and Tailwind utilities keep the highlight on the design-token system with zero new dependencies. The regex-free matcher sidesteps the stateful `RegExp.lastIndex` pitfall and removes the need to escape regex metacharacters in user-supplied queries                                                                                       | Case-insensitivity relies on `String.prototype.toLowerCase`, which is locale-agnostic; some non-English casing pairs (e.g., German ß / ẞ) may not highlight perfectly — acceptable for the PoC's predominantly English content |
| The message-result author `Avatar` overrides the primitive default (`size-8 rounded-full`) with `size-10 rounded-md` — slightly larger and squared                                                               | (a) keep the primitive default `size-8 rounded-full`; (b) `size-12 rounded-lg` (larger, more rounded)                                                                             | Slack's web client renders squared, rounded avatars in dense list contexts such as search results and mentions; `size-10` gives the avatar the correct visual weight as the leading element of a result row (Rule 1, ref `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 100.png`)                                                                                                                                        | Departs from the `Avatar` primitive default, so a future global avatar restyle will not auto-propagate to this row                                                                                                             |
| Message results render generic context labels — "in a channel" / "in a direct message" — instead of the specific channel or DM name                                                                              | (a) join channel/DM names into the search response server-side; (b) fetch each result's channel/DM detail on the client (N+1 requests)                                            | The `GET /api/search?q=` contract returns `MessageWithAuthor[]` carrying only `channelId`/`dmId` (no joined names); adding server-side joins or client N+1 lookups is out of PoC scope and risks the `<2s` search budget (Gate 9). Generic labels are honest about the data actually available                                                                                                            | Reduces at-a-glance usefulness — the user must click through to learn which channel a hit came from; tracked as a backlog enhancement                                                                                          |
| File-result icons are selected by MIME prefix: `image/*` → `ImageIcon`, `text/*` + `application/pdf` + `application/json` → `FileText`, everything else → `FileIcon` (lucide `File`)                             | (a) a single generic file icon for every type; (b) an exhaustive one-icon-per-MIME-type map                                                                                       | A small set of category icons stays visually consistent and covers the overwhelming majority of uploads; the 10 MB cap (AAP §0.1.1) limits realistic file diversity, so a per-type map would be over-engineering                                                                                                                                                                                          | Some categories (e.g., `audio/*`, archives) fall back to the generic icon; trivially extendable later without breaking changes                                                                                                 |

## `packages/web` — Channel list item (`src/components/channels/ChannelListItem.tsx`)

Decisions for the single sidebar channel-row component — a leaf consumed by the downstream `ChannelList` surface (AAP §0.5.2, §0.5.4). It renders the `#` / `Lock` prefix, the channel name with overflow truncation, an optional unread `Badge`, and the active-route highlight; navigation and active-state derive from the React Router `:channelId` param. The light-lavender active-pill tokens it consumes (`--color-sidebar-accent` / `--color-sidebar-accent-foreground`) are defined and documented in the _Theme tokens_ section above.
