| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                         | What alternatives existed                                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                              |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Public-channel prefix rendered as a literal text `#` glyph in an `aria-hidden` `<span>`; the lucide `Hash` icon is deliberately not imported at all                                      | A lucide `<Hash />` icon, for visual parity with the private-channel `<Lock />`                      | Slack's web UI renders the prefix as a typographic `#` character, not an icon (Rule 1, ref `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 29.png` and `100.png`); a text glyph preserves the exact character weight and metrics the screenshots show, and the file-spec mandates text                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Visual asymmetry with the `Lock` icon (text vs icon) on private rows; accepted because it mirrors Slack exactly                                                    |
| Navigation via `useNavigate` with the call discarded as `void navigate(...)`, not an `<a>` / `<Link asChild>` anchor                                                                     | `<Link to={...} asChild>` wrapping the `Item`; a bare `<a href>`                                     | The file-spec mandates `useNavigate`, and programmatic navigation pairs symmetrically with the keyboard handler; react-router 7's `NavigateFunction` returns `void \| Promise<void>`, so a bare call trips `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises` (error, Rule 3) and the `void` operator discards the optional promise (the rule's `ignoreVoid` default accepts it)                                                                                                                                                          | Loses the native anchor's right-click "open in new tab" and middle-click affordances; acceptable for an in-app sidebar control                                     |
| The `Item` root is made an ARIA button (`role="button"`, `tabIndex={0}`, `onKeyDown` activating on `Enter` / `Space` with `preventDefault` on Space), not wrapped in a native `<button>` | Wrap `Item` in a real `<button>`; rely on a `<Link>` for semantics                                   | The shadcn `Item` primitive renders a `<div>`; nesting or wrapping it in an interactive `<button>` / `<a>` produces invalid or duplicated interactive nesting. The WAI-ARIA button pattern is the canonical way to make a non-button element keyboard-operable and satisfies `jsx-a11y/click-events-have-key-events` and `no-noninteractive-element-interactions`                                                                                                                                                                | Keyboard semantics a native button provides for free must be hand-maintained; the implemented `Enter` / `Space` handler covers the expected activation keys        |
| Props typed as the narrow `ChannelSummary` (`id`, `name`, `isPrivate`, optional `unreadCount`), not the wider `ChannelWithMembers`                                                       | Accept the full `ChannelWithMembers` shape; a local `Pick<...>`                                      | The row renders only the prefix, name, and unread count, so it needs no members or memberCount; the narrow contract follows least-privilege and `@app/shared/types/channel` already exports exactly this shape                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | If a future requirement adds a member-avatar stack to the row, the props must be widened; documented as a known extension point                                    |
| The unread-count `Badge` uses `variant="default"` (the `bg-primary` Slack-blue token), not `variant="destructive"` (red)                                                                 | `variant="destructive"` to mirror Slack's red unread pill; `variant="secondary"`                     | `default` keeps the unread indicator on the project's primary accent and reserves the destructive/red treatment for genuinely destructive affordances per shadcn convention; the blue also matches the `--color-primary` link accent established for the sidebar                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Deviates from Slack's red unread badge; flagged as a revisitable styling choice — a future swap to `destructive` or a bespoke red token is a one-line change       |
| Both the `#` span and the `<Lock />` icon carry `aria-hidden="true"`                                                                                                                     | Expose them to the accessibility tree; add an `sr-only` "private channel" label                      | The channel name plus `aria-current="page"` on the active row convey identity to assistive tech; the prefix is decorative, and the public/private distinction is surfaced functionally in the channel header, keeping the dense sidebar row's announcement concise ("design-project, button")                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | A screen-reader user is not told "private" at the row level; accepted for the PoC and reversible by adding an `sr-only` label                                      |
| `ItemContent` is given `min-w-0 gap-0`                                                                                                                                                   | Leave the primitive defaults (`flex flex-col gap-1`, `min-width: auto`)                              | No `ItemDescription` is rendered (the description lives in the channel header), so `gap-0` collapses the unused gap for a compact row; `min-w-0` overrides the flex item's default `min-width: auto` so the title can shrink below its content width and truncate                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | None material; both are layout-only utilities scoped to this row                                                                                                   |
| `ItemTitle` is given `block w-full truncate`, not the file-spec's literal `truncate` alone                                                                                               | `truncate` alone (as the prompt printed); a manual `overflow-hidden text-ellipsis whitespace-nowrap` | The `ItemTitle` primitive's base is `flex w-fit`, and `text-overflow: ellipsis` does not render on a flex / content-sized box, so the bare `truncate` silently failed and long names wrapped to two lines (found in Phase 4); `block` restores a block formatting context where `truncate` works and `w-full` overrides `w-fit` so the title fills and is bounded by the shrunk `ItemContent`; verified in-browser that a 40-char name clips with an ellipsis on a single 30 px row                                              | Overrides two primitive base utilities; if the `ItemTitle` primitive later changes its base display these overrides must be re-checked                             |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's `variant="icon"`: `ItemMedia` uses `variant="default"`                                                                                                    | The prompt's literal `variant="icon"`                                                                | The `icon` variant renders a `size-8 border rounded-sm bg-muted` box — a 32 px bordered muted square — but screenshots 29/100 show the prefix as a borderless inline glyph with no box (Rule 1); `variant="default"` is frameless and matches, and the file-spec's own stated intent ("renders compactly without an image frame", "matches screenshot 29") agrees with the screenshot over the literal token. `<Lock />` is sized explicitly with `size-4` since the frameless variant does not impose the icon-box child sizing | Departs from the literal prompt token; mitigated because the rendered result matches the authoritative screenshot, which Rule 1 ranks above a prompt example value |
| `ItemMedia` is muted with `opacity-70`, not a fixed colour class (`text-sidebar-foreground/70`)                                                                                          | The fixed `text-sidebar-foreground/70` the prompt printed; no muting                                 | A fixed `text-sidebar-foreground/70` (light lavender) rendered the prefix INVISIBLE on the active row's light pill (light-on-light), found in Phase 4; `opacity-70` lets the glyph inherit the `Item`'s current text colour — light when inactive on the dark aubergine, dark when active on the light pill — so it stays legible in both states while still reading as secondary to the channel name                                                                                                                            | `opacity` also fades any future non-text child of `ItemMedia`; acceptable as the slot holds only the single decorative glyph or icon                               |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/types/channel`: `ChannelSummary` is imported from `@app/shared/types/channel`                                          | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the prompt printed                                 | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` (its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and sibling components' `@app/shared/...` imports all confirm it); `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc` / Vite (Rule 3). Consistent with the `@app/*` precedent already recorded for `SearchBar`, `SearchResultItem`, `@app/db`, and `@app/web`                                                                                                                | None functional; a future monorepo rescope must change every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                           |
| The active row carries an empty `data-active=""` attribute alongside the `aria-current="page"` / class highlight                                                                         | Pure class-based active state with no data attribute                                                 | Provides a stable, semantics-free hook for Playwright E2E and the screenshot-fidelity suite (AAP Gate 8) to select or assert the active row without coupling to Tailwind class names; `aria-current` carries the accessible meaning while `data-active` carries the test hook                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | None; an empty data attribute has no rendered effect                                                                                                               |
| The conditional `Badge` uses an explicit `typeof channel.unreadCount === 'number' && channel.unreadCount > 0 ? <Badge /> : null` ternary                                                 | `channel.unreadCount && <Badge />`; `!!channel.unreadCount && ...`                                   | `unreadCount` is `number \| undefined`; a bare `&&` trips `@typescript-eslint/strict-boolean-expressions` and risks rendering a literal `0`. The `typeof === 'number'` guard plus `> 0` makes the condition explicit and the `: null` else-branch unambiguous (Rule 3)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | None                                                                                                                                                               |

## `packages/web` — Channel list hook (`src/hooks/useChannels.ts`)

Decisions for the single canonical reader of the authenticated user's channel list — a TanStack Query wrapper around `apiClient.get('/api/channels')` that exposes the normalized `UseChannelsResult` shape (AAP §0.1.1 "list channels", §0.6.2 "TanStack Query caches server data"). It is the read side only; mutation hooks and socket handlers own cache invalidation.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | What alternatives existed                                                                                 | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| The query cache key is the flat literal `['channels']` — no `userId` segment                                                                                                                                                                        | A user-scoped `['channels', userId]`; a nested `['user', userId, 'channels']` key                         | The channel list is per-authenticated-session and the JWT already scopes the `GET /api/channels` response to the caller, so the key needs no user discriminator; the flat key is also the exact value every mutation hook and socket handler invalidates via `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['channels'] })`, keeping the read and write sides referencing one literal (folder-spec mandate)                                                                                | A second user signing in on the same browser tab could momentarily see the prior user's cached channels until a refetch; mitigated by clearing the TanStack cache in `useAuth.logout()` (downstream hook) and by the `enabled` gate disabling the query while logged out |
| The query is auth-gated with `enabled: token !== null`, reading the token via the selector `useAuthStore((s) => s.token)`                                                                                                                           | Always-enabled with a conditional or throwing `queryFn`; the truthiness coercion `enabled: !!token`       | Gating on `enabled` means TanStack Query never fires `GET /api/channels` for a logged-out caller, who instead receives `channels: []` and `isLoading: false` with no flashing error state; the explicit `token !== null` (not `!!token`) satisfies `@typescript-eslint/strict-boolean-expressions` (Rule 3), and the selector form re-renders the hook only on token changes. On login the token flips from null to a value and TanStack auto-refetches on enable                       | None material — the brief enable transition during login is handled by TanStack's auto-refetch-on-enable                                                                                                                                                                 |
| A normalized `UseChannelsResult` (`{ channels, isLoading, isFetching, error, refetch }`) is returned instead of the raw `UseQueryResult`; `channels` defaults to `[]` when `data` is `undefined`, and `refetch` is reduced to `() => Promise<void>` | Pass through TanStack's full result (`data`/`isPending`/`isError`/…) directly; return `data` un-defaulted | A small, intention-revealing surface lets consumers (`ChannelList`, `Workspace`, `SearchResults`) read five fields without learning TanStack's result vocabulary, makes `query.data ?? []` a single "never `undefined`" guarantee, and reducing `refetch` to `Promise<void>` frees callers from the `QueryObserverResult` generic; the `void`-discarded `await query.refetch()` inside the async wrapper also satisfies `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises` (Rule 3)              | A consumer needing an extra field (e.g. `isStale`, `dataUpdatedAt`) must extend `UseChannelsResult`; a deliberate, low-cost interface-extension point                                                                                                                    |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt "exact imports": `ChannelWithMembers` is imported from `@app/shared/types/channel`, not the prompt's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/types/channel`                                                      | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the agent prompt printed                                | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and sibling web imports such as `SearchResultItem.tsx` / `ChannelListItem.tsx` (`@app/shared/types/channel`) all confirm it; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc` / Vite (Rule 3). Mirrors the `@app/*` precedent already recorded for `SearchBar`, `SearchResultItem`, `ChannelListItem`, `@app/db`, and `@app/web` | None functional — this aligns the import with the real workspace name; a future monorepo rescope must change every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                                                                           |

## `packages/api` — Socket.io handshake auth middleware (`middleware/socket-auth.ts`)

Decisions for the Socket.io connection-handshake JWT middleware — the WebSocket analogue of the HTTP `requireAuth` (`middleware/auth.ts`). Mounted once via `io.use(socketAuth)` in `sockets/index.ts` before any connection handlers, it verifies the token presented at handshake time and attaches the authenticated identity to `socket.data` (AAP Rule 2 — real-time auth; §0.8.4 — single-verifier discipline).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                  | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `socketAuth` delegates all JWT verification to `verifyToken` from `services/auth.service.ts`; the file contains no `jwt.verify`, secret access, or manual decode of its own                                                                                                                                                         | Re-implement `jwt.verify` locally in the middleware; extract a shared `verifyJwt` helper into a new `middleware/jwt.ts`                                                    | AAP §0.8.4 mandates one verifier shared by HTTP and WS so algorithm pinning, claim schema, and error semantics never drift; `auth.service.ts` is the established canonical location and the sibling `auth.ts` (HTTP `requireAuth`) already delegates there                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Introduces a middleware→service dependency; accepted because the service layer is the only place permitted to own JWT logic and the edge is one-directional (no cycle)                                                                                                                                  |
| Both rejection paths call `next(new Error('Unauthorized'))` — a generic `Error` with a constant message — never the service-layer `UnauthorizedError`                                                                                                                                                                               | Pass the caught `UnauthorizedError` straight through to `next`; pass a plain object carrying `{ statusCode: 401 }`                                                         | Socket.io ignores HTTP metadata such as `statusCode` and serializes only `err.message` to the client over `connect_error`; a constant `'Unauthorized'` gives a uniform client contract and leaks no server-side error class, stack, or specific cause (expired vs malformed vs bad signature)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | The client cannot distinguish failure causes; mitigated by a generic "Authentication failed" client UX while the server-side `warn` log retains the real `err.name`/`err.message` for forensics                                                                                                         |
| The token is read from `socket.handshake.auth.token` first, falling back to `socket.handshake.query.token`                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Support only the modern `handshake.auth` payload; support only the query string                                                                                            | Socket.io 4.x clients send the token in the `auth` handshake payload, but long-polling fallbacks and proxies that strip that payload can carry it only on the query string; verification is identical either way, so accepting both maximizes transport compatibility without weakening security                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Query strings can surface in intermediary/proxy access logs (a token-leak surface); mitigated by an HTTPS-only deployment policy and short JWT lifetimes                                                                                                                                                |
| Rejections (missing/invalid token) log at `warn`; successful handshakes log at `debug`; both lines carry structured fields (`socketId`, `remoteAddress` on rejections, `userId` on success) and never the raw token or full stack                                                                                                   | All lines at `info`; all at `debug`; rejections at `error`                                                                                                                 | Auth rejections are routine signal (expired tokens, tab refreshes) — worth a dashboard but not error-grade; successful handshakes are extremely frequent (every reconnect) and would flood `info` in production, so `debug` keeps them out of default production logs yet inspectable in development (Gate 10 structured logging)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | A brute-force spike sits at `warn` and may not page on-call; mitigated by SIEM aggregation thresholds rather than per-line severity                                                                                                                                                                     |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's `import type { ExtendedError } from 'socket.io/dist/namespace.js'`: `Socket`, `ExtendedError`, and `DefaultEventsMap` are imported (type-only) from the `socket.io` package root                                                                                                                     | The literal deep-path specifier the prompt printed; suppressing the resolution error with `@ts-expect-error` (forbidden by Rule 3)                                         | socket.io 4.8.3 ships an `exports` map exposing only `.` and `./package.json`, so under `moduleResolution: NodeNext` the deep path `socket.io/dist/namespace.js` is non-resolvable and fails `tsc` with TS2307 (verified empirically); `ExtendedError` and `DefaultEventsMap` are re-exported from the package root (`index.d.ts`), the file-spec itself sanctions this root-import fallback, and the external-imports contract names `socket.io` as the source                                                                                                                                                                                                                | None functional — the root re-export is part of socket.io's public type surface; a future major that dropped it would require revisiting (low likelihood within the 4.x line)                                                                                                                           |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's `declare module 'socket.io' { interface SocketData { … } }` augmentation: typed per-connection data is provided by a file-local `interface SocketData` bound as the fourth type argument of `Socket<DefaultEventsMap, DefaultEventsMap, DefaultEventsMap, SocketData>` (the `HandshakeSocket` alias) | The literal module-augmentation block the prompt printed; import the shared `SocketData` from `@app/shared/types/socket-events` (outside this file's dependency whitelist) | In socket.io 4.x `SocketData` is the `Socket` class's fourth generic parameter (default `any`), NOT a module-level interface, so the augmentation is inert — it adds an unrelated interface and leaves `socket.data` typed `any`, tripping `@typescript-eslint/no-unsafe-*` and failing Rule 3 (verified: 3 lint errors). Binding a local `SocketData` to the generic makes `socket.data.userId`/`email` resolve to `string`; defining it locally (rather than importing) honors the file's dependency whitelist, and because the shape is identical to the shared `SocketData`, the consumer's `io.use(socketAuth)` typechecks structurally (verified with a throwaway probe) | The local `SocketData` and the shared `@app/shared` `SocketData` must remain structurally identical or the consumer `io.use` call would fail to typecheck; mitigated because both are the minimal `{ userId: string; email: string }` identity and any divergence surfaces immediately at the call site |
| `socket.handshake.auth.token` is read into an explicitly `unknown`-typed binding before the `typeof === 'string'` guard; `query.token` is read directly                                                                                                                                                                             | Read it at its inferred type and narrow in place; cast with `as string`                                                                                                    | socket.io types `handshake.auth` with an `any`-valued index signature (`{ [key: string]: any }`), so a bare read yields `any` and trips `@typescript-eslint/no-unsafe-assignment` (Rule 3); annotating the binding `unknown` tames the `any` with no cast, and the existing `typeof`/length guard narrows it back to `string`. `query` is `ParsedUrlQuery` (already a safe `string \| string[] \| undefined`) so it needs no annotation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | None — `unknown` is strictly safer than the source `any` and the runtime behavior is unchanged                                                                                                                                                                                                          |

## `packages/web` — Create-channel dialog (`src/components/channels/CreateChannelDialog.tsx`)

Decisions for the controlled modal that creates a channel (AAP §0.5.2 Dialog mapping, screenshot 500 modal shell). It composes shadcn `Dialog` + `Form` primitives, drives the form with `react-hook-form` + `zodResolver(createChannelSchema)` (the single source of truth shared with the API per §0.8.4), submits through an inline `useMutation` calling `apiClient.post<ChannelWithMembers>('/api/channels', body)`, and on success invalidates `['channels']`, toasts, resets, closes, and navigates to the new channel. Visibility is owned by the parent via the `open` / `onOpenChange` controlled props.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What alternatives existed                                                                                         | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                 |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `isPrivate` is rendered as a Tailwind-styled native `<input type="checkbox">` wrapped in a shadcn `Label`, not a shadcn toggle primitive                                                                                      | A shadcn `Checkbox` or `Switch` primitive (e.g. via `npx shadcn@latest add checkbox`)                             | This PoC's UI inventory contains 23 primitives and neither `@/components/ui/checkbox` nor `@/components/ui/switch` exists; generating one is outside this file's scope and would be unrequested scope creep. A native checkbox is keyboard-operable for free (Space toggles), and `accent-primary` plus the shadcn `focus-visible:ring-ring` tokens keep it visually consistent with the design system                                                               | Slightly less polished than a Radix `Switch` (no toggle animation); functionally and visually adequate, and a future `add switch` swap is localized to this one field |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/...`: `createChannelSchema`, `CreateChannelInput`, and `ChannelWithMembers` are imported from `@app/shared/schemas/channel` and `@app/shared/types/channel` | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the prompt printed                                              | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — confirmed by its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and sibling components' `@app/shared/...` imports; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc` / Vite (Rule 3). Consistent with the `@app/*` precedent already recorded for `ChannelListItem`, `SearchBar`, `SearchResultItem`, `@app/db`, and `@app/web`                                   | None functional; a future monorepo rescope must change every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                              |
| The create-channel `useMutation` lives inline in this dialog; no `useCreateChannel` hook is extracted                                                                                                                         | Extract the mutation into a `useCreateChannel` hook under `@/hooks/`                                              | The `useChannels.ts` contract explicitly forbids adding a `useCreateChannel` mutation there (it is a read-only query hook); this dialog is the single channel-creation surface in the PoC, so co-locating the mutation with its only consumer keeps the create UX in one auditable place                                                                                                                                                                             | If multiple components later need to create channels, the mutation should be refactored into a shared hook; documented as a known extension point                     |
| On success the sidebar is refreshed with `void queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['channels'] })`                                                                                                                     | An optimistic `setQueryData(['channels'], (prev) => [...prev, newChannel])` prepend                               | The mutation already returns the canonical `ChannelWithMembers`, so a refetch is simpler and guaranteed consistent with the server; the PoC has no requirement for zero-latency optimistic updates                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | A brief (typically <500 ms) gap between submit and the sidebar reflecting the new channel; acceptable                                                                 |
| An empty `description` is omitted from the POST body via a conditional spread rather than sent as an empty string                                                                                                             | Always send `description: ''` in the request body                                                                 | `createChannelSchema.description` is `.trim().max(250).optional()`, so omitting the key keeps the wire payload clean and matches the optional intent; the controlled `Textarea` still binds `''` as its value to avoid React's controlled-to-uncontrolled warning, and the empty value is stripped only at submit time                                                                                                                                               | None                                                                                                                                                                  |
| The `name` field gets initial focus via a `useEffect([open])` that calls `nameInputRef.current?.focus()` inside `requestAnimationFrame`, returning `undefined` on the not-open branch                                         | Radix's `onOpenAutoFocus` event with `event.preventDefault()` then manual focus; the native `autoFocus` attribute | The `useEffect` form is decoupled from Radix internals and the `requestAnimationFrame` defers focus until after the portal has mounted, ensuring the `name` field — not the auto-rendered close X — receives focus; `autoFocus` interacts poorly with Radix's focus trap, and the explicit `return undefined` satisfies `noImplicitReturns` (Rule 3)                                                                                                                 | If Radix's own initial-focus runs first, the rAF simply refocuses the name field — idempotent and safe                                                                |
| The `name` input attaches two refs through a single callback (`field.ref(node); nameInputRef.current = node;`)                                                                                                                | Use only react-hook-form's `field.ref`; use only the local `nameInputRef`                                         | The field needs react-hook-form's ref for validation/registration AND the local ref for the auto-focus effect; the callback-ref pattern attaches both without one overwriting the other                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | None; the callback returns `void` and runs on mount/unmount as React expects                                                                                          |
| Cancel is a `Button type="button" variant="ghost"` with an explicit `onClick={() => onOpenChange(false)}`; Create is `type="submit"`; both are disabled while the mutation is pending                                         | Wrap Cancel in shadcn's `<DialogClose>`; leave buttons enabled during submit                                      | An explicit handler reads symmetrically next to the Create button and keeps both footer actions styled as `Button`s; `type="button"` ensures Enter inside the form triggers submit (Create), not cancel; disabling both during `isPending` prevents double-submit and mid-mutation cancel                                                                                                                                                                            | None                                                                                                                                                                  |
| `navigate(...)` and `invalidateQueries(...)` are discarded with the `void` operator, and the form uses `onSubmit={(event) => { void handleSubmit(event); }}`                                                                  | Bare fire-and-forget calls; an `async` `onSubmit` handler passed directly                                         | react-router 7's `navigate` returns `void \| Promise<void>` and `invalidateQueries` returns a `Promise`, both tripping `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises` (error, Rule 3); `form.handleSubmit(...)` returns a `Promise<void>` that, passed straight to `onSubmit`, trips `@typescript-eslint/no-misused-promises`. The `void` operator discards each promise per the rules' `ignoreVoid` default — matching the `StartDmDialog` / `ChannelListItem` precedent | None — fire-and-forget is the intended semantics for navigation and cache invalidation here                                                                           |
| The dialog renders Slack-style guidance copy: a `DialogDescription`, a `FormDescription` naming the allowed character set, and an `isPrivate` helper line                                                                     | Bare field labels with no guidance copy                                                                           | Slack's create-channel modal includes framing/guidance text (Rule 1); surfacing the lowercase `[a-z0-9_-]` constraint up front sets expectations before the user trips the Zod validation error, and the copy uses the curly apostrophe / em-dash glyphs the screenshots show so `react/no-unescaped-entities` is satisfied without HTML entities                                                                                                                    | Slightly more vertical space inside the `sm:max-w-lg` card; acceptable                                                                                                |

## `packages/web` — Search results list (`src/components/search/SearchResultsList.tsx`)

Decisions for the body of the `/app/search` page (AAP §0.6.3): a shadcn `Tabs` widget grouping Messages / Channels / Files, reading the `q` URL parameter via `useSearchParams` and fetching `GET /api/search?q=` through TanStack Query. It composes the `SearchResultItem` sibling and shadcn `Tabs` / `Empty` / `Skeleton` / `ScrollArea` primitives, and renders loading / empty / error / data states. Search is request/response, so no Socket.io subscriptions are added (Rule 2 N/A).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                             | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                     | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What risks it carries                                                                                                             |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `useQuery` is keyed `['search', query]` (the trimmed query), gated by `enabled: query.length > 0`, with `staleTime: 30_000`                                                                  | (a) one static `'search'` key with manual invalidation; (b) URL-only state with no TanStack cache; (c) per-query key `['search', query]`                                      | Caching by query makes back/forward and tab-switch navigation render prior results instantly without a refetch; the `enabled` gate avoids firing against the server Zod `min(1)` constraint when `q` is empty; the `staleTime` matches the global QueryClient window so toggling tabs never refetches                                                                                                                                 | Cache memory grows with each distinct query; TanStack Query garbage-collects stale entries, so growth is bounded within a session |
| The Channels tab renders an explanatory `Empty` ("Channel search coming soon"); the distinct-channel count is still derived from results for the tab label                                   | (a) add a separate `GET /api/channels?q=` endpoint and call it here; (b) derive degraded id-only channel rows from message `channelId`s; (c) honest `Empty` state             | `GET /api/search?q=` returns only `MessageWithAuthor` rows; extending the API is outside this component's scope, and an honest "coming soon" state beats a degraded id-only list                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Users expecting Slack-style channel search see no results in the PoC; acceptable for proof-of-concept and tracked as backlog      |
| The Files tab is derived client-side via `messages.filter((m) => m.file !== null)`, memoized                                                                                                 | (a) a separate `/api/search/files?q=` endpoint; (b) a server-side `type` query param; (c) client-side filter                                                                  | The server returns every matching message; an O(n) client filter over a small result set avoids expanding the API surface for the PoC and keeps a single search round-trip                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | The Files tab count can read 0 even when many messages match; accurate but may briefly surprise users                             |
| `EmptySearchPrompt`, `MessagesTabContent`, `FilesTabContent`, `ChannelsTabContent`, `SearchSkeletons`, and `SearchErrorState` are file-private (non-exported) helpers colocated in this file | (a) extract each tab body to its own file; (b) inline all logic into the main component; (c) file-private helpers                                                             | Each helper is under ~30 lines and tightly coupled to the search body, so colocation avoids a sprawl of micro-files while keeping the main component readable; only `SearchResultsList` (plus its props type) is exported, so `react-refresh/only-export-components` stays satisfied                                                                                                                                                  | If a helper grows beyond ~50 lines it should be extracted; re-evaluate at review                                                  |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/types/message`: `MessageWithAuthor` is imported from `@app/shared/types/message`                                           | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the prompt printed                                                                                                          | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` (confirmed by its package.json name, the web package's `@app/shared` workspace dependency, the exports map mapping `./types/*` to `./src/types/*.ts`, and sibling `@app/shared/...` imports including SearchResultItem and SearchBar); `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail tsc and Vite (Rule 3)                                                               | None functional; a future monorepo rescope must update every `@app/*` specifier together                                          |
| The mandated `import * as React from 'react'` is retained and consumed as a value via `React.useMemo` to derive `messages` / `fileMessages` / `channelIds`                                   | (a) drop the unused React import; (b) reference React only in a type position such as a `React.ReactElement` return type; (c) retain the value import and use `React.useMemo` | An unused `import * as React` fails `noUnusedLocals` (TS6133, verified), and a type-only reference would make `@typescript-eslint/consistent-type-imports` demand `import type`, conflicting with the schema value-import mandate; `React.useMemo` is a genuine value use that also gives the derived arrays referential stability across re-renders since they are passed as props, satisfying the React mandate and Rule 3 together | Memoization adds marginal overhead for typically small result sets; negligible and offset by stable prop identities               |

## `packages/web` — File upload button (`src/components/files/FileUploadButton.tsx`)

Decisions for the paperclip "attach a file" affordance rendered in the `MessageComposer` toolbar (AAP §0.1.1 file sharing, §0.5.2 ghost icon `Button` mapping, Rule 1 screenshot 29). Clicking it opens the browser's native file picker through a hidden `<input type="file">`; the chosen file is validated against the shared 10 MB cap, uploaded via a multipart `POST /api/files` through an inline `useMutation` calling `apiClient.upload<FileAttachment>`, and the resulting `FileAttachment` is handed to the parent via `onFileUploaded`. Sonner toasts sharing the `file-upload` id report the loading / success / error lifecycle (Gate 10), and a `Spinner` replaces the paperclip while the request is in flight. The upload is request/response, so no Socket.io subscriptions are added here (Rule 2 governs the later message broadcast, not the upload).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What alternatives existed                                                                                                   | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                        |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| The 10 MB guard reads `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES` (= 10_485_760) and `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB` (= 10) from the `@app/shared` constants barrel — the bytes constant for the `file.size >` comparison, the MB constant for the human-readable error toast                                                                         | Hardcode `10 * 1024 * 1024` in this component; read `import.meta.env.VITE_MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB`                                 | Single source of truth — the server's multer `limits.fileSize` and this client guard MUST agree, and sharing one workspace constant guarantees they stay in lockstep; an env var can silently drift between client and server, and a literal would duplicate the cap with no compile-time link                                                                                                                                                         | Changing the cap requires the `@app/shared` package to rebuild; mitigated because `pnpm dev` watches workspace packages and the constants are `as const`     |
| The picker `accept` attribute is the file-private constant `ACCEPTED_FILE_TYPES = 'image/*,application/pdf,text/plain'`, not a prop                                                                                                                                                                                | Expose an `accept` prop; allow `*/*`; accept only images; accept a much broader list (.docx, .xlsx, .zip)                   | Images (screenshots), PDFs (docs), and plain text (snippets) cover the Slack PoC use-cases, and an internal constant keeps a single source of truth per the §0.5.4 gap pattern; the attribute only filters the OS picker UX, so the server's multer middleware remains the authoritative type gatekeeper and no client-side mimeType allow-list is added beyond it                                                                                     | Users cannot attach other types (.docx, .zip) until scope expands; acceptable for the PoC and trivially widened by editing one constant                      |
| Drag-and-drop is NOT implemented here; it is deferred to the parent `MessageComposer`. This file renders only the click-to-upload paperclip and its hidden input                                                                                                                                                   | Add `onDragOver` / `onDrop` handlers plus a drop-zone overlay in this component                                             | Single-responsibility — this component triggers an upload, whereas a drop zone is a composer-level affordance that wraps the entire composer surface; co-locating it would couple `FileUploadButton` to composer layout, and the folder spec marks drag-and-drop optional                                                                                                                                                                              | Drag-and-drop becomes a separate work item on `MessageComposer`; acceptable                                                                                  |
| At most one upload at a time — the Button is `disabled` whenever `mutation.isPending`, and the input omits the `multiple` attribute                                                                                                                                                                                | Queue uploads; allow multiple concurrent uploads; add `multiple` to the input                                               | AAP §0.1.1 specifies one file per message, and concurrent uploads would need extra UI to track which result binds to the message; the guard is written `disabled === true \|\| isUploading` so a `boolean \| undefined` prop does not trip `@typescript-eslint/prefer-nullish-coalescing` (Rule 3)                                                                                                                                                     | A user must wait for an in-flight upload before starting another; acceptable for the PoC                                                                     |
| All three lifecycle toasts (loading / success / error) reuse the shared id `'file-upload'`                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Independent toasts per phase; no loading toast at all                                                                       | Passing the same id makes sonner REPLACE the loading toast in place with the success or error toast rather than stacking three toasts, matching Slack's single-status feedback                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | If two upload buttons were mounted simultaneously their toasts would collide; only one composer is mounted per channel/DM at a time, so the constraint holds |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared`: `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES`, `MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB`, and `FileAttachment` are imported from the `@app/shared` barrel                                                                                                                                     | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the prompt printed                                                        | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — confirmed by its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and every sibling component's `@app/*` imports; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc` and Vite (Rule 3). Consistent with the `@app/*` precedent already recorded for `ChannelListItem`, `SearchBar`, `SearchResultItem`, `CreateChannelDialog`, and `SearchResultsList` | None functional; a future monorepo rescope must change every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                     |
| The three shared symbols are pulled from the package-root barrel `@app/shared` in one combined import, rather than from the `@app/shared/constants/limits` and `@app/shared/types/message` subpaths most siblings use                                                                                              | Two subpath imports mirroring the codebase convention                                                                       | The file schema's `internal_imports` names a single `source_file_path` of `packages/shared/src/index.ts` (the barrel) for all three symbols, so the barrel import matches the planned contract; the barrel re-exports both modules and was verified to resolve under tsc Bundler resolution AND a Vite production build (`✓ 24 modules transformed`)                                                                                                   | None; the barrel is a stable public entrypoint declared in the package `exports` map                                                                         |
| The mandated `import * as React from 'react'` namespace import is retained and consumed as a value via `React.useRef`, with `React.ChangeEvent<HTMLInputElement>` and `React.JSX.Element` in type positions — instead of the file-spec's illustrative named `import { useRef }`                                    | Named hook imports (`import { useRef } from 'react'`) as the spec's code blocks show; a default `import React from 'react'` | All 10 sibling web components use the namespace form, and the web tsconfig restricts `types` to `['vite/client','node']`, so a bare `React.X` UMD global would error TS2686 unless React is a real binding; the namespace import yields `React.useRef` (a value use, satisfying `noUnusedLocals`) plus the `React.ChangeEvent` / `React.JSX.Element` types from one import without tripping `consistent-type-imports`                                  | None; matches the established codebase convention and Rule 3                                                                                                 |
| `ApiError` is imported as a VALUE (`import { apiClient, ApiError }`), not a type, and used in `onError` via `error instanceof ApiError ? error.message : …`                                                                                                                                                        | Import `type ApiError` and read `(error as ApiError).message`; show one generic error message for every failure             | `instanceof` is a runtime narrowing check that needs the class binding at runtime, so `ApiError` must be a value import (a `type`-only import would erase it and break the guard); discriminating `ApiError` surfaces the server-provided message (e.g. a multer rejection) while generic/network errors fall back to `Could not upload {name}`, and `consistent-type-imports` is satisfied because the symbol is genuinely used as a value            | None                                                                                                                                                         |
| The visible `Button` and the hidden `<input type="file">` are returned as siblings inside a React Fragment; the input is hidden with the Tailwind `hidden` utility and carries `aria-hidden="true"` + `tabIndex={-1}`, and the input is reset (`inputRef.current.value = ''`) on `onSettled` and on size-rejection | Wrap both in a `<div>`; hide the input with `style={{ display: 'none' }}`; give the input a label/id                        | A Fragment avoids injecting a box that could alter the composer toolbar's flex layout; the `hidden` utility keeps styling in Tailwind tokens per §0.5.3 (no inline styles); `aria-hidden` + `tabIndex={-1}` route keyboard focus and screen readers to the labelled visible Button (`aria-label="Attach a file"`); resetting the value lets the user re-select the same file and fire a fresh `change` event                                           | None                                                                                                                                                         |

## `packages/web` — File preview (`src/components/files/FilePreview.tsx`)

Decisions for the message attachment preview (AAP §0.5.4 documented design-system GAP — shadcn ships no file/image preview primitive; §0.6.3 image-inline vs file-tile rendering; Rule 1 screenshot 29). The component branches on `file.mimeType`: images render inline as an `<img>` inside a `Card` with a `Skeleton` overlay shown until `onLoad` fires and an opacity transition to avoid flash, and click-to-open a Dialog lightbox; non-image files render a `Card` tile with a lucide type icon, truncated filename, human-readable size, and an outline/sm `Button asChild` wrapping a native `<a download>` anchor. All data arrives via props; no network calls are made here, so Rule 2 (Socket.io) does not apply.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                               | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                       |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Full-size image viewing uses a shadcn `Dialog` lightbox (in-app modal) with a visually-hidden `DialogTitle` for the Radix accessibility requirement                                                                   | Open the raw image in a new tab via `<a target="_blank" rel="noreferrer">`; a bespoke fixed-position overlay without the Dialog primitive                                                               | Slack presents attachments in an in-app lightbox, the `Dialog` primitive is already in the design system (verified present), and keeping the user in-context beats spawning a new tab; the `sr-only` `DialogTitle` satisfies Radix without altering the visual                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | The `Dialog` subtree mounts even for images never expanded; negligible for the PoC and removable via lazy import if it ever matters                         |
| File size is rendered by an inline `formatFileSize(bytes)` helper colocated in this file (`B` / `KB` / `MB` / `GB`, one-decimal for KB and up, whole bytes under 1 KB)                                                | Add a `pretty-bytes` dependency; extract the helper to a shared `format-file-size.ts` module                                                                                                            | The folder spec mandates an inline helper to avoid a dependency; the formatter is roughly ten lines, so a package or a separate file would be over-engineering, and zero `0 B` is handled by the first branch                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Slightly coarser output than `pretty-bytes` locale-aware formatting (e.g. no thousands separators); acceptable for the PoC                                  |
| The MIME-to-icon mapping is an inline `selectFileIcon(mimeType)` function using `startsWith` prefix checks over image / video / audio / text / json / javascript / typescript, falling back to the generic `FileIcon` | A full `Record<string, LucideIcon>` map; a `mime-db`-style lookup dependency                                                                                                                            | Only a handful of coarse categories need distinguishing for the PoC, prefix matching adds zero dependencies and stays tree-shake friendly with direct named lucide imports, and an exhaustive map would be larger with no user-visible benefit                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Niche types (e.g. `application/vnd.openxmlformats-…`) fall through to the generic icon; acceptable and easily extended                                      |
| Image `alt` text and the filename `title` tooltip both use `file.originalName` verbatim                                                                                                                               | Synthesize descriptive alt text via heuristics; require the parent to pass an explicit `alt` prop                                                                                                       | The uploaded filename is the best description available without extra user input and mirrors Slack's own behaviour; a mandatory alt prop would push burden onto every call site for marginal gain                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Opaque filenames such as `IMG_2034.jpg` yield weak alt text; mitigated when users upload descriptively-named files                                          |
| `FileAttachment` is received as the required `file` prop; the component performs no fetch and exposes no `fileId`-with-internal-fetch path                                                                            | Add a `useFile(fileId)` hook that fetches metadata by id; accept a bare `fileId` and resolve it internally                                                                                              | The hydrated `MessageWithAuthor.file` already embeds the full `FileAttachment`, so the parent passes it straight down — no `useFile` hook exists in `src/hooks/` and adding one would create needless N+1 fetches                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Tight coupling to the parent Message DTO shape; mitigated by the strong `FileAttachment` typing from `@app/shared`                                          |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared`: `FileAttachment` is imported (type-only) from the `@app/shared` barrel                                                                            | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the prompt printed                                                                                                                                    | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — confirmed by its `package.json` `name`, the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and the sibling `FileUploadButton.tsx` `@app/shared` import; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc` and Vite (Rule 3). Consistent with the `@app/*` precedent recorded for `FileUploadButton`, `SearchResultsList`, `SearchResultItem`, `SearchBar`, `ChannelListItem`, and `CreateChannelDialog` | None functional; a future monorepo rescope must update every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                    |
| `selectFileIcon` has no explicit return-type annotation; TypeScript infers the `LucideIcon` union, rendered via `const Icon = selectFileIcon(...)` then `<Icon className="size-5 …" />`                               | Annotate the return as `React.ComponentType<{ className?: string }>` per the spec's illustrative signature                                                                                              | The schema's react `members_accessed` is exactly `useState`; annotating with `React.ComponentType` would force an extra `React`/`ComponentType` import beyond the contract, whereas every branch returns the same `LucideIcon` type so the inferred union collapses and renders without error under strict TS                                                                                                                                                                   | None; all lucide icons share one props type, so the inferred type is precise                                                                                |
| The API base is computed as `(import.meta.env.VITE_API_URL ?? '').replace(/\/$/, '')`, retaining the `??
