''` guard even though `vite-env.d.ts` types `VITE_API_URL` as a non-null `string`                            | Drop the guard to mirror `src/lib/api-client.ts` (`import.meta.env.VITE_API_URL.replace(…)`)                                                                                                            | The file-spec mandates the fallback as defence against a genuinely unset env var at runtime (the ambient type is a compile-time assertion, not a runtime guarantee); the project's ESLint preset is `recommended`+`stylistic` type-checked, so `no-unnecessary-condition` is off and the redundant `??` raises no warning under the zero-warning build (Rule 3)                                                                                                                 | Marginally redundant against the declared type; harmless and isolated to one expression                                                                     |
| The lightbox `DialogContent` is given an explicit `aria-describedby={undefined}` to opt out of Radix's optional description                                                                                           | Add a visually-hidden `DialogDescription` (requires importing `DialogDescription`, beyond the schema's `{Dialog, DialogContent, DialogTitle}` dialog imports); leave the Radix dev advisory unaddressed | Runtime browser testing surfaced Radix's "Missing `Description` or `aria-describedby={undefined}` for {DialogContent}" dev-console advisory; the lightbox needs no description beyond its `DialogTitle` (the filename), so the Radix-documented `aria-describedby={undefined}` opt-out is the minimal, schema-faithful fix — it adds no import, makes no visual change, and clears the console in line with the Rule 3 zero-warning philosophy                                  | None; the attribute is accessibility-only and changes no rendered output. If a textual description is ever desired, swap to a `sr-only` `DialogDescription` |

## `packages/web` — Socket.io React bindings (`src/hooks/useSocket.ts`)

Decisions for the foundational typed Socket.io hooks layer (AAP §0.1.1 real-time delivery, §0.4.5 real-time event contract, §0.8.1 Rule 2 "all real-time updates traverse Socket.io", §0.8.4 typed events). The file exports `useConnectSocket()` (app-shell connect lifecycle + Sonner toasts), `useSocket()` (live socket, connection state, typed `emit`), `useSocketEvent(event, handler)` (component-scoped subscription), and the `UseSocketResult` interface. It consumes the singleton from `src/lib/socket.ts` and the typed event contracts from `@app/shared/types/socket-events`, and is the only hooks module permitted to call `getSocket()` directly. Authoring it also required a one-keyword change to its dependency `src/lib/socket.ts` (first row below).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                        | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                   |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The `AppSocket` type alias in the dependency `src/lib/socket.ts` was changed from `type AppSocket = …` to `export type AppSocket = …` (a one-keyword addition) so this file can import it                                                                                                                                                                                          | Define a duplicate `AppSocket` alias locally in `useSocket.ts`; import the bare `socket.io-client` `Socket` and re-parameterise it here                          | `socket.ts` already declared `type AppSocket = Socket<ServerToClientEvents, ClientToServerEvents>` but omitted `export`, while this file's schema `internal_imports` and the folder spec both require importing `AppSocket` from `@/lib/socket`; adding `export` is the minimal, backward-compatible fix and keeps ONE definition of the inverted-generic client socket type (DRY), avoiding drift if the generics ever change                                                                                             | A second (type-only) symbol is now exported from `socket.ts`; negligible — it is erased at build time and the internal usages on lines 26/46 are unaffected             |
| `disconnectSocket` is NOT imported, even though this file's schema `internal_imports` `names` list includes it                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Import it verbatim to mirror the schema `names` list                                                                                                             | The schema's own purpose text states `disconnectSocket()` is "used by `useAuth.logout()` orchestration but NOT by this file's effects"; this module never calls it (the orchestrated logout disconnect is owned by the auth flow), so importing it would be an unused binding that fails `noUnusedLocals` (TS6133) and `@typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars` under the zero-warning build (Rule 3). Honouring the purpose text over the literal `names` list is the only form that compiles                                  | A reader comparing the import list to the schema `names` sees a missing symbol; this row reconciles it so the omission is not treated as a defect (Explainability rule) |
| DEVIATION from the agent-prompt's illustrative `@blitzy-slack/shared/types/socket-events`: `ClientToServerEvents` / `ServerToClientEvents` are imported (type-only) from `@app/shared/types/socket-events`                                                                                                                                                                         | Keep the literal `@blitzy-slack/shared` specifier the prompt printed                                                                                             | The workspace package is scoped `@app/shared` — confirmed by `packages/shared/package.json` `name`, its `exports` map (`"./types/*": "./src/types/*.ts"`), the web package's `@app/shared` `workspace:*` dependency, and the dependency `src/lib/socket.ts` itself importing the same `@app/shared/types/socket-events`; `@blitzy-slack/shared` resolves to no package and would fail `tsc`/Vite (Rule 3). Mirrors the `@app/*` precedent recorded for `useChannels` and every sibling web file                            | None functional; a future monorepo rescope must update every `@app/*` specifier together                                                                                |
| `useState` (printed in the agent-prompt's Phase-1 import block) is NOT imported                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Import it alongside the other four react hooks as the prompt sketched                                                                                            | `useState` is never used here — all connection state flows through the module-level `useSyncExternalStore` pub/sub, not component state — and the schema `external_imports` for `react` lists exactly `useCallback`, `useEffect`, `useRef`, `useSyncExternalStore`. Importing the unused `useState` would fail `noUnusedLocals` / `no-unused-vars` (Rule 3)                                                                                                                                                                | None; the four imported hooks cover the full implementation                                                                                                             |
| Connection state is held in a module-level pub/sub (`connectionState` + a `Set` of listeners) consumed via `useSyncExternalStore`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | `useState` plus a global event-emitter; a Zustand slice for connection state; reading `socket.connected` directly inside each component                          | The socket is a singleton with ONE global connection status that many components observe at once; `useSyncExternalStore` is React 18's canonical primitive for subscribing to external mutable state and is tear-free under concurrent rendering, and `getConnectionSnapshot` returns a reference that is stable between transitions so re-renders fire only on real changes                                                                                                                                               | Slightly more boilerplate than `useState`; accepted for the correctness guarantee                                                                                       |
| `useSocketEvent` captures `handler` in a ref and registers a stable listener, keying the subscription effect on `[event, token]` only                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Include `handler` in the subscription-effect deps and re-subscribe whenever it changes                                                                           | The ref pattern registers ONE listener per `(component, event)` pair while always invoking the latest closure, so consumers may pass inline handlers without `useCallback` and without re-subscribing every render; `handler` is read only through `handlerRef.current` inside the effect, so `react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` is satisfied by `[event, token]` with NO eslint-disable required                                                                                                                               | If a future edit references `handler` directly inside the subscription effect, exhaustive-deps would correctly demand it; the ref indirection must be preserved         |
| LOCALIZED function-type casts at the Socket.io call sites — `socket.emit`, `socket.on`, and `socket.off` are each asserted to a concrete `(ev: E, …) => void` signature (the parenthesised-method form erases to a grouped call that preserves `this`, verified) — plus two shape assertions, `stableListener as ServerToClientEvents[E]` and `handlerRef.current as (…a) => void` | Call `socket.emit` / `socket.on` directly with no cast; widen to `any` (forbidden by Rule 3)                                                                     | Socket.io's generic `emit<Ev>(ev, …args: EventParams<EmitEvents, Ev>)` and `on`/`off<Ev>(ev, listener: ListenEvents[Ev])` do not unify with this file's own generic bridge (`E extends keyof …` + `Parameters<…[E]>`) when `E` is an unresolved type parameter; the casts are concrete FUNCTION-type assertions (never `any`, so `no-explicit-any` / `no-unsafe-*` stay green) localized to one call site each. `@ts-ignore` / `@ts-expect-error` are forbidden (Rule 3), so a localized `as` is the only compliant bridge | The casts assert shapes the surrounding generics guarantee by construction; if an event signature gains parameters the cast site must be revisited                      |
| `useConnectSocket` is a separate hook from `useSocket`, and its effect cleanup does NOT call `disconnectSocket()`; a module-level `lifecycleAttached` guard makes attachment idempotent                                                                                                                                                                                            | A single mega-hook that connects on first mount of any consumer; disconnect the singleton on every effect cleanup; an instance-level (`useRef`) attachment guard | Connection bring-up is an app-shell concern mounted once, not something every `useSocket()` consumer triggers; disconnecting on cleanup would race sibling consumers of the shared singleton, so the orchestrated disconnect is owned solely by the auth-store logout flow. The guard belongs at module level because the socket it guards is module-level, keeping repeated mounts and Fast Refresh idempotent                                                                                                            | If the app shell unmounts without logout (e.g. HMR) the socket persists; acceptable because the logout path is explicit                                                 |
| `emit` and `useSocketEvent` no-op when `token === null` (logged out), and `useSocket().socket` is `null` in that state                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Throw an error when called while logged out; queue events until authenticated                                                                                    | A logged-out caller has no socket; a silent no-op is the least-surprising behaviour and lets consumers call `emit` / subscribe without gating on auth themselves. The public `socket` field is typed `AppSocket \| null`, so TypeScript forces consumers to handle the null state                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Silent failures could mask a bug; mitigated because the dev-tools network/WS panel shows the absence of traffic                                                         |
| The disconnect toast uses `duration: Infinity`, and the `'io client disconnect'` reason is filtered out of the toast path                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Auto-dismiss the disconnect toast after a few seconds; toast on every disconnect including explicit logout                                                       | A dropped connection is a persistent state until it recovers, so the toast must stay visible (it is dismissed by the `connect` handler on reconnect); the `'io client disconnect'` reason is emitted only by an explicit `socket.disconnect()` (logout), where a "connection lost" toast would be wrong                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | None significant; the user is kept aware that real-time features are degraded while offline                                                                             |
| All four `SOCKET_TOAST_IDS` keys are retained although only `disconnected` and `connectError` are currently referenced; ids are used to deduplicate Sonner toasts                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Drop the unreferenced `reconnecting` / `reconnected` keys; stack a fresh toast on every lifecycle event                                                          | Passing a fixed `id` makes Sonner update a toast in place rather than stacking during reconnect churn; the object binding is used (its `disconnected` / `connectError` members are read) and `noUnusedLocals` / `no-unused-vars` target bindings, not individual object properties, so the unused keys raise no warning. Keeping all four matches the schema's declared toast-id namespace and reserves the reconnect-phase vocabulary for future handlers                                                                 | A reader may wonder why two ids are unused; this row records that they are the reserved namespace for reconnect-phase toasts                                            |

## `packages/web` — Content header (`src/components/layout/Header.tsx`)

Decisions for the authenticated content column's top bar (`Header`) — the first row of the right-most column in the three-column app shell, visible in `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 100.png`. It renders the route-context title on the left, the shared `SearchBar` in the centre, and `Help` / `Members` ghost icon buttons on the right (AAP §0.5.2, §0.6.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                   | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                           |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The `/app/dms/:dmId` route renders the static placeholder title `Direct Message` instead of resolving the other participant's display name                                                         | (a) inline a TanStack Query call to `apiClient.get('/api/dms')` to resolve the participant; (b) wait for a `@/hooks/useDms` hook (no pending plan exists); (c) hardcode placeholder text        | No `useDms` hook exists under `@/hooks`, and the auth store holds only `{ id, email }` for the logged-in user — never the other participant; AAP §0.7.2 puts profile editing out of scope and the spec exposes no display-name endpoint for the counterpart. A static placeholder is the simplest correct UX until a follow-up adds DM-name resolution                                                                                                                                                                                      | Suboptimal UX — the DM header does not name the conversation partner; a downstream agent SHOULD add a `useDms` hook in a follow-up so the header can show the real display name |
| The `Help` button (`HelpCircle`) is rendered with no `onClick` handler — icon plus tooltip only, inert when clicked                                                                                | (a) link to Slack's external help centre; (b) open an in-app FAQ / help popover; (c) omit the button entirely                                                                                   | AAP §0.7.2 puts external integrations and help documentation out of scope, so there is nothing for the button to open in this PoC; retaining the control preserves visual fidelity with `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 100.png` (the `?` glyph in the top-right) without pulling an out-of-scope surface into the build                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | The control looks interactive but is inert, which can mislead a user; acceptable for a PoC and trivially wired once a help surface exists                                       |
| The `Members` button (`Users`) is likewise rendered with no `onClick` handler — icon plus tooltip only                                                                                             | (a) open a member-list panel / sheet; (b) navigate to a channel-members route; (c) omit the button                                                                                              | No member-list panel is in scope (AAP §0.7.2), so there is no destination to open; the button is retained for screenshot fidelity (the member-avatar cluster in `screenshots/Slack web Jul 2024 100.png` maps to a `Users` affordance) while staying inert until a members surface is added                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Same inert-but-interactive-looking risk as the `Help` button; acceptable for the PoC and easy to wire to a future members panel                                                 |
| JSX attributes are written with double quotes (e.g. `className="…"`, `aria-hidden="true"`) even though this file's agent-prompt code sample printed single-quoted JSX attributes and no semicolons | Follow the prompt's illustrative snippet literally (single-quoted JSX attributes, no semicolons)                                                                                                | The committed `.prettierrc` sets `jsxSingleQuote: false` and `semi: true`, and `make format` / `prettier --check` enforces it repo-wide (Rule 3); every sibling non-`ui/**` component (`SearchBar.tsx`, `ChannelListItem.tsx`, `Landing.tsx`) already emits double-quoted JSX. The enforced formatter — not an illustrative snippet — is the authoritative style, so the file was run through `prettier --write` and verified with `prettier --check`                                                                                       | None functional — Prettier owns formatting uniformly; the only risk is a reader comparing the file to the prompt snippet, which this row reconciles                             |
| `HeaderRouteParams` is declared as `interface HeaderRouteParams extends Record<string, string \| undefined>` rather than the agent-prompt's `type HeaderRouteParams = { … }` object alias          | (a) keep the `type` alias the prompt printed; (b) drop the named type and inline the literal at the call site as the sibling `ChannelListItem.tsx` does (`useParams<{ channelId?: string }>()`) | The enforced `@typescript-eslint/consistent-type-definitions` rule (from `stylisticTypeChecked`) requires `interface` for object shapes, so the prompt's `type` form fails `eslint --max-warnings 0` (Rule 3); a bare `interface`, however, lacks the implicit index signature React Router 7's `useParams<T extends Record<string, string \| undefined>>` constraint needs, so it must `extends Record<string, string \| undefined>`. This keeps the prompt's named, documented `HeaderRouteParams` while satisfying both `tsc` and ESLint | None functional — the `extends Record` widening only adds the index signature the generic constraint already assumes; both `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint` pass clean               |

## `packages/api` — Presence heartbeat handler (`sockets/handlers/presence.handler.ts`)

Decisions for the Socket.io presence-heartbeat handler — the fourth socket handler family alongside `channel`, `message`, and `reaction`. It attaches the `presence:heartbeat` listener, refreshes the user's Redis TTL through `recordHeartbeat` (`services/presence.service.ts`), and broadcasts `presence:update` to the user's own room only when the user's bucket transitions (AAP §0.4.5 real-time contract, §0.8.4 presence semantics, Rule 2, Gate 9, Gate 10).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                           | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                        |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `presence:update` is broadcast ONLY when `recordHeartbeat`'s returned `previousState !== currentState`; a heartbeat that finds the user already `online` refreshes the Redis TTL silently and emits nothing                                                                                                               | Broadcast on every heartbeat; have the service return a boolean "did transition" instead of the `{ previousState, currentState, lastSeenAt }` tuple | Gating on a real transition is the primary presence scalability lever — at 50 users each emitting a 30 s heartbeat, unconditional broadcasting is ~1.7 events/s of pure noise (AAP §0.8.4, Gate 9 presence < 5 s). The service's `HeartbeatResult` tuple carries both states, so the handler both gates the broadcast and includes `previousState`/`currentState` in the emitted payload and the log line                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | The first heartbeat after a fresh connect typically finds the user already `online` and so skips a broadcast; mitigated by the web client's initial `getPresenceMap` fetch on workspace load |
| The transition is emitted to `io.to(userRoom(userId))` (the user's own `user:<id>` room) only — not into each channel/DM room the user belongs to                                                                                                                                                                         | Iterate the user's channel memberships and emit `presence:update` into every `channelRoom(id)`; broadcast globally with `io.emit(...)`              | Reusing the always-joined `user:<id>` room keeps the handler free of a membership lookup on every transition and lets the user's own tabs reconcile immediately; other members' sidebars hydrate presence from `getPresenceMap` on workspace open (AAP §0.6.2). A global `io.emit` would leak presence to unrelated sockets and is forbidden by the handler contract                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Other users' sidebars do not see the transition in real time until they refetch — accepted for the PoC and tracked as a future per-channel fan-out enhancement                               |
| No-transition heartbeats log at `debug`; transitions log at `info`; failures log at `error` — every line carries `component`/`event`/`socketId`/`userId`/`latency`                                                                                                                                                        | Skip logging non-transitions entirely; log them at `info`                                                                                           | Heartbeats are high-frequency (every 30 s per connected tab), so `info`-level non-transition lines would flood production logs; `debug` keeps heartbeat arrival observable in development (where the logger level is `debug`) while the production `info` level suppresses them, and transition/error lines stay visible (Gate 10 structured logging)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Slightly more verbose development logs — acceptable                                                                                                                                          |
| The `presence:heartbeat` listener is `() => void` — no payload parse, no acknowledgement callback; it delegates via `void handleHeartbeat(io, socket)`                                                                                                                                                                    | Add an ack so the client can confirm delivery; add a Zod `.parse()` validation step                                                                 | `ClientToServerEvents[PRESENCE_HEARTBEAT]` is declared `() => void` in `@app/shared/types/socket-events` (no payload, no ack), and heartbeats are fire-and-forget — an ack adds a round-trip on every 30 s emit and the client self-heals on its next heartbeat; with no payload there is nothing to validate, so a `.parse()` would be dead code. The `void` prefix satisfies `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises` (Rule 3)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | A heartbeat lost in a disconnect window slightly prolongs the "away" perception — absorbed by the 5-minute offline threshold                                                                 |
| The catch block derives the client error code inline (`err instanceof ServiceError ? err.name.replace(/Error$/, '').toUpperCase() \|\| 'SERVICE_ERROR' : 'INTERNAL_ERROR'`) and imports ONLY `ServiceError` from the errors module — no shared `resolveErrorCode` helper, no `ZodError`/subclass arms                     | Reuse the sibling handlers' fuller `resolveErrorCode` helper that special-cases `ZodError` and each `ServiceError` subclass                         | This handler performs no schema parse (the event has no payload), so `ZodError` and the per-subclass arms are unreachable; importing them would trip `no-unused-vars` (Rule 3). The inline form matches the file-spec's prescribed body and the `ServiceError`-only import matches the file's declared internal-imports contract; a thrown error here can only be a Redis-connectivity failure, which the generic `INTERNAL_ERROR`/name-derived code covers                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Codes here are coarser than the sibling handlers' — acceptable because the only realistic failure is infrastructure, not a business-rule subclass                                            |
| DEVIATION from the file-spec's literal imports: `ServiceError` is imported from `../../middleware/errors.js` (spec printed `../../services/errors.js`), the error event uses the `ERROR` constant (spec printed `SOCKET_ERROR`), and shared imports use the `@app/shared/*` scope (spec printed `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`) | Follow the spec's literal specifiers; suppress the resulting resolution errors with `@ts-ignore` (forbidden by Rule 3)                              | `packages/api/src/services/errors.ts` does not exist — the canonical errors module is `middleware/errors.ts`, the source of `ServiceError`, which all three sibling handlers import from there; `@app/shared/constants/events` exports `ERROR = 'error'` and has no `SOCKET_ERROR` symbol (the reserved Socket.io channel mapped by `ServerToClientEvents[ERROR]`); and the workspace is scoped `@app/*` (already recorded in the _Decision-log format_ reconciliation row), not `@blitzy-slack/*`. Any literal spec specifier fails `tsc` with TS2307 and breaks `make build` (Rule 3). Verified: full-module `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint . --max-warnings 0` pass | None functional — the corrected specifiers are the established codebase conventions used by every sibling handler                                                                            |

## `packages/api` — Files route (`routes/files.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                             | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                   |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `GET /api/files/:id` sets `Content-Disposition: inline; filename="<percent-encoded originalName>"`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | `attachment; filename=...` to force a download                                                                                                        | Slack web renders image/PDF attachments inline, so `inline` lets the browser display the type negotiated from the persisted `mimeType`; the user-meaningful original filename (not the random `storedName`) is percent-encoded into the header so a "Save As" still yields a sensible name                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | A user cannot one-click "download" an inline-displayable type; mitigated because browser right-click "Save As" preserves the encoded filename           |
| A missing multipart `file` field throws `ValidationError('Missing file field "file" in multipart body')` rather than writing a `res.status(400).json(...)` body inline                                                                                                                                                                                         | Construct the 400 response body inline in the handler                                                                                                 | `uploadMiddleware` leaves `req.file` `undefined` (it does not throw) when the field is absent, so the route must detect it; throwing `ValidationError` routes through the centralized errorHandler and yields the SAME 400 envelope as a Zod failure, keeping the route free of response-shaping logic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | None — `ValidationError` maps to errorHandler 400 `{ error: 'BadRequest', message }`, identical to every other validation 400                           |
| The `res.sendFile` error callback responds `500 { error: 'InternalServerError', message, code: 'file_read_error' }` guarded by `!res.headersSent`, instead of rethrowing to the errorHandler                                                                                                                                                                   | `next(err)` to the errorHandler; retry the disk read                                                                                                  | Once `res.sendFile` has begun streaming, headers may already be flushed, so the errorHandler could only terminate the socket; emitting a guarded JSON 500 only when nothing has been written gives the client a clean error, while a post-flush failure simply ends the stream. A disk read failing after the ACL passed signals corruption/path drift, so surfacing 500 (not retrying) is safest. The `'InternalServerError'` label matches the codebase's canonical `ErrorPayload` 500s in `error-handler.ts`, not the agent-prompt draft's `'Internal Server Error'`                                                                                                                           | The caller sees a 500 with no retry; mitigated by the structured `download.error` log carrying `diskPath`/`fileId`/`userId` for diagnosis               |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt metadata/internal-imports: the upload handler calls `createFile` (metadata/spec printed `saveUploadedFile`), `ValidationError` is imported from `../middleware/errors.js` (spec printed `../services/errors.js`), and the `FileAttachment` type uses the `@app/shared/*` scope (spec printed `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`) | Follow the literal spec specifiers; add a `saveUploadedFile` alias to the service; suppress resolution errors with `@ts-ignore` (forbidden by Rule 3) | The files service export was renamed to `createFile` during CP3 remediation (see the service-contracts alignment row above) as a clean rename with zero consumers — this route is its first consumer and binds to `createFile`; `packages/api/src/services/errors.ts` does not exist (the canonical module is `middleware/errors.ts`, from which every sibling route/service imports the error classes); and the workspace is scoped `@app/*` (recorded in the Decision-log format reconciliation row), not `@blitzy-slack/*`. Any literal spec specifier fails `tsc` (TS2305/TS2307) and breaks `make build` (Rule 3). Verified: full-module `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint . --max-warnings 0` pass | None functional — the corrected specifiers are the established conventions used by every sibling route (`health.ts`, `search.ts`) and the files service |

## `packages/api` — Direct-messages route (`routes/dms.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                     | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                   |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt metadata/internal-imports: the `POST /api/dms` handler calls `startDm` (the metadata/skeleton printed `createOrFindDm`), workspace contracts are imported from the `@app/shared/*` scope (the skeleton printed `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`), and a bare `import type {} from 'pino-http';` is added so `req.log` is typed | Follow the literal skeleton specifiers (`createOrFindDm`, `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`); add a `createOrFindDm` alias to the dms service; access `req.log` untyped or through an `any` cast (forbidden by Rule 3) | The dms-service export was renamed to `startDm` during CP3 remediation (see the Direct-messages service section and the CP3 service-contracts alignment row) as a clean rename with zero consumers — this route is its first consumer and binds to `startDm`; the workspace is scoped `@app/*` (recorded in the Decision-log format reconciliation row), not `@blitzy-slack/*`; and pino-http's `declare module` augmentation is what types `req.log` on the Express `Request`, matching the sibling `routes/messages.ts` and `routes/search.ts` convention. Any literal skeleton specifier fails `tsc` (TS2305/TS2307) and an untyped or `any`-cast `req.log` breaks Rule 3. Verified: full-workspace `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint . --max-warnings 0` pass | None functional — the corrected specifiers and the augmentation import are the conventions already used by every sibling route and the dms service      |
| `POST /api/dms` always responds `200`, never `201`, mirroring the idempotent create-or-find semantics of `startDm`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Return `201` when a new conversation is created and `200` when an existing one is found                                                                                                                       | `startDm` returns the existing conversation on a repeat call or creates one otherwise and does not report which path ran, so a single `200` keeps the client uniform: it always receives the same `DMWithParticipants` body and never branches on status. The web DM-start flow treats both cases identically                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | REST purists may expect `201` on creation; immaterial for the PoC because the client never differentiates and the response body is identical either way |

## `packages/api` — Channels route (`routes/channels.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                            |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Channel mutations (create/join/leave) emit NO Socket.io events; the route never reads `req.app.get('io')`                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Emit `channel:created` / `channel:joined` / `channel:left` broadcasts                                                                                                                           | The AAP §0.4.5 server→client event list defines no channel-lifecycle event, so the web client refetches the channel list on workspace open (Slack's minimal-broadcast pattern); messages posted into a channel are broadcast by `routes/messages.ts`, not here                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | A second tab or other members reflect a created/joined/left channel only after a refetch; acceptable for the PoC                                                 |
| The pagination `cursor` is treated as opaque by the route — never decoded                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Decode the `(createdAt, id)` cursor in the route and pass the parts to the service                                                                                                              | Encapsulation: `channels.service.listChannelMessages` owns the keyset cursor format (base64url JSON), so the route forwards the token verbatim and stays free of pagination internals                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | The service must keep the cursor format stable across versions; documented in the Channels service section above                                                 |
| `limit` is capped at `MAX_PAGE_SIZE` (100) in the inline Zod query schema via `.max(MAX_PAGE_SIZE)` and defaults to `PAGE_SIZE` (50)                                                                                                                                                                                            | Enforce the ceiling inside the service; hardcode `50` / `100` literals                                                                                                                          | Failing fast at the validation layer returns a clean 400 before any DB work, and reusing the `@app/shared/constants/limits` constants keeps the client and server caps in lockstep with no magic numbers                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | None                                                                                                                                                             |
| Path-param/query validation uses inline `channelIdParamsSchema` (`{ id: cuid }`) and `channelMessagesQuerySchema`, passed via `validate({ params, query })`                                                                                                                                                                     | Add these shapes to `@app/shared/schemas/channel`; reuse the shared `joinChannelSchema` (which validates `{ channelId }`) for the `:id` param                                                   | The `:id` and query shapes are HTTP-route-specific and not consumed by the web client, so they live inline (matching the sibling `routes/dms.ts` `dmIdParamsSchema`); `joinChannelSchema` validates the key `channelId`, not the route's `:id` param, so it cannot be used with `validate({ params })` against `req.params`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Minor duplication of the cuid-param shape across route files; accepted as HTTP-local                                                                             |
| `POST /:id/leave` responds `200 { ok: true }`, not `204 No Content`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Return `204` with an empty body                                                                                                                                                                 | A consistent non-empty JSON envelope across every route simplifies the web client's deserializer (it never special-cases an empty body)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | REST purists may prefer `204`; immaterial for the PoC                                                                                                            |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt skeleton: the message-history handler calls `listChannelMessages` (the skeleton printed `listMessages`) and workspace contracts use the `@app/shared/*` scope (the skeleton printed `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`); a bare `import type {} from 'pino-http';` is added so `req.log` is typed | Follow the literal skeleton (`listMessages`, `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`); add a `listMessages` alias to the channels service; access `req.log` untyped or via an `any` cast (forbidden by Rule 3) | The channels-service export is `listChannelMessages` (renamed during CP3 remediation as a clean, zero-consumer rename — this route is its first consumer); the workspace is scoped `@app/*` (recorded in the Decision-log format reconciliation row), not `@blitzy-slack/*`; and pino-http's `declare module` augmentation is what types `req.log`, matching sibling `routes/dms.ts` / `messages.ts` / `search.ts`. Any literal skeleton specifier fails `tsc` (TS2305/TS2307) and an untyped or `any`-cast `req.log` breaks Rule 3. Verified: full-module `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint . --max-warnings 0` pass | None functional — the corrected specifiers are the established conventions used by every sibling route                                                           |
| DEVIATION from this file's `internal_imports` metadata: `joinChannelSchema` and `JoinChannelInput` are NOT imported                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Import them verbatim to mirror the metadata `names` list                                                                                                                                        | Approach A (inline `channelIdParamsSchema` for the `:id` param) never references `joinChannelSchema` / `JoinChannelInput`, and `createChannel`'s argument is structurally checked from the object literal so `CreateChannelInputWithCreator` needs no import either; importing any unused symbol fails `noUnusedLocals` (TS6133) and `@typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars` under the zero-warning build (Rule 3)                                                                                                                                                                                                 | A reader comparing the import list to the metadata sees missing symbols; this row reconciles the omission so it is not treated as a defect (Explainability rule) |

## `packages/api` — Authentication route (`routes/auth.ts`)

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                           |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| DEVIATION from this file's agent-prompt skeleton: the handlers call `registerUser` / `loginUser` / `getMe` (the skeleton printed `register` / `login` / `getCurrentUser`); `GET /me` and `AuthResult.user` are typed `UserResponse` (the skeleton printed `User`); workspace contracts use the `@app/shared/*` scope (the skeleton printed `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`); and a bare `import type {} from 'pino-http';` is added so `req.log` is typed | Follow the literal skeleton specifiers (`register`/`login`/`getCurrentUser`, `User`, `@blitzy-slack/shared/*`); add aliases to the auth service; access `req.log` untyped or via an `any` cast (forbidden by Rule 3) | The auth-service exports are `registerUser` / `loginUser` / `getMe` (recorded in the Authentication service section above); `User` includes `passwordHash` while the passwordHash-free self view and `AuthResult.user` are `UserResponse` (`Omit<User, 'passwordHash'>`), so typing the responses `User` would fail `tsc` and mis-signal a hash field; the workspace is scoped `@app/*` (recorded in the Decision-log format reconciliation row), not `@blitzy-slack/*`; and pino-http's `declare module` augmentation is what types `req.log` on the Express `Request`, matching every sibling route. Any literal skeleton specifier fails `tsc` (TS2305/TS2307) and breaks `make build` (Rule 3). Verified: full-module `tsc --noEmit` and `eslint . --max-warnings 0` pass | None functional — the corrected specifiers and the augmentation import are the conventions already used by every sibling route and the auth service                                             |
| The three handlers carry NO try/catch — every error from the service and middleware layers (Prisma P2002 / `ConflictError`, `UnauthorizedError`, `NotFoundError`, `ValidationError`) propagates to the centralized error-handler; a duplicate-email `register` surfaces Prisma P2002 unwrapped                                                                                                                                                     | Catch the duplicate-email error in the route and shape a custom 409 body; wrap each handler in try/catch and map errors locally                                                                                      | Express 5 auto-forwards rejected async handlers to the error-handler middleware, which maps P2002 to 409 (verified at `error-handler.ts`); letting the error bubble keeps error-to-status mapping centralized and identical across routes, and it is precisely what makes `register` return 409 on a duplicate so `scripts/seed-via-api.ts` treats a re-run as idempotent success (Rule 4). Catching locally would duplicate mapping logic and risk drifting from the central envelope                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Handlers look thin, but that is intentional — all business logic lives in the service layer; the only coupling is the documented errorHandler contract                                          |
| `POST /register` responds `201`; `POST /login` and `GET /me` respond `200`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Return `200` from `register` too (uniform 2xx); return `204` from any endpoint                                                                                                                                       | `register` creates a new user resource, for which `201 Created` is the RESTful signal, while `login` (a session established from existing credentials) and `me` (a read of existing data) are `200 OK`; the bodies are the full `AuthResult` (`{ token, user }`) for register/login and `UserResponse` for me, so no endpoint is a candidate for an empty `204`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Clients must not branch on the specific 2xx code; none do — they read the JSON body uniformly                                                                                                   |
| `GET /me` reads the authenticated id via the non-null assertion `req.user!.id` after the `requireAuth` middleware                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Optional chaining with a fallback (`req.user?.id ?? …`); a redundant runtime `if (!req.user) throw …` guard inside the handler                                                                                       | `requireAuth` populates `req.user` or short-circuits with 401 before this handler runs, so within the handler `req.user` is guaranteed present; the `!` is the cleanest expression of that middleware contract and matches every sibling authenticated route (`dms.ts`, `channels.ts`). A runtime re-check would be dead code under that contract                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | If `requireAuth` were ever misordered (mounted after the handler), the assertion would crash at runtime; mitigated because the mount order is fixed in this file and covered by the route tests |

## `packages/web` — Message timeline hook (`src/hooks/useMessages.ts`)

Decisions for the paginated message-timeline hook that backs both the channel and DM views (AAP §0.1.1 "message history pagination — 50 per page, cursor-based, infinite scroll"; §0.6.3; §0.8.4 pagination contract). It composes three concerns — cursor pagination via TanStack `useInfiniteQuery`, `IntersectionObserver`-driven infinite scroll, and real-time `message:new` cache prepends — behind the `UseMessagesResult` surface consumed by the (planned) `Channel.tsx` / `DirectMessage.tsx` pages.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | What alternatives existed                                                                                             | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Pagination uses `useInfiniteQuery` with an opaque `string` cursor (`pageParam: string \| null`, `initialPageParam: null`, `getNextPageParam: (p) => p.nextCursor`)                                                                                      | Offset pagination (`?page=`); a numeric cursor; decoding the `(createdAt,id)` keyset client-side                      | A cursor is stable under concurrent inserts (an offset shifts when new messages arrive) and treating it as opaque lets the server own the encoding (the API base64url-encodes `(createdAt,id)`) without any client change; mandated by AAP §0.8.4. `null` initial param maps to the server's "newest first page"                                                                                                        | A cursor cannot jump to an arbitrary position, so a future "jump to date" feature is unsupported — explicitly out of PoC scope                                                                                             |
| Incoming `message:new` events update the cache via `queryClient.setQueryData`, never `invalidateQueries`/refetch                                                                                                                                        | `invalidateQueries(['messages', scopeKey])`; a manual refetch; an `onMessage` refetch trigger                         | An in-memory prepend re-renders subscribers on the next tick with zero round-trips, holding the message-delivery budget (<500 ms, AAP Gate 9); a refetch on every arrival would add latency and defeat the budget, and Rule 2 forbids polling                                                                                                                                                                           | If the cache and server diverge (rare reconnect race), there is no automatic reconciliation; acceptable for the PoC and recoverable by a manual remount/refetch                                                            |
| The new message is prepended to `pages[0].messages` (newest-first), and only the first page object is rebuilt immutably (`{...current, pages: [updatedFirst, ...rest]}`)                                                                                | Append to the last page; keep a separate "new messages" array merged at render; mutate the page in place              | The API returns messages newest-first per page with page 0 the latest, so prepending to page 0 keeps the flattened order correct and matches Slack's behaviour (a new message appears at the bottom-newest end of the timeline); an immutable rebuild preserves TanStack's change detection                                                                                                                             | If the user has scrolled far into history, a new arrival still lands on page 0 (the live end) rather than near their viewport — the intended Slack behaviour, not a defect                                                 |
| Incoming events are filtered to `parentId === null` AND a scope match (`incoming.channelId === channelId` for a channel, or `incoming.dmId === dmId` for a DM); non-matching events are ignored, and the message is de-duplicated by `id` before insert | Insert every `message:new`; include thread replies; rely on server-side room scoping alone; skip the dedup check      | The hook owns only the top-level timeline of its own conversation — thread replies live in a separate thread-scoped hook, and another channel/DM's messages must not leak in; the `id` dedup makes a re-delivered event (reconnect, optimistic collision) idempotent so a message is never shown twice                                                                                                                  | The thread panel must run its own `message:new` subscription (explicit, documented); a malformed event lacking `parentId`/scope ids would be dropped silently — acceptable given the typed `ServerToClientEvents` contract |
