| No version prefix (`/api/v1`); sub-routers mount at flat paths (`/auth`, `/channels`, …)                                                            | Add `/api/v1/…`; mount at deep paths like `/auth/v1`                                    | The PoC has a single client and no v2 surface, so a version segment adds path noise with no benefit and matches Slack web's unversioned `/api/...` convention; a `/v2` prefix can be introduced later with no client migration                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | If a breaking v2 ever ships, a `/v2` prefix must be added at that time — a localized, additive change                  |
| The 404 / catch-all handler lives in `app.ts`, NOT in this barrel                                                                                   | Add a wildcard `router.use((req, res) => res.status(404)…)` in the barrel               | Separation of concerns — the barrel is composition-only; request-level fallbacks (404, error handler) belong to the app layer that owns the full middleware chain. Verified at runtime: an unknown `/api/*` path falls through to a 404 (no catch-all swallows it here)                                                                                                                                                                                                             | None — a well-established Express composition pattern                                                                  |
| Sub-routers are imported and mounted in alphabetical order (auth → channels → dms → files → health → messages → search)                             | Order by importance or by request frequency                                             | Express path matching is exact (none of the seven prefixes overlap), so mount order is functionally irrelevant; alphabetical order is purely a code-review readability convention and makes a missing/duplicated mount obvious at a glance                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | None — order has no runtime effect                                                                                     |

## CP4 review remediation — Explainability, room lifecycle, presence fan-out, REST/realtime contract alignment & UI fidelity

Consolidated record of the decisions made while resolving the Checkpoint-4 review (Complete API + Frontend Orchestration). The five rows the CP4 review explicitly flagged as missing Explainability entries — `connectionStateRecovery` window, Express `app.ts` middleware order, the API bootstrap graceful-shutdown sequence, the multi-tab `fetchSockets()` disconnect strategy, and presence TTL semantics — lead the table. The remaining rows capture the cross-cutting rationale for the critical/major/minor fixes that closed the realtime-delivery, REST-contract, auth/observability, and design-system findings. Per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3) these rows are the single source of truth for "why"; a row that changes previously-recorded behaviour explicitly names the decision it supersedes.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Socket.io is constructed with `connectionStateRecovery` ENABLED and `maxDisconnectionDuration = CONNECTION_RECOVERY_WINDOW_MS` (`2 * 60 * 1000` = 2 minutes), `skipMiddlewares: false` (`index.ts` L55, L96-99)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Leave `connectionStateRecovery` off (the Socket.io default — a brief drop loses buffered events and resets room membership); a shorter 30 s window; a longer 5 min+ window; `skipMiddlewares: true`                                                           | A 2-minute window lets a client that briefly loses its connection (tab sleep, network blip, laptop lid) resume the SAME session — Socket.io replays the events missed during the gap and restores room membership — so a transient drop does not surface as a message gap or a presence flap. `skipMiddlewares: false` re-runs the JWT handshake auth on recovery, so a token that expired during the gap is still rejected (a recovered session is never auth-exempt). 2 min balances UX (covers the common short drops) against the adapter's per-session event-buffer memory                                                                                                                                                                     | Each disconnected-but-recoverable session buffers events in the adapter for up to 2 min — a bounded memory cost; a session offline longer than the window does a full reconnect (new socket id, re-auth, re-join), which is the intended fallback                                       |
| Express `app.ts` composes middleware in a fixed, load-bearing order: `disable('x-powered-by')` → `set('trust proxy', 1)` → helmet → cors → `requestLogger` (pino-http) → `express.json` + `express.urlencoded` → `/api` router → JSON 404 handler → `errorHandler` LAST (`app.ts` L55-139)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Body parsers before the logger; CORS before helmet; the 404 as a router-level catch-all (rejected — see the Routes-barrel row above); the error handler not mounted last                                                                                      | Order is functional, not cosmetic: helmet sets security headers before anything can respond; cors runs before the body parsers so a rejected cross-origin preflight short-circuits without parsing a body; pino-http runs before the router so EVERY request (including 404s and validation errors) gets a `reqId` and a log line (Gate 10); the body parsers run before the router so handlers see a parsed `req.body`; the 404 sits after the router so only genuinely unmatched paths reach it; `errorHandler` is mounted LAST so Express 5 funnels every sync throw and async rejection from any upstream layer into the single centralized formatter (AAP §0.6.1 Group 4)                                                                      | Reordering any pair silently breaks an invariant (e.g. a logger mounted after the router would miss 404 lines); the order is load-bearing and recorded here so a future edit does not casually shuffle it                                                                               |
| The API bootstrap (`index.ts`) registers SIGTERM/SIGINT handlers that run ONE guarded shutdown sequence in dependency order: stop accepting new HTTP connections (`httpServer.close`) → `await io.close()` → `await disconnectRedisClients()` → `await prisma.$disconnect()` → `process.exit(0)`; a 10 s `SHUTDOWN_TIMEOUT_MS` hard-exit timer (`setTimeout(...).unref()`) forces `process.exit(1)` if a step hangs; an `isShuttingDown` re-entrancy guard makes a second signal a no-op (`index.ts` L144-205)                                                                                                       | Fire-and-forget `void` disconnects with no ordering; rely on the `@app/db` package's own `disconnectPrisma()` signal handler alone (recorded near the top of this log); no hard-exit timer; exit immediately on the second signal                             | Order matters: closing the HTTP server first stops new requests, closing `io` next drains WebSocket sessions, then the Redis adapter clients and finally Prisma release their pools — reversing this could disconnect Redis while sockets still publish, or drop Postgres while a request is mid-flight, leaking connections ("too many connections" under repeated `docker compose down` / `make down`). This API-layer sequence COORDINATES the per-package disconnect helpers (the standalone `@app/db` `disconnectPrisma` handler is subsumed here so the API owns the full ordering). The `unref()`'d timer guarantees the process eventually dies even if a `close()` hangs, and the guard prevents a double-Ctrl-C from racing two shutdowns | A step that hangs past 10 s is force-killed with exit code 1, potentially skipping later cleanup; acceptable because a hung `close()` already indicates an unhealthy process and the OS reclaims the sockets                                                                            |
| The disconnect handler (`sockets/index.ts`) clears presence and broadcasts `offline` ONLY when the user has no remaining sockets: it captures `userRoom(userId)`, calls `io.in(userRoomKey).fetchSockets()` AFTER the socket has left, and runs `clearPresence` + the `offline` `presence:update` only when `remainingSockets.length === 0` (`sockets/index.ts` L181-250)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Clear presence on EVERY socket disconnect (marks a multi-tab user offline the instant they close one tab); track an in-memory per-user socket counter; never clear on disconnect and rely solely on the Redis TTL                                             | A user routinely keeps several tabs/devices open; clearing on the first disconnect would flap them offline while they are still present elsewhere. `fetchSockets()` is the adapter-aware count — it sees sockets on EVERY API instance via the Redis adapter, so the "last socket" decision is correct cluster-wide, which a local in-memory counter cannot guarantee. Querying AFTER the socket leaves means the leaving socket is already excluded. Only the genuine last disconnect transitions the user offline                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | `fetchSockets()` is an async adapter round-trip on every disconnect (negligible at PoC scale); a hard instance crash leaves the Redis presence key to lapse via its TTL rather than an explicit clear, which the `AWAY_THRESHOLD_MS` TTL already handles                                |
| Presence is stored in Redis as `setex(presence:<userId>, PRESENCE_TTL_SECONDS, JSON.stringify({ lastSeenMs, state }))` where `PRESENCE_TTL_SECONDS = ceil(AWAY_THRESHOLD_MS / 1000)`; the LIVE state is always re-derived at read time from `Date.now() - lastSeenMs` via `bucketFromAge` (online `[0, ONLINE_THRESHOLD_MS)`, away `[ONLINE_THRESHOLD_MS, AWAY_THRESHOLD_MS)`, offline beyond), never trusting the stored `state` bucket; a missing/malformed key resolves to `offline` (`presence.service.ts` L60, L93-154, L188-206)                                                                               | Store a bare ISO timestamp string (the prior CP4 behaviour the review flagged); trust the persisted `state` bucket as the live value; a per-field Redis hash; no TTL with a cron sweeper                                                                      | The review required the `{ lastSeenMs, state }` JSON payload plus TTL-based resolution. `lastSeenMs` (epoch ms) is the authoritative age signal so read-time bucketing stays correct as the clock advances (a record written 4 min ago reads `away`, 6 min ago reads `offline`, even though stored as `online`); the persisted `state` is retained only for the payload contract and debugging. Aligning the TTL to `AWAY_THRESHOLD_MS` lets Redis garbage-collect fully-offline users with no cron — a missing key IS `offline` by definition. A single GET/MGET keeps `getPresenceMap` a one-round-trip batch (Gate 9)                                                                                                                            | Read-time bucketing assumes reasonably-synced clocks across instances; a future timestamp (clock skew) is clamped to age 0 (online) via `Math.max(0, ...)`. The stored `state` can be stale relative to the live bucket by design — it is intentionally never trusted as the live value |
| `index.ts` calls `app.set('io', io)` immediately after constructing the Socket.io server + attaching the Redis adapter and BEFORE `registerSocketHandlers(io)` (`index.ts` L113), so REST routes resolve the emitter via `req.app.get('io')` (`messages.ts` `getIo`)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Pass `io` explicitly into each router factory; export a module-level `io` singleton; a dependency-injection container                                                                                                                                         | The CP4 CRITICAL C1: `POST /api/messages` and the reaction routes broadcast via `req.app.get('io')`, but bootstrap never registered it, so `getIo` returned `undefined` and every REST-origin broadcast threw. `app.set('io', io)` is the idiomatic Express way to share a singleton with routes without threading it through every factory; calling it AFTER adapter setup guarantees the stored instance is the adapter-backed one, and BEFORE handler registration guarantees it is present before the first request                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | `req.app.get('io')` is loosely typed (`any`), so `getIo` casts to the typed server; a missing `set('io')` would resurface as a runtime `undefined` — mitigated by this fixed bootstrap order and the single typed `getIo` accessor                                                      |
| On connection (`sockets/index.ts`) the socket always joins `user:<id>`, then `autoJoinAuthorizedRooms(socket)` resolves `listMemberChannelIds(userId)` + `listDmIds(userId)` and joins every `channel:<id>` / `dm:<id>` the user is authorized for; failures are logged and swallowed (degrade to "no auto-join", never drop the connection). Thread rooms are NOT auto-joined — they are joined on demand when a thread panel opens (`sockets/index.ts` L82-122, L154-160)                                                                                                                                          | Require the client to emit `channel:join` for every channel on load (chatty, race-prone); a global broadcast with client-side filtering (leaks data, defeats the ACL); auto-join thread rooms too (unbounded)                                                 | The CP4 CRITICAL realtime finding: room-targeted `message:new` / reaction / typing broadcasts reached nobody because clients never joined the rooms. Server-side auto-join on connect, gated by the SAME membership rule the REST ACL enforces, makes protected delivery work immediately with no client choreography and no data leak. Thread rooms stay on-demand because a user has potentially thousands of threads but views one panel at a time. Swallowing a join error keeps a transient DB blip from dropping the whole socket — the user simply misses live updates until reconnect                                                                                                                                                       | A channel joined AFTER connect (via the join mutation) is not auto-joined on the existing socket until the next reconnect; acceptable for the PoC and covered by the `channel.handler` `channel:join` event for the explicit-join path                                                  |
| Both the server (`index.ts` L92-95) and the client (`web/src/lib/socket.ts` L68-71) pin `transports: ['websocket']` — HTTP long-polling is removed from the transport list                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Keep the Socket.io default `['polling', 'websocket']` (the CP4 behaviour the review flagged as a Rule 2 violation); allow polling only as a fallback                                                                                                          | Rule 2 forbids polling outright. Pinning websocket-only on BOTH ends removes the long-polling handshake and the polling fallback, eliminating the HTTP-poll attack surface the security review flagged and guaranteeing every realtime byte travels over a single WebSocket. The two lists are kept identical so the handshake cannot negotiate down to polling                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | A network that blocks WebSocket upgrades (rare corporate proxies) cannot connect at all rather than degrading to polling; accepted as the explicit Rule 2 trade-off, with `connectionStateRecovery` plus the client reconnect logic covering transient drops                            |
| A new `typing.handler.ts` registers `typing:start` / `typing:stop` server listeners: validate the payload with `typingScopeSchema` (channel/DM XOR), enforce the channel/DM ACL via the now-exported `assertChannelAccess` / `assertDmAccess`, then re-broadcast with `socket.to(room)` (excluding the sender) stamping the server-trusted `socket.data.userId`; `assertChannelAccess` / `assertDmAccess` were exported from `messages.service.ts` for reuse                                                                                                                                                         | Leave typing unhandled (the CP4 gap — the client emitted into the void); broadcast to the whole room including the sender; trust the client-supplied `userId`; duplicate the ACL logic inside the handler                                                     | The CP4 review flagged that `typing:start`/`typing:stop` were declared in the shared contract and emitted by the client but had NO server handler. Reusing the message path's ACL (now exported) keeps ONE authorization rule for posting and typing; `socket.to(room)` reaches the other room members (the typist never sees their own indicator); taking `userId` from `socket.data` (not the payload) prevents a client spoofing "someone else is typing"                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Typing is fire-and-forget (no ack); a validation/ACL failure is logged at `warn` and the indicator simply not broadcast — the client's own 5 s inactivity timer clears any stale local indicator                                                                                        |
| SUPERSEDES the earlier "presence transition emitted to `io.to(userRoom(userId))` only" decision (the `presence.handler` row above): transitions now fan out via the new `broadcastPresenceUpdate(io, userId, update)`, which emits a single `presence:update` to the de-duplicated union of `user:<id>` + every `channel:<id>` the user is a member of + every `dm:<id>` they participate in; the disconnect handler builds an `offline` `PresenceUpdate` and calls the same helper after the last-socket `clearPresence` (`presence-broadcast.ts`; `presence.handler.ts` L126; `sockets/index.ts` disconnect block) | Keep the user-room-only emit plus rely solely on `getPresenceMap` hydration (the prior decision the CP4 review found insufficient — peers stayed stale); a global `io.emit` (leaks presence to unrelated users); iterate memberships inline at each call site | The CP4 MAJOR presence findings: updates reached only the changed user's own tabs (peers' sidebars stayed stale) and no `offline` event fired on disconnect. Fanning out to the user's authorized audience — resolved through the SAME membership rule the ACL uses, so presence never leaks to a stranger — makes every peer who shares a channel/DM reconcile live. Routing both the heartbeat-transition and the disconnect-offline paths through one helper keeps the audience rule in a single place. Initial `getPresenceMap` hydration (next row) still covers the join-before-first-transition gap                                                                                                                                          | Each transition now does a membership lookup (two service calls) instead of a bare emit; acceptable at PoC scale and bounded by transition-gating (only a real bucket change broadcasts, not every 30 s heartbeat)                                                                      |
| New `GET /api/presence?userIds=<csv>` route (auth required) validates `presenceQuerySchema` (comma-separated cuids, capped at `MAX_PRESENCE_QUERY_IDS`), returns `Record<userId, PresenceState>` resolved in a single Redis `MGET`, and logs the requested COUNT only (`presence.ts`; `presence.service.getPresenceMap`). Consumed by `useHydratePresence(userIds)` on mount                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | No hydration endpoint (the CP4 gap — peers defaulted offline until a live transition); a POST body of ids; per-user `GET /api/presence/:id` (N round-trips)                                                                                                   | The CP4 MAJOR client-hydration finding: with fan-out alone, a peer who had not transitioned since the viewer connected rendered as offline. A one-shot batch fetch on mount seeds the presence map for every visible sidebar/DM user, closing the gap before the first live event. `MGET` resolves the whole batch in one round-trip (Gate 9); logging only the count keeps user ids out of the logs (Gate 10 privacy)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Hydration is a point-in-time snapshot; staleness between mount and the first live event is bounded by how quickly the heartbeat/transition stream takes over — sub-heartbeat in practice                                                                                                |
| New `GET /api/users?q=<text>` route (auth required) validates `userSearchQuerySchema`, returns `PublicUser[]` (NO email) ordered by `displayName`, EXCLUDES the caller, and logs query LENGTH + result count only; backs `StartDmDialog`'s people picker (`users.ts`; `users.service.searchUsers`). Mounting it and `/api/presence` grew the routes barrel from seven to nine sub-routers, inserted alphabetically                                                                                                                                                                                                   | No endpoint (the CP4 gap — `StartDmDialog` called a nonexistent `/api/users` and the DM-start flow was dead); search by email; include the caller; return the full `User` (leaks `passwordHash`/email)                                                        | The CP4 MAJOR contract finding: `StartDmDialog` searched `/api/users?q=` but no users router existed. The new route returns the privacy-safe `PublicUser` shape (email is never searched or returned), excludes the caller (you cannot DM yourself), and logs only the query length (the query is a person's name — PII). This also updates the earlier Routes-barrel "seven sub-routers" note to nine                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Substring `displayName` match is case-insensitive via `toLowerCase` (locale-agnostic) and unpaginated beyond the result cap; sufficient for the PoC people picker, extendable to cursor pagination later                                                                                |
| `auth.service.verifyToken` now classifies the `jwt.verify` failure: `jwt.TokenExpiredError` → `UnauthorizedError('Token has expired', 'token_expired')`, checked BEFORE `jwt.JsonWebTokenError` → `UnauthorizedError('Invalid authentication token', 'token_invalid')`, with any non-JWT error falling through to a generic codeless 401; `UnauthorizedError` gained an optional `code` argument (`auth.service.ts` L124-159)                                                                                                                                                                                        | Keep the single generic `UnauthorizedError` for all failures (the CP4 behaviour the review flagged — `token_invalid`/`token_expired` were unreachable); check `JsonWebTokenError` first; map codes in the route instead of the service                        | The CP4 MAJOR auth-semantics finding: collapsing every `jwt.verify` error into a generic `UnauthorizedError` made the `token_expired` vs `token_invalid` codes the client needs (silent re-login vs hard logout) unreachable. `TokenExpiredError` extends `JsonWebTokenError`, so it MUST be checked first or the broader guard shadows it (the same ordering already recorded for the error-handler's `instanceof` chain). The message stays generic (no leak of which check failed) while the `code` carries the machine-readable signal; this is the service-layer source of the codes the error-handler maps to HTTP                                                                                                                            | None of note — the codes are additive (optional `code` argument), the verifier's public return type is unchanged, and the HTTP shape is unchanged for the non-JWT fallback                                                                                                              |
| PII-free logging: `email` was removed from the register-success and login-success `req.log` lines (`userId` only); the file-upload route logs `fileId` + `sizeBytes` + `mimeType` and DROPS the user-supplied `originalName` (`routes/auth.ts` L57-82; `routes/files.ts` L87-97). `originalName` is still used for the `Content-Disposition` download filename — that is a header, not a log                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Keep `email` in auth logs and `originalName` in upload logs for traceability (the CP4 behaviour the security review flagged)                                                                                                                                  | The CP4 MAJOR/MINOR privacy findings (Gate 10 + the security checklist forbid PII in logs): an email is PII and a user-supplied filename can embed personal/project information. `userId` is the durable, non-PII correlator that joins to the user record when needed; `fileId` is the durable correlator for an upload. This extends the CP3 auth-service PII removal to the ROUTE layer (a distinct log site) and to file uploads                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Slightly less human-readable logs; correlation now requires a `userId`/`fileId` join, which operators already perform                                                                                                                                                                   |
| `GET /api/health` now returns `{ ok, api, postgres, redis, infrastructure }` and responds 200 when `ok` else 503: `api` is `'ok'` by definition (the process is serving the response), `postgres`/`redis` come from liveness probes, and `infrastructure` is the `postgres && redis` aggregate (the Docker-services readiness signal `make local` blocks on) (`routes/health.ts`)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Keep the prior `{ ok, postgres, redis }` shape (the CP4 contract the review flagged as missing the api/Docker fields); a single boolean; separate `/health/live` and `/health/ready` endpoints                                                                | The CP4 MINOR AAP-contract finding: the prompt's health example required readiness for Docker, Postgres, Redis, AND the API. Adding an explicit `api` field (trivially `ok` when reachable) and an `infrastructure` aggregate (the Docker-provisioned backing services) satisfies the literal contract and gives `make local` a single field to gate seeding/browser-open on. The 503-on-failure lets orchestrators treat the endpoint as a real readiness probe                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | `api` is always `ok` when the endpoint responds (it cannot report its own hard-down state); acceptable — an unreachable API is observable by the request itself failing, the standard liveness semantics                                                                                |
| New `lib/session.ts` exports `performLogout()` which calls `useAuthStore.getState().logout()` THEN `disconnectSocket()`; both the api-client 401 interceptor (`api-client.ts` L177-185) and `useAuth.logout` route through it, so clearing the token and dropping the WebSocket always happen together; `useAuth` additionally gained `/me` self-refresh backed by `GET /api/auth/me` (`session.ts`; `api-client.ts`; `useAuth.ts`)                                                                                                                                                                                  | Keep the api-client 401 handler calling the raw store `logout()` only (the CP4 behaviour the review flagged — the comment claimed the socket disconnected but it did not); a global event bus; duplicate the teardown in each caller                          | The CP4 MAJOR session-cleanup finding: the 401 path cleared the auth store but left the authenticated socket connected (a half-logged-out state where the WebSocket kept streaming with a now-invalid identity). Centralizing the teardown in one `performLogout()` makes the store-clear and socket-disconnect atomic from the caller's view and removes the drift between the comment and the behaviour. Adding `/me` self-refresh lets a persisted session be verified on reload and cleared on a 401 through the same orchestrated path                                                                                                                                                                                                         | A 401 from the login endpoint itself also runs `performLogout`, harmless because the store is already logged-out (`logout` is idempotent) and the socket is not yet connected                                                                                                           |
| `useMessages` now subscribes to `reaction:added` and `reaction:removed` (in addition to `message:new`), patching the target message's `reactions` array across every cached page via `queryClient.setQueryData`; `hasCurrentUser` is recomputed against the viewer and `reaction:removed` flatMaps the reactor out of the `userIds` (`useMessages.ts` L228-243)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Ignore reaction broadcasts (the CP4 gap — reactions never updated live); invalidate/refetch the whole timeline on each reaction (latency, defeats the budget); a separate reaction cache                                                                      | The CP4 MAJOR cache-integration finding: the server emitted reaction events but the web cache consumed only `message:new`, so a reaction added by another user never appeared. An in-place `setQueryData` patch (mirroring the `message:new` approach) re-renders subscribers with zero round-trips, holding the realtime budget (Gate 9) and honouring Rule 2 (no polling). Recomputing `hasCurrentUser` against the current viewer keeps the "you reacted" highlight correct on every client                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | A cache/server divergence on a rare reconnect race has no auto-reconciliation; recoverable by a remount/refetch, acceptable for the PoC                                                                                                                                                 |
| `MessageComposer` always POSTs to the single `/api/messages` endpoint with the validated `sendMessageSchema` body `{ content, channelId, dmId, parentId, fileId }`; the form `defaultValues` carry the scope and the server derives channel/DM/thread routing from the body (`MessageComposer.tsx` L147-154)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Keep posting to the computed per-scope endpoints `/api/channels/:id/messages`, `/api/dms/:id/messages`, `/api/messages/:parentId/replies` (the CP4 behaviour the review flagged — those write routes do not exist); add those routes to the backend           | The CP4 CRITICAL frontend-backend contract finding: the composer wrote to three nonexistent endpoints, so EVERY message send 404'd. The backend exposes exactly ONE write route (`POST /api/messages`) that derives scope from the body, so the fix is to always hit it with the shared schema's body — keeping one write contract for channel posts, DM posts, and thread replies, and reusing the single `sendMessageSchema` both sides validate (AAP §0.8.4 single source of validation)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | None — the body-routed contract is the backend's actual shape; the shared Zod XOR refinement guarantees exactly one of `channelId`/`dmId` is present (`parentId` is additive for thread mode)                                                                                           |
| `useChannels` query is typed `ChannelSummary[]` (matching the backend `GET /api/channels`) and gains the canonical mutations `useCreateChannel` (→ `Channel`), `useJoinChannel` (→ `Channel`), `useLeaveChannel` (→ `{ ok: true }`), each invalidating `['channels']`; `CreateChannelDialog` uses `useCreateChannel` typed to the base `Channel` DTO (NOT `ChannelWithMembers`) (`useChannels.ts`; `CreateChannelDialog.tsx`)                                                                                                                                                                                        | Keep the read-only hook typed `ChannelWithMembers[]` (the CP4 drift the review flagged — the backend returns `ChannelSummary[]`); have the backend return a hydrated shape; keep mutations scattered in components                                            | The CP4 MAJOR contract findings: the hook asserted `ChannelWithMembers[]` while the backend returned `ChannelSummary[]` (a typecheck-passing lie), and the create dialog expected `ChannelWithMembers` while `POST /api/channels` returns a base `Channel`. Aligning the client generics to the ACTUAL backend shapes removes the drift, and consolidating create/join/leave into named mutation hooks that invalidate the one `['channels']` key gives a single read/write contract                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | `memberCount` is unavailable from the list endpoint (`ChannelSummary` omits it), deferred to a future channel-detail endpoint returning `ChannelWithMembers` — already noted in the channels-service row above                                                                          |
| `SearchResponse` `{ results: MessageWithAuthor[]; query: string }` was added to `@app/shared/types/message.ts` as the single source of truth; `SearchResultsList` types the call `apiClient.get<SearchResponse>(...)` and reads `data?.results`, not a bare array (`shared/types/message.ts` L168; `SearchResultsList.tsx`)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Type the call as `MessageWithAuthor[]` and read `data ?? []` (the CP4 behaviour the review flagged — the backend returns the `{ results, query }` wrapper); declare a local response type in the web component                                                | The CP4 MAJOR contract finding: the backend search route returns `{ results, query }` but the frontend treated the response as a bare array, so results never rendered. Promoting the response shape to the shared package (AAP §0.8.4 single source of truth) lets both the API route and the web consumer reference one interface, and reading `data?.results` matches the actual wire shape                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | None — `SearchResponse` derives from the existing `MessageWithAuthor`, so a change to the message DTO propagates once                                                                                                                                                                   |
| New `components/ui/checkbox.tsx` is a native-backed `Checkbox`: a real `<input type="checkbox">` styled `appearance-none` with an overlaid lucide `Check` revealed via `peer-checked`, NOT `@radix-ui/react-checkbox` (which is not installed in this offline workspace); it forwards `checked`/`onChange`/`onBlur`/`name`/`ref` so it is drop-in for react-hook-form, and `CreateChannelDialog` uses it for the `isPrivate` toggle (`checkbox.tsx`; `CreateChannelDialog.tsx`)                                                                                                                                      | Keep the native `<input>` the dialog used before (the CP4 MINOR design-system gap the review flagged); add `@radix-ui/react-checkbox` (unavailable offline, would fail install); use a `Switch`                                                               | The CP4 MINOR finding: the create-channel dialog used a raw native checkbox while the rest of the UI composes shadcn primitives. shadcn ships `Checkbox` on Radix, which is not in this workspace, so a native-backed primitive preserves the shadcn look and prop surface while staying fully accessible (native focus/keyboard/label association) and react-hook-form compatible — the same owned-source philosophy as the rest of `components/ui/`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Diverges from upstream shadcn's Radix-based `Checkbox`, so a future shadcn upgrade is not a drop-in CLI re-add; documented as an intentional offline adaptation (mirrors the Sonner Vite-adaptation precedent)                                                                          |

Markdown-marker formatting on the existing `Textarea` gives real, working formatting behaviour with no new editor-framework dependency, matching Slack's markdown-style composer; restoring the selection after the programmatic edit keeps the caret/highlight where the user expects so successive formats compose naturally                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Markdown markers are a lighter-weight model than a full WYSIWYG editor (no inline rendered styling in the input); acceptable for the PoC composer and upgradeable to Tiptap/Lexical later if rich preview is needed                                                                     |

## QA remediation — Incremental #1 (Milestone A — API Operational)

Consolidated record of the decisions made while resolving the Incremental-#1 QA report (1 Critical, 1 Major, 3 Minor). Each row documents a non-trivial fix per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3); behaviour is otherwise unchanged from the checkpoint baseline.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `middleware/upload.ts` calls `mkdirSync(env.FILE_UPLOAD_PATH, { recursive: true })` ONCE at module load, before configuring multer `diskStorage`, so the upload destination always exists; `.gitignore` additionally ignores the runtime-created `packages/api/uploads/` (the path the API resolves under its own CWD via `make local`, and which `make clean` already removes) | Create the directory only in the server bootstrap (`index.ts`); a Make or postinstall step; an absolute default path; commit a `packages/api/uploads/.gitkeep`                                                                  | QA #1 CRITICAL: with the shipped `FILE_UPLOAD_PATH=./uploads` and the API process CWD at `packages/api`, the resolved `packages/api/uploads` did not exist (only a repo-root `uploads/.gitkeep` was committed), so multer threw `ENOENT` and EVERY `POST /api/files` returned 500. Creating it at module load is idempotent, independent of CWD, and covers both the server and the Jest/supertest suites (which import the middleware directly) without a separate bootstrap step                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | A read-only or unwritable `FILE_UPLOAD_PATH` makes `mkdirSync` throw at module load (fail-fast — the desired signal that the path is misconfigured); none for the PoC local filesystem                                                                                                                            |
| The `validate` middleware writes the parsed query/params back with `Object.defineProperty(req, target, { value, writable: true, enumerable: true, configurable: true })` via an `applyValidated` helper, replacing `Object.assign(req.query, …)` and `Object.assign(req.params, …)`                                                                                             | Keep `Object.assign` (the broken behaviour); assign `req.query = parsed` (throws — Express 5 exposes a getter-only); store the parsed value on a side channel such as `req.validatedQuery` and rewrite every handler to read it | QA #2 MAJOR: in Express 5 `req.query` is a lazily-recomputed GETTER, so `Object.assign(req.query, …)` mutates a throwaway object and the transformed value is discarded — a standalone probe confirmed the presence `userIds` string→string[] and the pagination `limit` string→number coercions were BOTH lost, leaving handlers with the raw strings. `GET /api/presence` then called `userIds.map` on a string and returned 500. Defining an own configurable data property shadows the prototype getter so the parsed value persists; centralizing it in the middleware fixes every transforming query schema at once and removes the latent fragility that only let pagination work by accidental `Math.floor("50")` re-coercion | Redefining `req.query`/`req.params` replaces the value for the remainder of the request (intended); routes with NO query/params schema keep Express's native getter untouched. Verified across all consumers (presence, search, users, messages, dms, channels) that none rely on the post-validate native getter |
| The error-handler `ValidationError` branch now includes the `details` (`error.flatten().fieldErrors`) the `validate` middleware attached; `ErrorPayload.details` was widened to also accept the field→messages map shape                                                                                                                                                        | Leave `details` dropped (the broken behaviour — the computed field errors were never returned); have `validate` throw a raw `ZodError` so the existing ZodError branch formats it; reformat the record into a flat issue array  | QA #3 MINOR / AAP Gate 12: the middleware computed per-field errors but the `ValidationError` branch omitted them, so `POST /api/auth/register` with a short password returned a 400 with no indication of which field failed. Surfacing `err.details` returns the field-keyed feedback the code already produced; the conditional spread mirrors the existing `UnauthorizedError` `code` pattern and omits the key when a service throws a bare `ValidationError` with no field detail                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Request-validation 400s carry the field→messages map while a raw `ZodError` (env/response validation) carries the `{path,message,code}[]` list — two detail shapes under one key; acceptable because each is self-describing and the request-validation path is the dominant client-facing case                   |
| `searchMessages` restricts hits to channels the caller is a member of or DMs they participate in; the public-channel `OR` clause was removed from the raw-SQL ACL (membership-only search)                                                                                                                                                                                      | Keep public-channel inclusion and add a deviation row plus correct the line-342 invariant; gate public inclusion behind a feature flag                                                                                          | QA #4 MINOR / Explainability: the prior SQL also admitted any non-private channel, so a non-member saw public-channel hits — contradicting AAP §0.6.2 ("users only see hits from channels they belong to or DMs they participate in"), AAP §0.1.1 ("ACL-filtered by the requesting user's channel and DM membership"), AND this log's own search-service invariant. Per the AAP-precedence rule the correct resolution is to make the code membership-only, which simultaneously realigns it with §0.6.2 and the existing invariant (no contradiction remains) and matches the channel-membership ACL already enforced on the timeline, thread, and reaction paths                                                                    | A user must JOIN a public channel before its messages become searchable; this matches the Slack-style membership model and the rest of the channel ACL. Private-channel hiding (covenant #156) is unchanged — non-members still see zero private hits                                                             |
| The error-handler maps body-parser `entity.*` errors to their parser-assigned 4xx status — 400 for `entity.parse.failed` (malformed JSON), 413 for `entity.too.large` (oversized body) — instead of letting them reach the generic 500                                                                                                                                          | Leave them as 500 (the broken behaviour); match only `err instanceof SyntaxError` (would miss `entity.too.large` and risk catching genuine application SyntaxErrors); hardcode 400 for every body-parser failure                | QA #5 MINOR / HTTP semantics: malformed JSON to any endpoint returned 500 even though `express.json()` already attaches `type:'entity.parse.failed'` and `status:400`; a client-triggerable 500 pollutes 5xx error-rate monitoring. Matching only a string `type` that begins with `entity.` (a marker no application code sets) and honouring the numeric 4xx status returns the semantically-correct client-error code while leaving genuine application `SyntaxError`s as 500                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Relies on body-parser's stable `type`/`status` fields; if a future body-parser release renamed them the branch would stop matching and the error would fall back to the safe 500 default                                                                                                                          |

## `packages/api` — Test infrastructure helpers (`test/setup.ts`)

`test/setup.ts` is the shared Jest helper module imported by every `packages/api/test/*.test.ts` integration suite; it is not matched by `testMatch` and is loaded only via an explicit `import './setup.js'`. Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3); the cross-cutting `@app/*`-scope reconciliation lives in the Decision-log format section.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                    | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Integration suites run against the SAME `slack_dev` Postgres instance as local dev (the `DATABASE_URL` already in `packages/api/.env`), with `cleanDatabase()` truncating all eight tables in each suite's `beforeEach`, rather than provisioning a dedicated `slack_dev_test` database                                                                                                | A separate test database; an in-memory `pg-mem`/SQLite; a per-test transaction rolled back in `afterEach`                                    | For a single-stack PoC the committed migrations already define the schema, so aggressive per-test cleanup yields isolation without the create + `prisma migrate deploy` + teardown ceremony a second database needs, and it matches the `make local` environment exactly (AAP Decision #1)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | A run pointed at a populated dev DB will DELETE its rows; mitigated because `cleanDatabase()` only fires inside the Jest lifecycle and CI is expected to override `DATABASE_URL` to a throwaway database                                                                           |
| No `.env.test` file; suites reuse `packages/api/.env` and force the profile with `process.env.NODE_ENV ??= 'test'` as the FIRST statement of `setup.ts`, before any import that triggers `config/env.ts`'s `loadDotenv()`                                                                                                                                                              | A dedicated `.env.test` with its own `DATABASE_URL`/`REDIS_URL`; a `dotenv-cli`-injected env; hardcoding the test env in `jest.config.ts`    | `env.ts` validates at module load, so the override MUST precede the first deep import; making it the literal first statement guarantees that because `setup.ts` is the import root of every suite, and it keeps config identical to `make local` (AAP Decision #2). The statement-before-imports ordering is lint-safe — the flat config ships no `eslint-plugin-import`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Same dev-DB blast radius as the row above; the `??=` preserves any externally supplied `NODE_ENV` (e.g. a CI value) instead of clobbering it                                                                                                                                       |
| `registerUser()` performs a real `POST /api/auth/register` through supertest and returns the live `{ token, user }` body; it NEVER calls `prisma.user.create`, and `loginUser()` likewise drives `POST /api/auth/login`                                                                                                                                                                | Insert via `prismaTest.user.create` and synthesise a token; build a synthetic `User` from the input; return only the token                   | Rule 4 is absolute — test users MUST be born through the registration HTTP flow — and returning the live response hands tests the real Prisma-generated CUID `user.id` and the exact server-issued token, eliminating drift between a hand-built object and the wire shape (AAP Decision #3)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | The helper is coupled to the `/api/auth/register` response shape, so a shape change ripples to every suite; mitigated by `setup.ts` being the single constructor of `RegisteredUser`                                                                                               |
| `cleanDatabase()` issues eight ordered `deleteMany()` calls — `messageReaction` → `message` → `channelMember` → `channel` → `dMParticipant` → `directMessage` → `file` → `user` — instead of raw `TRUNCATE … CASCADE`, and `clearUploadsDirectory()` wipes the CONTENTS of `FILE_UPLOAD_PATH` while keeping the directory                                                              | A single `TRUNCATE TABLE … RESTART IDENTITY CASCADE`; a `prisma.$transaction([...])` batch; deleting the uploads directory itself            | `deleteMany` is type-safe and honours FK constraints when ordered child→parent (the order is read off `schema.prisma`; note Prisma maps the `DMParticipant` model to the `dMParticipant` delegate — only the first character lower-cases), and the perf gap vs `TRUNCATE` is negligible at PoC scale; recreating-but-keeping the uploads dir means multer's destination always exists (AAP Decision #4)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Slower than `TRUNCATE` on large datasets (immaterial here); the explicit order must gain an entry whenever a new FK-bearing model is added, or `beforeEach` will surface a FK violation                                                                                            |
| `closeTestResources()` is guarded by a module-level `resourcesClosed` flag (early-return on re-entry) and swallows disconnect failures with `.catch(() => undefined)` on both `prisma.$disconnect()` and `disconnectRedisClients()`                                                                                                                                                    | Strict teardown that rethrows; no idempotency guard; closing each Redis client individually from the suite                                   | Every suite calls it in `afterAll`, so a forgiving, idempotent teardown stops a secondary disconnect error from masking the real test failure and makes a defensive double-call a safe no-op (AAP Decision #5)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | A genuine disconnect failure is silenced (possible handle leak); mitigated because Node reclaims sockets on process exit and `--detectOpenHandles` is run during validation to catch real leaks                                                                                    |
| `cachedApp` and `createTestApp()` are typed `Application` (not `Express`), the app is lazily memoised via `cachedApp ??= createApp()` (never built at module load), and supertest's `any` `response.body` is narrowed with a WHOLE-OBJECT assertion (`response.body as RegisteredUser`/`as Channel`/`as DirectMessage`)                                                                | Type the app `Express` (the schema's wording); eagerly construct the app at import; assert per field such as `response.body.token as string` | `createApp()` returns the Express 5 `Application` type while `Express` is a distinct request-callable interface, so `Application` is the assignable annotation and still satisfies supertest's `RequestListener`-shaped parameter; lazy memoisation leaves the app un-built in suites that never request it and is parallel-safe (Express apps are stateless per request); the test-file ESLint block relaxes only `no-explicit-any`/`no-console` while the `no-unsafe-*` rules stay ON, so one whole-object cast launders the `any` whereas per-field casts trip `no-unsafe-member-access`                                                                            | A whole-object cast trusts the payload matches the DTO at runtime; acceptable because the same shared Zod schemas validate these payloads server-side and the integration suite exercises the real shapes                                                                          |
| The assigned file's printed "Required File Content" was adapted four ways: (a) the unused `randomUUID` import was DROPPED (only `randomBytes` is used), (b) workspace imports use the `@app/*` scope, (c) `@app/shared/*` subpath imports carry NO `.js` extension while relative `../src/*.js` imports keep it, and (d) the JWT `expiresIn` is asserted `as SignOptions['expiresIn']` | Keep the literal seed verbatim: `randomUUID` imported, `@blitzy-slack/*` scope, `.js` on shared subpaths, and an un-narrowed `expiresIn`     | Each literal breaks the strict build (Rule 3): an unused `randomUUID` fails `noUnusedLocals`/`no-unused-vars`; `@blitzy-slack/*` resolves to no package (the workspace is `@app/*` — see the Decision-log format reconciliation and the `moduleNameMapper` rows); `.js` on `@app/shared` subpaths fails `tsc` because the package `exports` map points `./types/*` and `./constants/*` at the `.ts` sources (the no-`.js` subpath convention every sibling uses); and jsonwebtoken@9 types `expiresIn` as a narrow `StringValue \| number`, so a validated free-form duration string needs the same single assertion the auth service uses — `@ts-ignore` is forbidden | A future monorepo rescope must update every `@app/*` specifier together and a malformed `JWT_EXPIRES_IN` fails at sign time; otherwise none functional — these are the conventions already used across the codebase, verified by module `tsc --noEmit` + `eslint --max-warnings 0` |

## `packages/web` — Message list timeline (`src/components/messages/MessageList.tsx`)

`MessageList` is the scrollable, infinite-paginated, real-time timeline rendered inside a channel or DM (and, via `messagesOverride`, the thread panel). The decisions below are non-trivial per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3); the data-ordering contract they build on is recorded in the _Message timeline hook_ and _Messages service_ rows.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The live timeline is rendered by reversing the hook's array — `[...hookResult.messages].reverse()` inside a `useMemo` — so the oldest message sits at the top and the newest at the bottom; the `messagesOverride` (thread-reply) path is rendered as-is because it already arrives oldest-first | Trust the assigned-file prompt's literal comment that `useMessages` returns "oldest → newest" and render the array directly; render with CSS `flex-direction: column-reverse`; change `useMessages` to return ascending order | The implemented `useMessages` returns messages NEWEST-first (it prepends each `message:new` to `pages[0]` and the API paginates newest-first — see the _Message timeline hook_ and _Messages service_ rows), so rendering directly would invert Slack's chronological order. Reversing a shallow copy in `useMemo` leaves the source array immutable (preserving TanStack Query cache identity), composes cleanly with the day-boundary separator grouping, and corrects the assigned-file prompt's inaccurate "oldest → newest" comment — an explicit deviation logged here. `column-reverse` was rejected because it flips paint order but not DOM/AT reading order and fights the separator insertion | Recomputed whenever the message-array identity changes; negligible at the 50-per-page size and memoised. A future switch to an ascending hook would require removing this reversal — guarded by the ad-hoc render test that asserts oldest-at-top ordering |
| The zero-message state renders the shadcn `Empty` primitive (centered `MessageSquareText` in `EmptyMedia variant="icon"` + `EmptyTitle` + `EmptyDescription`), with the channel/DM-specific welcome text supplied by the parent through the `emptyLabel` prop (defaulting to "No messages yet")  | Hard-code a left-aligned "Welcome to the #channel" hero replicating screenshot 29 pixel-for-pixel inside `MessageList`; bespoke empty markup instead of the `Empty` primitive                                                 | AAP §0.5.2 maps the empty channel state to the shadcn `Empty` primitive and the assigned-file prompt mandates "using shadcn `Empty`", so the design-system component takes precedence over Slack's literal hero layout (DS conflict-resolution hierarchy). Taking the welcome string via `emptyLabel` keeps `MessageList` scope-agnostic — one component serves channels, DMs and the thread panel — letting the `Channel` page pass "Welcome to the #&lt;name&gt; channel" while a DM or thread passes its own copy                                                                                                                                                                                     | The centered `Empty` layout differs from Slack's left-aligned welcome block; accepted as the design-system-compliant reading. If a parent omits `emptyLabel`, the generic "No messages yet" shows instead of channel-specific copy — an acceptable default |
| `DateSeparator` exposes its day label as visible pill text only — it does NOT set `role="separator"`/`aria-label`, the decorative divider line carries `aria-hidden`, and the separator omits Slack's interactive date-dropdown chevron                                                          | Apply `role="separator"` + `aria-label={label}` as sketched in the assigned-file prompt; render the chevron "jump to date" affordance visible in screenshots 29/100                                                           | An ARIA `separator` is a leaf role whose descendant text is not surfaced to assistive tech, so labelling the pill as a separator would HIDE the very date it announces; leaving the date as ordinary readable text keeps it in the accessibility tree while the line stays decorative (`aria-hidden`). The chevron drives "jump to date", which the assigned-file prompt lists under Out of Scope, so it is intentionally not built for the PoC                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | No machine-readable "separator" semantic between day groups; immaterial because the date text itself is the meaningful, readable boundary.
