Re-introducing jump-to-date later is additive                                                                   |

## `packages/api` — Socket.io integration tests (`test/socket.test.ts`)

`test/socket.test.ts` is the Jest + `socket.io-client` integration suite for the real-time WebSocket layer: JWT handshake, room subscription, message/reaction/presence/typing handlers, dual-broadcast thread semantics, transition-only presence, and multi-tab disconnect safety. It boots a real Node HTTP server plus a typed `socket.io` server wired to the production `registerSocketHandlers`. Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                         | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The test IO server wires the REAL Redis adapter via `io.adapter(createAdapter(pubClient, subClient))` (the `pubClient`/`subClient` re-exported from `test/setup.ts`), not Socket.io's default in-memory adapter                                                                                                                                                       | The default in-memory adapter for tests; a mocked Redis pub/sub                                                                                   | Rule 2 mandates `@socket.io/redis-adapter`; wiring the SAME adapter the production `index.ts` uses makes the suite validate the real cross-instance broadcast path end-to-end and surfaces any Redis-specific race, and the Docker-Compose Redis is already running for local dev. `redisClient.flushdb()` in `beforeEach` clears presence/adapter keys so adapter state cannot leak across tests                                                                                                                                                 | Tests require Redis up (provided by `make up`/Docker) and run marginally slower than in-memory; both accepted for production fidelity                                                                          |
| `socket.io-client`'s `io()` is invoked with ZERO type arguments and the typed event maps are applied through the receiving `const`'s `ClientConn` (= `Socket<ServerToClientEvents, ClientToServerEvents>`) annotation; the client generic order is INVERTED relative to the server (`<S2C, C2S>` on the client vs `<C2S, S2C, Inter, Data>` on the server)            | Pass the maps as call generics `io<ServerToClientEvents, ClientToServerEvents>(url, opts)` (the assigned-file seed sketch); cast the bare result  | socket.io-client 4.8.3's exported `lookup` overloads declare zero type parameters, so a call-site generic fails the strict build with `TS2558 Expected 0 type arguments`; annotating the receiving variable is the documented socket.io-client typing approach and a bare `Socket` (`DefaultEventsMap`) is assignable to the parameterised `Socket`. The inverted generic order is the §0.8.4 client/server asymmetry — getting it wrong silently disables event-name/payload type-checking                                                       | A socket.io-client major that re-introduces call generics would shift the pattern; the pinned `^4.8.0` range holds the contract, and `@ts-ignore` is forbidden so the annotation is the only strict-safe route |
| `socket.io-client` `^4.8.0` was added to `packages/api`'s `devDependencies`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Rely on pnpm hoisting the client from `packages/web`; declare it as a root devDependency                                                          | The suite imports `socket.io-client` directly and pnpm's isolated `node_modules` resolves a specifier only against the importing package's own manifest, so it MUST be a declared dependency of `@app/api`; it is test-only, hence `devDependencies`; the `^4.8.0` range matches the server's `socket.io` `4.8.x` for wire/protocol compatibility                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Any other workspace importing the client must declare it too (no implicit hoist under pnpm strictness); accepted as the correct, explicit dependency model                                                     |
| Presence-propagation and last-tab-offline tests make the OBSERVER a co-member of a shared channel and have the observer explicitly `CHANNEL_JOIN` (awaiting the ack) before the subject's heartbeat/disconnect, rather than asserting that any connected client receives a global presence broadcast                                                                  | Trust the assigned-file seed's assumption that presence uses `io.emit(...)` to every connected client and assert receipt on an unrelated observer | The implemented `broadcastPresenceUpdate` is TARGETED — it emits to `io.to([userRoom(subject), …subject's member channels, …subject's DMs])`, NOT globally — so an observer that shares no room with the subject never receives the update; reproducing the real audience requires a shared channel the observer has joined. The subject still receives its OWN transition via its always-joined `userRoom`, so subject-side assertions need no extra setup. This is an explicit deviation from the seed, logged here per the Explainability rule | If presence were later made global the shared-channel setup becomes redundant (harmless); these tests now pin the targeted-audience contract, so a regression to a narrower audience is caught                 |
| Asynchronous receipt is asserted by a per-event `waitForEvent` helper (Promise + own `setTimeout` reject, default 2000 ms, per-call overridable); positive assertions are strictly event-driven and never poll, while the two NEGATIVE "silence" assertions (no broadcast on same-state heartbeat; no offline on single-tab disconnect) use a short fixed wait window | Rely on Jest's global `testTimeout`; poll the adapter/room state in a loop                                                                        | A per-event timeout names the exact missing event and fails fast and locally instead of stalling the whole test to the global timeout; same-instance room delivery is synchronous so event-driven receipt is deterministic. "Absence of an event" cannot be awaited, so the negative cases necessarily sample a short window                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | An overloaded CI could make a tight per-event budget flaky; mitigated by generous defaults and explicit longer overrides for the Gate-9 presence (5500 ms) and last-tab-offline (6000 ms) cases                |
| The suite does NOT capture or assert Pino log lines; Gate 10 is verified indirectly (handlers run without crashing and produce the correct wire behaviour)                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Redirect/parse stdout and assert structured log fields (`reqId`/`socketId`/`userId`/`event`)                                                      | stdout capture of the shared Pino singleton is brittle and ordering-dependent under `--runInBand`, and the logger configuration is unit-tested in isolation; Gate 10's requirement that every socket event is logged is met by the handlers calling the logger, while THIS suite's job is to prove the handlers behave correctly end-to-end                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Lower direct log-assertion coverage in this suite; mitigated by the dedicated logger unit tests                                                                                                                |
| `afterAll` inserts a 250 ms drain delay between `stopTestSocketServer()` and `closeTestResources()`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Tear resources down immediately after closing the server; await each server-side disconnect handler from the test                                 | `io.close()` fires the server's async disconnect handlers (presence-cleanup Prisma queries) which otherwise race `prisma.$disconnect()` and emit benign "Response from the Engine was empty" error logs; a short drain lets them settle for clean teardown. The handlers are server-internal, so the suite cannot await them individually                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Adds 250 ms per suite (negligible) and a pathologically slow handler could still race (not observed); acceptable for the PoC                                                                                   |
| Non-user preconditions — `ChannelMember`, parent `Message`, and seeded `MessageReaction` rows — are arranged with direct `prismaTest` writes, while USERS are created ONLY through `registerUser()` (`POST /api/auth/register`)                                                                                                                                       | Drive every precondition through the REST or socket layers                                                                                        | Rule 4 governs USER creation only; channel membership, parent messages, and seeded reactions are plain fixtures, so a direct Prisma write is the least-coupled, most deterministic way to set them up, and cross-protocol REST orchestration is flaky here because the WS server's port exposes no Express app. The REST membership/message/reaction service paths are covered by `channels.test.ts`/`messages.test.ts`                                                                                                                           | Bypasses the service layer for those fixtures; mitigated because the dedicated REST suites exercise those services directly                                                                                    |

## `packages/api` — Full-text search integration tests (`test/search.test.ts`)

`test/search.test.ts` is the Jest + supertest integration suite for the single search endpoint `GET /api/search?q=` — full-text `tsvector` matching, `ts_rank` ordering, ACL filtering by the caller's channel membership and DM participation, Gate 12 query validation, Gate 9 latency, tsvector normalization/stemming, and SQL-injection defense. Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The "public channel" ACL tests assert an outsider who has NOT joined a PUBLIC channel sees ZERO results, and a separate positive test JOINs the channel via `POST /api/channels/:id/join` before asserting the message becomes visible — DEVIATING from the assigned-file seed's "returns public channel messages even to non-members" (which expected length 1)                   | Encode the seed verbatim (assert non-members can search public channels); omit the join-then-visible test                                                                            | The implemented `search.service.ts` ACL is membership-gated — `m."channelId" IN (caller's ChannelMember rows) OR m."dmId" IN (caller's DMParticipant rows)` with NO public-channel exemption (the service comment states public channels the caller has not joined are NOT searchable until joined) — so the seed assertion would FAIL against the real code; the suite must pin the REAL contract, and the deviation is logged here per §0.8.3                                                                                                                                                       | If search is later widened to expose unjoined public channels this test must flip to expect visibility; the join-then-visible positive case still documents the membership boundary and would catch a silent ACL widening             |
| Test USERS are created only through `registerUser()` (`POST /api/auth/register`, Rule 4); message/channel/DM CONTENT is seeded with direct `prismaTest.message.create`/`createMany` rather than `POST /api/messages`                                                                                                                                                               | Drive every message through the REST or socket layer                                                                                                                                 | Rule 4 governs USER creation only; messages are read-fixtures for a READ-only endpoint, so direct inserts are the least-coupled, most deterministic setup and keep the 500-row Gate-9 seed fast. `Message.contentTsv` is `GENERATED ALWAYS AS (to_tsvector('english', content)) STORED`, so direct inserts auto-populate the search vector — no trigger is bypassed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Relies on the GENERATED column staying materialized (guaranteed by migration `add_message_tsvector`); a hypothetical switch to a trigger-populated vector would require routing seeds through the triggering path                     |
| `supertest`'s `any`-typed `response.body` is narrowed with a single WHOLE-OBJECT cast `as SearchResponse`, and result assertions use direct TYPED property access (`body.results[0].content`, `match.author.id`, `match.author.displayName`) instead of jest's `expect.stringContaining()`/`expect.objectContaining()` matcher helpers                                             | Per-field casts (`response.body.results as MessageWithAuthor[]`); keep `toMatchObject({ content: expect.stringContaining(...) })`                                                    | The test-file ESLint block relaxes only `no-explicit-any`/`no-console` while the `no-unsafe-*` rules stay ON; a whole-object cast launders the `any` once whereas per-field casts trip `no-unsafe-member-access`, and `expect.stringContaining()`/`objectContaining()` are themselves typed `any`, so using them as object-literal values trips `no-unsafe-assignment` — typed property assertions are strict-clean AND stronger (they check the real DTO shape). Keeping `const results: MessageWithAuthor[] = body.results` preserves the `MessageWithAuthor` type reference                        | A whole-object cast trusts the runtime payload matches `SearchResponse`; acceptable because the shared Zod schema validates the wire shape server-side and the suite exercises the real response                                      |
| Workspace imports use the `@app/*` scope with NO `.js` on `@app/shared/*` subpaths (`@app/shared/types/message`, `@app/shared/constants/limits`) while the relative helper import keeps `.js` (`./setup.js`), and the app handle is typed `Application` (type-only from `express`), not `Express`                                                                                  | The seed's literal `@blitzy-slack/shared/...js` specifiers and `app: Express`                                                                                                        | `@blitzy-slack/*` resolves to no package (the monorepo is `@app/*`); the `@app/shared` `exports` map points `./types/*` and `./constants/*` at the `.ts` sources so a `.js` suffix fails `tsc`, while ESM relative imports still require `.js`; and `createTestApp()` returns Express 5's `Application` interface (distinct from `Express`), so `Application` is the assignable annotation — matching the conventions already recorded for `test/setup.ts`                                                                                                                                            | A future monorepo rescope must update every `@app/*` specifier together; otherwise none — these conventions are verified by ts-jest compile + `eslint --max-warnings 0`                                                               |
| The stop-word test asserts only that the query SUCCEEDS and returns an array (`Array.isArray(results)`); the extra-query-param and SQL-injection tests accept BOTH `200` and `400` (`expect([200, 400]).toContain(status)`), rather than pinning a single outcome                                                                                                                  | Assert stop-words return exactly empty/full; pin the extra-param and injection cases to one fixed status                                                                             | `plainto_tsquery('english', …)` strips stop-words and the empty-query result is Postgres-version dependent, so the meaningful property is "no crash, well-formed array", not a fixed count; the `searchQuerySchema.strict()` may reject an extra `channel=` param with 400 (or the validate middleware may drop it → 200), and an injection string may pass length validation (200, parameterized → no rows) or be rejected (400) — both outcomes are SAFE, so the test pins the security/robustness property, not an implementation-specific status code                                             | Slightly looser assertions; mitigated because the SQLi test ALSO asserts the `messages` table still has rows (`count() > 0`), directly proving no destructive SQL executed                                                            |
| Index and destructured-first-element accesses under `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` (the prior `body.results[0].content`, and `const [match] = results; match.content/authorId/author.id/author.displayName`) are narrowed with an explicit guard `if (x === undefined) throw new Error('expected exactly one search result')` placed immediately after the `toHaveLength(1)` assertion | A non-null assertion `match!.content`; optional chaining `match?.content` on every read; an `@ts-expect-error` comment (forbidden by Rule 3); or leaving the direct access unchanged | The direct-access pattern previously recorded in this section as strict-clean actually FAILED the build — `tsc` emitted TS2532 and TS18048 because `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` widens an index or destructure result to `T or undefined`, and a jest `toHaveLength(1)` matcher does not narrow the TypeScript type. A throwing guard narrows the value to `T` for the subsequent dotted reads, preserves semantics (length is asserted as 1 immediately prior), introduces no `!` and no `@ts-*` comment, and satisfies `only-throw-error` by throwing an `Error`. This row corrects the earlier claim | A few extra guard lines per assertion cluster (negligible). If the endpoint could legitimately return an empty result set the guard throws a clear message instead of a cryptic undefined-property crash — the preferred failure mode |

## `packages/api` — File upload & download integration tests (`test/files.test.ts`)

`test/files.test.ts` is the Jest + supertest integration suite for the two file endpoints — `POST /api/files` (multipart upload, field `file`, 10 MB cap) and `GET /api/files/:id` (ACL-gated download: uploader OR channel-member OR DM-participant). Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The file-to-message ACL precondition in the four GET-ACL tests is seeded with a direct `prismaTest.message.create({ data: { content, authorId, channelId or dmId, fileId, parentId: null } })` rather than `POST /api/messages` carrying a `fileId`                                                                                                                                                               | POST the linking message through the message route (the assigned-file prompt's literal sketch); attach a stub Socket.io server to the test app via `app.set('io', stub)`; add a missing-io guard to routes/messages.ts; or wire a stub io inside setup.ts's createTestApp | createTestApp() returns the bare production createApp(), which does NOT attach Socket.io — `app.set('io', io)` runs only in the index.ts bootstrap. The route's post-write broadcast `req.app.get('io').to(room).emit(MESSAGE_NEW, msg)` (messages.ts:208) therefore throws a TypeError reading 'to' of undefined (HTTP 500) for ANY routed message POST, AFTER createMessage has already succeeded. The file endpoints are this suite's subject-under-test; the linking message is merely the ACL precondition (getFile grants a non-uploader access iff a Message references the file in a channel they belong to or a DM they participate in). A direct Prisma write matches the established repo convention (search.test.ts seeds 17 messages this way; socket.test.ts seeds parents likewise), keeps the whole fix inside the assigned file, and touches neither shared setup.ts nor production route semantics. Rule 4 is unaffected (users still go through registerUser). Deviation from the prompt logged here | This suite does not exercise the message route's real-time emit for file-bearing messages — that path is covered by socket.test.ts and a future messages.test.ts. If the getFile ACL query were changed to require routed-message provenance the direct seed would need revisiting, which the 200/403 ACL assertions would catch                        |
| The size cap is INCLUSIVE: exactly `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES` (10 MB) is accepted (201) and only `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES + 1` is rejected (413, code LIMIT_FILE_SIZE, zero rows). This SUPERSEDES the prior EXCLUSIVE-cap decision (which asserted exactly-at-cap -> 413). The boundary is pinned with four points: `MAX-1` -> 201, `MAX` -> 201, `MAX+1` -> 413, plus the general `oversizedBuffer()` (= `MAX+1`) -> 413 | Keep the prior exclusive-cap assertion (`MAX` -> 413) and change nothing in the middleware; or advertise `maxBytes - 1` everywhere so UI/API/test all agree on an exclusive cap                                                                                           | CP5 review finding (MAJOR, files.test.ts L219-235): the AAP File contract defines the cap with `oversizedBuffer()` = `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES + 1` (implying the cap itself is inclusive) and the checkpoint explicitly requires at-limit success, so the prior exclusive-cap behavior was a defect. busboy 1.6.0 emits 'limit' the moment `fileSize === fileSizeLimit`, so to make exactly 10 MB succeed the upload middleware (`middleware/upload.ts`) now sets `limits.fileSize = MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB * 1024 * 1024 + 1`; the service layer (`services/files.service.ts`) already enforces the true cap with a strict `size > maxBytes` guard, so `MAX` passes the service while `MAX+1` is caught by busboy before the route runs. Empirically verified with a busboy probe (limit = MAX+1 -> MAX accepted, MAX+1 rejected). UI/API/test now consistently advertise an inclusive 10 MB cap                                                                                                                                 | The +1 offset relies on busboy's `===` comparison and is therefore version-specific; a future busboy that switched to strictly-greater-than would make the limit accept `MAX+1` -- caught by the `MAX+1 -> 413` boundary test, the intended signal that dependency behavior changed. The pinned multer `^2.x` / busboy `1.6.x` range holds the contract |
| GET /api/files/:id is validated by content-type sniffing that accepts BOTH a binary stream and a JSON metadata body; only the 200 status is pinned, and the binary branch additionally asserts a non-empty image/png Buffer (retrieved with supertest `.responseType('blob')`)                                                                                                                                    | Pin strictly to the binary stream; or pin strictly to a JSON body carrying FileAttachment.url                                                                                                                                                                             | The route streams bytes via res.sendFile (verified), but keying the assertion on the pinned 200 status plus a content-type sniff makes the contract test robust to a future switch to a JSON-plus-url response (the FileAttachment.url field exists for exactly that). `.responseType('blob')` is required for supertest to expose the body as a Buffer instead of attempting to parse it                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Lower strictness on the response-body shape; mitigated by pinning the 200 status and asserting a non-empty image/png Buffer in the binary branch                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| Upload payloads are synthesized in-memory with Buffer.alloc / Buffer.from and the tinyPngBuffer() / oversizedBuffer() setup helpers; no on-disk fixture files are used                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | A fixtures/ directory of real PNG, JPEG, and PDF files                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | In-memory buffers give deterministic, dependency-free byte counts (essential for the exact cap-boundary tests), avoid filesystem coupling in the suite, and reuse the shared setup helpers. The backend persists the multipart part's mimetype and does not validate magic bytes, so a minimal 8-byte PNG signature is a sufficient fixture                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | tinyPngBuffer is not a decodable image; immaterial because no assertion relies on backend image decoding or content-based MIME sniffing                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| supertest's any-typed response.body is narrowed with a single WHOLE-OBJECT cast to a concrete interface (`as FileAttachment`, or a local `ErrorResponseBody` for error envelopes), not per-field casts or jest matcher helpers                                                                                                                                                                                    | Per-field `as` casts; or jest expect.objectContaining() / expect.any() applied to the raw any body                                                                                                                                                                        | The test-file ESLint override relaxes only no-explicit-any and no-console while the no-unsafe-\* rules stay ON, so a whole-object cast launders the any body once and stays strict-clean, whereas per-field access on any trips no-unsafe-member-access. A small local ErrorResponseBody interface (error, message, optional code) types the 413 and bad-request error envelopes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | A whole-object cast trusts the runtime payload matches the interface; acceptable because the response is the server-produced FileAttachment DTO and the status code is asserted independently                                                                                                                                                           |
| The wrong-multipart-field-name test (`.attach('attachment', …)`) accepts BOTH 400 and 500                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Pin to 400 assuming a global multer-error catcher; or pin to 500                                                                                                                                                                                                          | multer's .single('file') rejects an unexpected field with LIMIT_UNEXPECTED_FILE; whether the error-handler maps that to 400 or lets it surface as 500 is not pinned by the AAP or the upload.ts prompt. The test pins the meaningful property — the upload is NOT accepted (never 201) — while tolerating either error status. The current implementation returns 400 via its MulterError-to-400 mapping, but the assertion stays tolerant to avoid over-pinning an unspecified behavior                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A looser status assertion; mitigated by asserting a non-success status so a silent-acceptance regression is still caught                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |

## `packages/api` — Message route integration tests (`test/messages.test.ts`)

`test/messages.test.ts` is the Jest + supertest integration suite for the four message endpoints — `POST /api/messages` (channel, DM, thread-reply, and file-attachment variants), `GET /api/messages/:id/replies`, `POST /api/messages/:id/reactions`, and `DELETE /api/messages/:id/reactions/:emoji` — plus message immutability and the Gate 9 delivery-latency budget. Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The cached app handle is typed `Application` (a type-only `express` import), not the `Express` type the assigned file's schema `external_imports` named                                                                                                           | Type it `Express`; type via `ReturnType<typeof createTestApp>`; leave it untyped                                                                                                                                                                                                     | `createTestApp()` is declared to return `Application`, which is not assignable to the `Express` application-factory type, and the sibling suites (`search.test.ts`, `files.test.ts`) already type the cached app as `Application`. Typing it `Express` would fail Rule 3 strict compilation. Schema-name deviation logged here                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | A reader following the schema's `Express` name finds `Application`; immaterial — both are `express` exports and `Application` is the correct return type of `createTestApp()`                                                                                                             |
| `beforeAll` registers a no-op Socket.io stub via `app.set('io', ioStub)` whose surface covers both `to(room).emit(...)` and `in(room).socketsJoin(...)`/`socketsLeave(...)`, and the suite drives every mutation through the real HTTP routes                     | Seed link state with a direct `prismaTest.message.create` to bypass the route's emit (the `files.test.ts` approach); attach a real Socket.io server (the `socket.test.ts` approach); add a missing-io guard to `routes/messages.ts`; wire a stub inside `setup.ts`'s `createTestApp` | This suite's subject IS the message route, so it must exercise `POST /api/messages` rather than bypass it with a direct DB write. `createTestApp()` returns the bare `createApp()` with no io attached (the real `app.set('io', io)` runs only in `index.ts`), so the route's post-mutation broadcast throws a TypeError and 500s after persistence succeeds. A minimal app-local stub keeps the whole fix inside the assigned file — touching neither `setup.ts` nor production semantics — and faithfully no-ops every io method the exercised routes invoke: `messages.ts` uses `io.to(room).emit(...)`, and the DM route reached via `createTestDm()` uses `io.in(userRoom).socketsJoin(dmRoom)`. The `files.test.ts` row explicitly deferred this realtime-emit handling to "a future messages.test.ts" — this is that file | The stub does not assert realtime payload shapes (covered by `socket.test.ts`); if a route later calls an io method beyond `to().emit()` and `in().socketsJoin()`, the stub must grow — a missing method surfaces immediately as a 500 in the affected test, which is the intended signal |
| `GET /:id/replies` is asserted to return a bare `MessageWithAuthor[]` array                                                                                                                                                                                       | Assert a `{ replies: [...] }` envelope (the assigned-file prompt's sketch)                                                                                                                                                                                                           | The implemented route responds `res.status(200).json(messages)` with the array directly; asserting an envelope would fail the shipped contract. Prompt deviation logged                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | If the route later wraps the payload in an envelope this assertion breaks — the intended signal of a contract change                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `POST /:id/reactions` and `DELETE /:id/reactions/:emoji` are asserted to return the full post-mutation `MessageWithAuthor` (the reaction summary read from `body.reactions`), at HTTP 200                                                                         | Assert the AAP §0.4.5 `{ messageId, reaction }` / `{ messageId, emoji, userId }` bodies, or a 201 on add                                                                                                                                                                             | Those AAP §0.4.5 shapes are the Socket.io `REACTION_ADDED`/`REACTION_REMOVED` payloads (asserted in `socket.test.ts`); the HTTP routes instead return the hydrated message so a client rerenders from one response. Verified from `routes/messages.ts`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | HTTP and socket payloads diverge by design; documented here so a reader does not expect them to be symmetric                                                                                                                                                                              |
| Thread-reply requests send the matching `channelId` or `dmId` alongside `parentId`, not `parentId` alone                                                                                                                                                          | Send only `{ content, parentId }` and rely on container inheritance (the prompt prose)                                                                                                                                                                                               | `sendMessageSchema`'s XOR `superRefine` requires exactly one of `channelId`/`dmId` on every send, so omitting both fails validation with 400; the service additionally validates the supplied container matches the parent's. The assigned-file prompt's own example code sends the container id, so the tests follow the example and the schema rather than the prose                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | A client sending a container id that mismatches the parent is rejected (Forbidden/Validation) — exercised by the reply-to-reply and parent-context cases                                                                                                                                  |

## `packages/api` — Direct-message route integration tests (`test/dms.test.ts`)

`test/dms.test.ts` is the Jest + supertest integration suite for the three direct-message endpoints — `GET /api/dms` (list the caller's conversations), `POST /api/dms` (start-or-find a 1:1 DM, idempotent), and `GET /api/dms/:id/messages?cursor=&limit=` (paginated, participant-gated history). Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                          | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `packages/api/jest.config.ts` gained `maxWorkers: 1`, forcing the api Jest suite to run serially (single worker).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Pass `--runInBand` only from the Makefile/CI invocation; give each Jest worker its own Postgres schema/database in `test/setup.ts`; leave Jest's default multi-worker parallelism. | The six integration suites share one Postgres database and `test/setup.ts`'s `cleanDatabase()` issues a global `deleteMany()` truncation in every `beforeEach`; under Jest's default multi-worker parallelism one worker's truncation wipes another worker's in-flight rows, so the suites fail nondeterministically when run together. This was proven pre-existing and independent of this file: with `dms.test.ts` temporarily removed, the other five suites still failed 4 of 5 (39 tests) in parallel. Enforcing a single worker in the config makes the canonical `make test` (bare `jest`, no flag) deterministic for every invocation — `make test`, `pnpm test`, and a bare `jest` alike — which a Makefile-only `--runInBand` would not guarantee. Per-worker database isolation is the parallel-friendly alternative but requires reworking the shared `setup.ts` (out of scope for a test-suite addition) and buys only suite wall-clock time, which Gate 9's budgets (API latency, not test runtime) do not require. | The api suite no longer benefits from multi-core parallelism (full run ≈ 21 s serial). Acceptable at PoC scale; if suite runtime later matters, the durable fix is per-worker database isolation in `setup.ts`, after which `maxWorkers` can be raised.                                                                                                                                   |
| The first `POST /api/dms` is asserted with an accept-list `expect([200, 201]).toContain(status)`, while the second (idempotent) call is pinned to `200`.                                                                                                                                                                                          | Pin the first call to `201` (created) always; pin it to `200` (find-or-create) always.                                                                                             | The route is find-then-create idempotent and returns `200` for both paths in the shipped implementation, but whether a first-ever create _should_ surface `201` is a legitimate design choice the AAP does not pin; the accept-list tolerates either without a false failure, while the second-call assertion is pinned to `200` because an idempotent re-request must never report a fresh creation.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | A slightly looser contract on the first call; mitigated because the pinned second-call `200` plus the `prismaTest.directMessage.findMany().length === 1` row-count assertion prove idempotency regardless of the first status.                                                                                                                                                            |
| DM messages used as fixtures are seeded with a direct `prismaTest.message.create` / `createMany` (`{ content, authorId, dmId, parentId }`), not through `POST /api/messages`.                                                                                                                                                                     | Send each fixture message through the message route.                                                                                                                               | Rule 4 mandates the registration flow only for _users_ (created here via `registerUser`); messages are not users. A direct Prisma write keeps the suite focused on the DM endpoints, avoids the message route's Socket.io broadcast (which 500s under `createTestApp()` since no `io` is attached), and matches the established repo convention (`search.test.ts`, `socket.test.ts`, `files.test.ts` all seed messages this way).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Bypasses the message route's `sendMessageSchema` XOR refinement for the seeded rows; immaterial because the DM endpoints under test only read messages, and the send-path validation is covered by `messages.test.ts`.                                                                                                                                                                    |
| No Socket.io stub is attached to the test app, unlike `messages.test.ts`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Attach a no-op `io` stub via `app.set('io', stub)` defensively.                                                                                                                    | The DM routes guard their optional realtime side effects with `const io = req.app.get('io'); if (io !== undefined) { … }`, so `POST /api/dms` completes cleanly at `200` with no `io` present. Adding a stub would be dead scaffolding.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | If a DM route later emits unconditionally (dropping the guard) the affected test would 500 — the intended signal to revisit, at which point a stub or real `io` would be wired.                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| The cached app handle is typed `Application` (type-only `express` import), not the `Express` type named by the file's schema `external_imports`.                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Type it `Express`; use `ReturnType<typeof createTestApp>`; leave it untyped.                                                                                                       | `createTestApp()` returns Express 5's `Application` interface, which is not assignable to `Express`; every sibling suite types the cached app as `Application`, and `Express` would fail Rule 3 strict compilation.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A reader following the schema's `Express` label finds `Application`; immaterial — both are `express` exports and `Application` is the correct return type.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| `GET /api/dms/:id/messages` responses are asserted against a `{ messages: MessageWithAuthor[]; nextCursor: string \| null }` envelope; last-page/emptiness is `nextCursor === null` and more-pages is `typeof nextCursor === 'string'`.                                                                                                           | Assert the prompt sketch's `{ messages, hasMore, nextCursor }` shape with a boolean `hasMore`.                                                                                     | The shipped route returns `{ messages, nextCursor }` with no `hasMore` field; asserting `hasMore` would compare against `undefined` and fail. `nextCursor` nullability already encodes "are there more pages?", so it is the authoritative end-of-history signal.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | If a `hasMore` field is later added these tests still pass (they ignore extra fields); if `nextCursor` semantics change the pagination assertions catch it.                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| DM list entries are read as `DMWithParticipants` whose `participants` is `PublicUser[]`, so participant identity is `participant.id`.                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Read `participant.userId` as in the prompt sketch.                                                                                                                                 | The hydrated DTO exposes each participant as a `PublicUser` (`{ id, displayName, avatarUrl }`); there is no `userId` field, so `participant.userId` would be `undefined` at runtime and fail the membership assertions.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | None — verified against `packages/shared/src/types/dm.ts`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| Coverage of `dms.service.ts` was driven to ≥ 80 % lines (80.23 %) by adding in-scope edge-case tests (DM list ordering with adversarial input, a malformed cursor, a well-formed-but-wrong-shape cursor, and out-of-range `limit`), while the global services coverage threshold is left failing.                                                 | Create the missing `auth.test.ts` / `channels.test.ts` to lift the global aggregate; lower the `coverageThreshold` in `jest.config.ts`.                                            | The added tests exercise every DM-endpoint path reachable deterministically through HTTP, satisfying this file's "coverage on `dms.service.ts`" mandate (Gate 13). The remaining global shortfall is dominated by `channels.service.ts` (≈ 28 %) and `users.service.ts` (0 %), which require sibling test files (`auth.test.ts`, `channels.test.ts`) that are AAP §0.6.1 Group-4 files assigned to other pipeline agents and not yet authored — creating them here would exceed this file's scope, and lowering the correctly-set Gate-13 threshold would defeat its purpose.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | The `--coverage` aggregate gate stays red until the sibling service test files land; the canonical `make test` (no `--coverage`) is green. `resolveLimit`'s defensive `limit<1`/`>MAX` branches stay uncovered because the Zod query schema rejects those at validation before the service runs, and the P2002 race-recovery path is not deterministically reachable via sequential HTTP. |
| supertest's `any`-typed `response.body` is narrowed with whole-object casts (`as DirectMessage`, `as DMWithParticipants[]`, local `DmMessagesPage`, local `ErrorResponseBody`); indexed/destructured reads are guarded with `if (x === undefined) throw new Error(...)`; no `expect.any` / `toMatchObject` / `arrayContaining` matchers are used. | Per-field `as` casts; jest `expect.objectContaining` / `expect.any`; non-null `!` assertions; `@ts-expect-error`.                                                                  | The test-file ESLint override relaxes only `no-explicit-any` and `no-console` while the `no-unsafe-*` rules stay on, so a whole-object cast launders the `any` body once and stays strict-clean, whereas jest matchers on an `any` body trip `no-unsafe-assignment`; throwing guards narrow `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` results without `!` or `@ts-*` (both forbidden by Rule 3).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | A whole-object cast trusts the runtime payload matches the type; acceptable because each status code is asserted independently and the payloads are server-produced DTOs.                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |

## `packages/api` — Channel route integration tests (`test/channels.test.ts`)

`test/channels.test.ts` is the Jest + supertest integration suite for the five channel endpoints — `GET /api/channels` (ACL-filtered list), `POST /api/channels` (create + auto-owner), `POST /api/channels/:id/join`, `POST /api/channels/:id/leave`, and `GET /api/channels/:id/messages?cursor=&limit=` (cursor-paginated, member-gated history). Each row records a non-trivial decision per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3); the conventions this suite shares with its siblings (the `Application` app type, the `@app/*` import scope, and the whole-object-cast / throwing-`undefined`-guard idiom that keeps supertest's `any` body strict-clean) follow the patterns already recorded for `test/setup.ts`, `test/search.test.ts`, `test/messages.test.ts`, and `test/dms.test.ts`.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                            | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
