| The app handle is typed `Application` (type-only `express` import); workspace imports use the `@app/*` scope with NO `.js` on `@app/shared/*` subpaths (`@app/shared/types/channel`, `@app/shared/types/message`, `@app/shared/constants/limits`) while the relative helper keeps `.js` (`./setup.js`); and only the six `setup.ts` helpers the suite actually calls are imported — `createTestApp`, `cleanDatabase`, `closeTestResources`, `registerUser`, `uniqueChannelName`, `prismaTest` — with `uniqueEmail`/`uniqueDisplayName` deliberately omitted. | The schema's `app: Express` type and its literal `@blitzy-slack/shared/...js` specifiers; importing the full `setup.ts` helper set named in the internal-imports list (including `uniqueEmail`/`uniqueDisplayName`). | `createTestApp()` returns Express 5's `Application` interface, which is not assignable to the distinct `Express` factory type, so `Application` is the correct annotation (matching every sibling suite); `@blitzy-slack/*` resolves to no package (the monorepo is `@app/*`) and the `@app/shared` `exports` map points its subpaths at `.ts` sources, so a `.js` suffix fails `tsc` while the ESM relative import still requires `.js`; and `registerUser()` generates a unique email and display name internally, so importing `uniqueEmail`/`uniqueDisplayName` would leave them unused and trip `noUnusedLocals` (Rule 3) — whereas `uniqueChannelName` IS imported because channel names are caller-supplied and must stay collision-free across the serially-run suite. | A reader following the schema's `Express` / `@blitzy-slack` labels or its full import list instead finds `Application`, `@app/*`, and a six-symbol subset; immaterial and verified by the ts-jest compile plus `eslint --max-warnings 0`. A future monorepo rescope must update every `@app/*` specifier together. |
| `GET /api/channels/:id/messages` responses are asserted against a local `ChannelMessagesPage` = `{ messages: MessageWithAuthor[]; nextCursor: string \| null }` envelope; "another (older) page remains" is asserted as `typeof nextCursor === 'string'` and "timeline exhausted" as `nextCursor === null`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Assert the assigned-file prompt sketch's `response.body.hasMore` boolean (alongside, or instead of, `nextCursor`).                                                                                                   | The shipped route/service returns `{ messages, nextCursor }` with NO `hasMore` field; the sketch's repeated `expect(response.body.hasMore).toBe(true/false)` would compare against `undefined` and fail. A non-null `nextCursor` already encodes the end-of-history signal — the service emits it only when its `take: limit + 1` "peek" row is present — so it is the authoritative more-pages indicator. Verified against `services/channels.service.ts`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | If a `hasMore` field is later added these tests still pass (extra response fields are ignored); if `nextCursor` semantics change, the page-size and no-overlap assertions catch the regression.                                                                                                                    |
| Channel member rows and channel `Message` rows used as fixtures are arranged with direct `prismaTest` writes, and the persisted side effects — the auto-created owner membership, and a joiner's/leaver's membership presence-then-absence — are asserted with `prismaTest.channelMember.findUnique({ where: { channelId_userId: { … } } })`; USERS are created ONLY through `registerUser()` (`POST /api/auth/register`).                                                                                                                                   | Drive every fixture and side-effect assertion through the REST layer; mock the service/Prisma.                                                                                                                       | Rule 4 governs USER creation only — channel memberships and messages are plain fixtures — so a direct Prisma write is the least-coupled, most deterministic setup and matches the established repo convention (`search.test.ts`, `socket.test.ts`, `files.test.ts`, `dms.test.ts` all seed messages this way). Reading the `channelId_userId` compound-unique key directly verifies the owner-auto-add and join/leave mutations at the persistence layer without depending on a list endpoint's projection, while the create/join/leave service paths themselves are still exercised through the real HTTP routes (the subject under test).                                                                                                                                    | The seeded rows bypass service-layer validation; mitigated because every mutation under test still flows through its route and the negative paths assert the mapped HTTP status.                                                                                                                                   |
| The owner-auto-assignment expectation is built as a `Pick<ChannelMember, 'channelId' \| 'userId' \| 'role'>` literal and compared field-wise against the persisted row.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Compare against the full `ChannelMember` DTO; use jest's `toMatchObject` / `objectContaining` on the `any`-typed Prisma row.                                                                                         | The Prisma row's `joinedAt` is a `Date` whereas the shared `ChannelMember` DTO types it as an ISO `string`, so a full-shape equality is a type conflict; projecting to the three structurally-identical scalar fields keeps the assertion strict-clean, and jest's structural matchers are avoided because they trip `no-unsafe-*` on the `any`-typed result under the test-file ESLint override.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | The assertion does not cover `joinedAt`/`id`; immaterial — those are framework-assigned, and the membership's existence plus `role: 'owner'` is the contract under test.                                                                                                                                           |
| Cursor pagination is validated by round-tripping `nextCursor` OPAQUELY: page 1 requests the default 50, its returned `nextCursor` is fed verbatim (URL-encoded) into page 2 which returns the remaining 25, the two pages are asserted non-overlapping by id-set difference, and page 2's `nextCursor` is `null` — the cursor string is never decoded or shape-inspected.                                                                                                                                                                                    | Decode the base64url cursor and assert its `(createdAt, id)` contents/format.                                                                                                                                        | The cursor encoding is an implementation detail of `channels.service.ts`; the tests pin observable behaviour (correct page sizes, no overlap, end-of-history null) rather than couple to the encoding, mirroring the `dms.test.ts` pagination approach.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Does not catch a cursor-format regression directly; mitigated because a broken encode/decode round-trip surfaces as a wrong page-2 size or an overlap (which these assertions detect), and the dedicated malformed-cursor test pins the 400 rejection path.                                                        |
| Three edge cases assert an accept-LIST rather than a single status: re-joining an already-joined channel `expect([200, 409]).toContain(status)`; leaving a channel the caller is not a member of `expect([403, 404]).toContain(status)`; and `?limit=999` (above `MAX_PAGE_SIZE`) `expect([200, 400]).toContain(status)`, with a `messages.length <= MAX_PAGE_SIZE` guard on the 200 branch.                                                                                                                                                                 | Pin each to the single status the shipped route currently returns (re-join 200, leave-non-member 404, over-limit 400).                                                                                               | These three behaviours are legitimate design choices the AAP does not pin — idempotent re-join could reasonably surface "ok" or "already a member"; leaving a non-membership could be "forbidden" or "not found"; an over-large `limit` could be rejected or silently capped. The accept-lists make the suite robust to either valid contract without a false failure, while the happy-path and ACL tests still pin the exact 200/403/404 codes that ARE contractually fixed.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | A slightly looser contract on those three edges; mitigated because each accept-list still excludes the wrong-category codes (a 500, or a 200 on the non-member leave, would fail) and the shipped route's actual codes — 200 / 404 / 400 — all fall inside the lists.                                              |

## CP5 review remediation — API integration coverage, file-cap semantics & early web accessibility

Consolidated record of the decisions made while resolving the CP5 review (API integration test suite + early web layout components: 5 Major, 6 Minor). Each row documents a non-trivial fix per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3). The file-upload cap change additionally SUPERSEDES the prior exclusive-cap row in the _File upload & download integration tests_ section above (now rewritten to the inclusive contract).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                      | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| `middleware/upload.ts` sets multer `limits.fileSize = MAX_FILE_SIZE_MB * 1024 * 1024 + 1` (the byte cap PLUS ONE) so a file of exactly `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES` (10 MB) is accepted                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Leave the limit at `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES` (exclusive cap); enforce the cap only in the service and disable multer's limit; switch to a multer/busboy build with strictly-greater-than semantics | CP5 MAJOR (file contract): busboy 1.6.0 emits 'limit' the moment `fileSize === fileSizeLimit`, so a multer limit equal to the cap rejects exactly-at-cap with 413. The AAP File contract (`oversizedBuffer()` = `MAX+1`) and the checkpoint both require at-limit SUCCESS, so the limit is raised by one byte; `services/files.service.ts` still enforces the real cap with a strict `size > maxBytes` guard, so `MAX` passes and `MAX+1` trips busboy before the route runs. Verified with a standalone busboy probe.                                                                                                                            | The +1 depends on busboy's `===` comparison; a future busboy switching to `>` would accept `MAX+1`. Caught by the `MAX+1 -> 413` boundary test; the pinned multer `^2.x` range holds the contract.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| `packages/api/jest.config.ts` `collectCoverageFrom` now ALSO includes `<rootDir>/../shared/src/schemas/**/*.ts` (excluding `index.ts` and `*.d.ts`), alongside the existing `src/services/**/*.ts`                                                                                                                                                                                               | Keep services-only coverage; add a separate root/workspace coverage job for the shared package; move schema unit tests into `packages/shared`                                                  | CP5 MAJOR (Gate 13): the gate requires >=80% line coverage on API services AND `packages/shared/src/schemas`, but coverage collection omitted the schemas entirely, so the gate could not prove its required scope. The `moduleNameMapper` already maps `@app/shared` to `../shared/src`, so the API suites (which import every schema through the routes/validate middleware) already exercise the schema source; adding it to `collectCoverageFrom` surfaces that coverage under the same global >=80% threshold.                                                                                                                               | Shared-schema lines now count toward the API package's threshold; if a schema is added but never exercised by an API suite the global threshold could dip, which is the intended signal to add coverage. SUPERSEDED IN PART: the `<rootDir>/../shared/...` path anchoring shown here was revised when `rootDir` was relocated to `packages/` so istanbul actually instruments the shared tree (see _Gate 13 coverage instrumentation — Jest `rootDir` relocation_ below); the decision to include shared schemas in coverage stands and is now effective rather than silently no-op. |
| `test/setup.ts` REMOVED the unused exported helpers `loginUser()` and `waitForTestInfra()` (and the now-orphaned `sleep` const + `promisify` import)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Keep them exported for future suites; keep but stop exporting until first use; annotate them as intentionally reserved                                                                         | CP5 MINOR (dead code): a grep across `packages/api` found no caller of either helper, and the checkpoint requires every setup helper to be used. Removing them keeps the shared module lean and satisfies Rule 3 (`noUnusedLocals`/`no-unused-vars` would flag the orphaned `sleep`/`promisify` once `waitForTestInfra` was gone). `registerUser()` already covers user creation (Rule 4); a future suite needing a login flow can re-add a focused helper.                                                                                                                                                                                       | A future suite that wanted `loginUser()`/`waitForTestInfra()` must re-introduce them; trivial, and re-adding on first real use keeps the module free of speculative dead code.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| `test/setup.ts` `clearUploadsDirectory()` now resolves `env.FILE_UPLOAD_PATH` and refuses to recursively delete it unless it is a recognized test-upload directory (basename in `{uploads, uploads-test}`) OR lives under the OS temp dir; it throws on the filesystem root, the home dir, and `process.cwd()`                                                                                   | Keep the unguarded `rm(..., { recursive: true, force: true })`; hardcode a fixed `/tmp` path; skip cleanup entirely                                                                            | CP5 MINOR / Security: a misconfigured CI `FILE_UPLOAD_PATH` (e.g. `/` or `$HOME`) would have let the `beforeEach` recursively delete unintended files. The guard `assertSafeUploadPath()` allow-lists only the explicit test-upload basenames and the temp dir, failing closed (throw) on dangerous targets while still clearing the legitimate `./uploads` contents multer needs.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | A project that legitimately configured a differently-named upload dir outside `/tmp` would trip the guard; acceptable for the PoC, and the allow-list is a single edit to extend.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| `test/socket.test.ts` adds a reusable `expectNoEvent(socket, event, timeoutMs?, predicate?)` helper (with a documented `NO_EVENT_WINDOW_MS = 500` tied to the <500ms delivery SLA) and uses it for the two negative 'silence' assertions, replacing the prior raw `sleep(300)` / `sleep(500)` waits                                                                                              | Keep the fixed sleeps; rely on the global `testTimeout`; poll room/adapter state                                                                                                               | CP5 MINOR (flakiness): a raw fixed sleep can false-pass if the forbidden event arrives just after the arbitrary window. `expectNoEvent` registers a one-shot listener, removes it before settling, resolves when the window elapses with no (matching) event, and rejects immediately if the event fires — making the negative assertion deterministic and naming the offending event on failure. The optional `predicate` scopes the multi-tab case to `state === 'offline'`.                                                                                                                                                                    | The window is still a sampling interval (absence of an event cannot be awaited indefinitely); mitigated by tying it to the propagation SLA and removing the listener on settle so no cross-test leakage occurs.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `test/socket.test.ts` adds a Gate 9 '50 concurrent WebSocket sessions' test: it registers 50 users, opens 50 authenticated `{ transports: ['websocket'], reconnection: false, forceNew: true }` clients concurrently, has all 50 join one public channel, then asserts a single host broadcast is received by all 49 other clients within a 5000ms budget; all clients are closed in `afterEach` | Assert only the two-tab case already present; simulate concurrency by reusing one client; omit the budget                                                                                      | CP5 MAJOR (Gate 9): the prompt's performance budget explicitly lists 50 concurrent WebSocket sessions, which no test covered. Opening 50 real authenticated clients against the production handler + Redis adapter exercises the actual fan-out path end-to-end; a per-test timeout of 45s accommodates the 50 sequential bcrypt registrations (~95ms each) while the message fan-out itself is asserted under the 5s budget.                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | 50 clients + 50 registrations make this the slowest test (~ tens of seconds); bounded by the 45s per-test timeout and run under `maxWorkers: 1`, so it cannot contend with other suites.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| Three new integration suites — `test/health.test.ts`, `test/presence.test.ts`, `test/users.test.ts` — cover the previously-untested `GET /api/health`, `GET /api/presence?userIds=`, and `GET /api/users?q=` endpoints (auth failures, Zod validation failures, happy paths, the `PublicUser` privacy shape, and the `X-Request-Id` Gate 10 header)                                              | Leave these endpoints untested (the prior state); cover only `/api/health`; assert presence/users only at the service layer                                                                    | CP5 MAJOR (Gate 12): every backend endpoint must have at least one integration test, and `/api/users` + `/api/presence` are authenticated, privacy-sensitive surfaces whose validation and `PublicUser` (no email / no passwordHash) contracts were unverified. The suites assert `requireAuth` runs before `validate` (401 regardless of query), the `.strict()`/bound validation (400), the offline-by-default presence of a fresh user, the caller-exclusion + case-insensitive substring + result cap of user search, and the redaction of email/passwordHash from the serialized body. Users are created only via `registerUser()` (Rule 4). | The presence happy path asserts `offline` (no heartbeat in an HTTP-only suite), so it does not exercise the online/away buckets; those transitions are covered by `socket.test.ts`. The suites require the Docker Postgres/Redis up, like every other integration suite.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| `components/messages/MessageList.tsx` adds `role="log" aria-live="polite" aria-relevant="additions text" aria-label="Messages"` to the inner timeline container; the surrounding Radix `ScrollArea` is left untouched                                                                                                                                                                            | Put the live-region attributes on the `ScrollArea` root/viewport; use `aria-live="assertive"`; add an off-screen mirror region that re-announces each message                                  | CP5 MAJOR (accessibility): Socket.io-delivered messages updated visually but were never announced to screen-reader users. `role="log"` marks an append-only chat timeline and `aria-live="polite"` queues announcements without interrupting; `aria-relevant="additions text"` limits announcements to newly added nodes so pagination/reordering does not re-announce history. Placing the attributes on the inner container (not the ScrollArea) preserves Radix's keyboard-scroll behavior.                                                                                                                                                    | `aria-live="polite"` may briefly queue announcements under heavy bursts; acceptable and preferable to the interrupting `assertive`. Very long backfills are bounded because `aria-relevant` excludes existing nodes.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| New `hooks/useDms.ts` exports `DMS_QUERY_KEY = ['dms']` and a token-gated `useDms()` returning `{ dms, isLoading, isFetching, error, refetch }` over `GET /api/dms`, mirroring `useChannels.ts`; `DmList` now consumes it instead of an inline `useQuery`                                                                                                                                        | Keep the inline `useQuery(['dms'])` in `DmList`; duplicate the literal query key at each call site                                                                                             | CP5 MINOR (integration/perf): the checkpoint asks for the shared-hook pattern the sidebar already uses for channels. Extracting `useDms` gives a single source of truth for the `['dms']` query and its auth gating + `staleTime`, lets the socket handler invalidate via the exported `DMS_QUERY_KEY` constant instead of a duplicated literal, and keeps the two sidebar sections (`useChannels`/`useDms`) symmetric.                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | An extra hook module; negligible, and it removes the literal-key duplication that risked drift between the read and invalidation sites.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| `components/dms/DmList.tsx` filters the `message:new` socket handler so it invalidates `DMS_QUERY_KEY` ONLY when `message.dmId !== null`, and adds `aria-busy={isLoading}` to the section plus a visually-hidden `role="status"` loading announcement                                                                                                                                            | Keep invalidating the DM list on EVERY `message:new` (the prior behavior); rely on `staleTime` to absorb the churn; convey loading with the skeleton rows only                                 | CP5 MINOR (perf + accessibility): the inline handler refetched the DM list for every message, including channel and thread traffic (`dmId === null`). The `message:new` payload is a `MessageWithAuthor` whose `dmId` is non-null only for DM messages, so filtering on `dmId !== null` scopes the refetch to events that can actually change the DM list. Separately, the loading skeletons were decorative-only; `aria-busy` + an `sr-only` `role="status"` announce the loading state to assistive tech.                                                                                                                                       | If a future feature needs the DM list to react to a non-DM event it must widen the filter; explicit and easy to adjust. The `role="status"` text is English-only, consistent with the rest of the PoC UI.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |

### CP5 review remediation — Gate 13 coverage instrumentation (Jest `rootDir` relocation)

Follow-up to the `collectCoverageFrom` row above. Adding the shared schemas to `collectCoverageFrom` was necessary but **not sufficient**: with `rootDir` at the api package, Jest's coverage instrumenter silently skipped the shared tree, so the schemas appeared with 0% (or were absent) rather than being measured. Resolving Gate 13 required relocating `rootDir` and choosing a coverage provider that can attribute cross-package ESM source. Each decision below is non-trivial per the Explainability rule (AAP §0.8.3).

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | What alternatives existed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `packages/api/jest.config.ts` sets `rootDir: '..'` (the monorepo `packages/` directory) and re-anchors every path (`roots`, `testMatch`, `transform`, `moduleNameMapper`, `collectCoverageFrom`, `coverageDirectory`) to `<rootDir>/api/...` and `<rootDir>/shared/...`. The default **babel/istanbul** coverage provider is retained (no `coverageProvider` override).                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Keep `rootDir: '.'` (the api package) with `collectCoverageFrom` pointed at `<rootDir>/../shared/...`; switch to the **V8** coverage provider; build both packages to `dist/` and collect coverage from compiled output; move the shared-schema unit tests into `packages/shared` and run a separate coverage job there. | CP5 MAJOR (Gate 13) root cause: Jest configures `babel-plugin-istanbul` with `cwd: config.rootDir`, and the underlying `test-exclude` silently refuses to instrument any file whose path **relative to that cwd begins with `..`**. With `rootDir` at the api package, `packages/shared/src/schemas/*` resolves to `../shared/...` and was therefore never instrumented — `shouldInstrument` passed but the transform was a no-op, so the schemas read back null coverage and Gate 13's required scope could not be proven. Moving `rootDir` up to `packages/` places BOTH Gate 13 targets (`api/src/services` and `shared/src/schemas`) under the instrumenter's cwd with no `..` prefix, so istanbul instruments both. The V8 alternative was tried and **rejected empirically**: with V8, the schemas appeared in the report but at **0%** even when imported directly in an isolated probe test, because v8-to-istanbul cannot reconcile V8 byte ranges back to cross-package source when ts-jest compiles those files under the api tsconfig's `rootDir` (the emitted source-map `sources` paths are mangled for files outside that tsconfig root); setting `inlineSources: true` in `tsconfig.base.json` did not fix it (verified, then reverted clean). The babel provider with a shared-ancestor `rootDir` is the only configuration that measures the shared schemas correctly. | A higher `rootDir` widens Jest's module-discovery surface; mitigated by scoping `roots` to `['<rootDir>/api', '<rootDir>/shared']` and anchoring `testMatch` to `<rootDir>/api/test/**` (the shared tree holds no `*.test.ts`), so discovery does not actually broaden. The `db` package is reached only via `moduleNameMapper` at runtime, which does not require a root.                                                                                                                         |
| The `ts-jest/presets/default-esm` preset **shorthand was dropped** and its two settings inlined: `extensionsToTreatAsEsm: ['.ts']` plus a `transform` whose transformer is referenced by the explicit, rootDir-relative path `<rootDir>/api/node_modules/ts-jest` (with `useESM: true`, `tsconfig: '<rootDir>/api/tsconfig.json'`).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Keep `preset: 'ts-jest/presets/default-esm'`; hoist `ts-jest` to the repo root or `packages/` so the preset resolver finds it; author a root-level jest config that re-exports the preset.                                                                                                                               | Once `rootDir` moved to `packages/`, Jest's preset resolver (which searches from `rootDir`) could no longer find `ts-jest` — pnpm installs it only under `packages/api/node_modules/ts-jest`. Rather than hoist a dependency (which would mutate the lockfile and the AAP §0.3.1 inventory placement) the preset's behaviour is reproduced inline with an explicit transformer path that always resolves regardless of `rootDir`. Net transform behaviour is identical to the preset.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | If `ts-jest`'s preset internals change in a future major, the inlined settings must be re-synced by hand; low risk at the pinned `ts-jest@29.x` and documented here.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| Coverage was lifted to clear all self-imposed thresholds by **adding tests, never lowering thresholds**: a new `packages/api/test/schemas.test.ts` (57 dedicated unit tests across all six shared schema files → schemas at 100% lines), one service-layer defense-in-depth guard test in `files.test.ts` (`createFile` rejects `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES + 1` with `ForbiddenError` → `files.service.ts` 100%), and one reaction-aggregation integration test in `search.test.ts` (exercises the `toReactionSummaries` group-merge branch → `search.service.ts` 72%→86% lines). | Lower the `coverageThreshold` (especially the 70% branch floor, which services-only ran below at HEAD); mark the cross-package gap as an accepted exception; add `/* istanbul ignore */` to the unreachable defensive branches.                                                                                          | Gate 13 mandates ≥80% line coverage on services + shared schemas; lowering a correctly-set threshold would defeat the gate. The added tests target genuinely reachable, in-scope paths (the shared schemas through direct unit tests fulfilling Gate 13's explicit "Jest unit tests on `packages/shared/src/schemas`" wording; the files service guard and the search aggregation through real HTTP/Prisma paths). Final measured state exceeds every threshold without any threshold change: lines 83.29%, branches 70.91%, functions 96.1%, statements 83.43%; schemas 100%. Note: the committed branch floor (70) was never actually met at HEAD because the canonical `make test` runs without `--coverage`, so the gate was unenforced; it is now genuinely satisfied.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | `schemas.test.ts` lives under `packages/api/test` (where the api Jest runner discovers it) rather than in `packages/shared`; acceptable because `packages/shared` has no test runner of its own and the api runner already resolves `@app/shared/*` to shared source. The `typingScopeSchema` XOR-invalid branch and the `files.service.ts` size guard are covered by these unit/service tests because they are unreachable through the HTTP layer (the Zod query schema and multer reject first). |

### Sidebar layout container — `packages/web/src/components/layout/Sidebar.tsx`

Decisions made while authoring the workspace sidebar (second column of the three-column app shell). The component is a pure layout container: an aubergine `<aside>` wrapping a `ScrollArea` that stacks `<ChannelList />` above `<DmList />` with a `<Separator />` between them. All list content, section headings, and interactive rows are owned by the sibling `ChannelList`/`DmList` components.

| What was decided                                                                                                                                                                                                            | What alternatives existed                                                                                                  | Why this choice was made                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | What risks it carries                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The sidebar surface uses the Tailwind utility `bg-sidebar-bg` (with `text-sidebar-foreground` and `border-sidebar-border`) for its aubergine chrome, rather than the `bg-sidebar` class named in the file-generation brief. | Use `bg-sidebar` literally as written in the brief; or add a new `--color-sidebar` alias token to `src/index.css`.         | The `@theme` block in `src/index.css` defines `--color-sidebar-bg` (`oklch(0.272 0.101 327)`) but no bare `--color-sidebar`; in Tailwind v4 the `bg-sidebar` utility therefore resolves to nothing, leaving the sidebar transparent (a broken surface). The adjacent `WorkspaceNavRail.tsx` and `Landing.tsx` already use `bg-sidebar-bg`, so matching it makes the two adjacent shell columns share the identical aubergine and guarantees the token resolves. Verified at runtime: the `<aside>` computed `background-color` is exactly `oklch(0.272 0.101 327)`. Adding a new token was rejected to avoid editing the shared `index.css` (outside this file's scope) and duplicating the palette. | If `index.css` later introduces a distinct `--color-sidebar` token with a different value, this file would not pick it up; mitigated because the entire web package consistently uses the `sidebar-bg` token and re-alignment is a one-class change. |
| The Channels and Direct Messages sections are always expanded (NOT collapsible) in the PoC.                                                                                                                                 | Add `useState`-managed open/closed booleans plus a Radix `Collapsible` per section, with a chevron in each section header. | Collapsibility is UX polish, not a functional requirement, and the AAP does not list it. Keeping `Sidebar` a stateless container preserves the single-responsibility split (the container owns chrome; the sibling lists own content/state).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Long channel/DM lists scroll within the `ScrollArea` instead of letting a user collapse a whole section; acceptable for the PoC and reversible by wrapping each list in a `Collapsible` later.                                                       |
| The sidebar renders no workspace-name header; it starts directly with the channel list. Workspace identity is shown in the far-left `WorkspaceNavRail` instead.                                                             | Add a workspace-name header (and/or switcher) row at the top of the sidebar.                                               | Single-workspace PoC (AAP §0.7.2): the nav rail's workspace logo already identifies the one workspace, so a sidebar header would be redundant and is not part of the in-scope feature set derived from the screenshots.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | The workspace name is less prominent in the sidebar; acceptable for a single-workspace PoC and easy to add later if multi-workspace support is introduced.                                                                                           |
| JSX attributes use double quotes (e.g. `className="flex-1"`), not the single-quoted JSX shown in the file-generation brief's sample snippet.                                                                                | Use single-quoted JSX attributes as printed in the brief.                                                                  | The committed `.prettierrc` sets `jsxSingleQuote: false`, so Prettier — enforced by `make lint`/`format:check` under Rule 3 (zero-warning build) — requires double quotes in JSX; the sibling layout files (`Header.tsx`, `WorkspaceNavRail.tsx`) confirm the convention. Single-quoted JSX would fail `prettier --check`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | None — this is mandatory conformance to the project's committed Prettier configuration.                                                                                                                                                              |
